201 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Dunne v. County of Cook


No. 60178


Supreme Court of Illinois


108 Ill. 2d 161; 483 N.E.2d 13; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 264; 90 Ill. Dec. 866



July 26, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 27, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. James C. Murray, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, board president and board members, filed an action against defendant commissioners seeking a declaratory judgment that an ordinance was invalid. The trial court ruled that the ordinance was invalid. The Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) affirmed, and the commissioners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The ordinance reduced from four-fifths to three-fifths the majority necessary for the county board of commissioners to override a veto by the board president. The ordinance was passed under the county's home rule authority, Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6(a)(1970). The trial court ruled that the passage of the ordinance affected an alteration in the form of government under Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6(f)(1970) without referendum approval. To determine the meaning of "form of government" as used in § 6(f), the court examined the debates and proceedings in the drafting of the 1970 constitution. The court found that form of government included the relative powers of the board president and the county board. Reducing the votes needed to override the board president's veto did effect a diminution of his power. Because the change to the county's form of government had not been approved by referendum as required by § 6(f), the ordinance was invalid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's ruling, which affirmed the trial court's order holding that the county ordinance was invalid as having changed the county's form of government without referendum approval.

 

202 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wick


No. 59912


Supreme Court of Illinois


107 Ill. 2d 62; 481 N.E.2d 676; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 244; 89 Ill. Dec. 833



July 17, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Ogle County, the Hon. John L. Moore, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the judgment of the Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois), which reversed defendant's conviction for aggravated arson, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20 (1981), on the basis that the statute was an unreasonable and arbitrary exercise of the state's police power, which violated the guarantee of due process in Ill. Const. art. I, § 2.


OVERVIEW: A fire occurred at defendant's place of business. A fireman was injured fighting the fire. Defendant was convicted of aggravated arson, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20(a)(3) (1981). Defendant's conviction was reversed on appeal and the state sought review. The court held that to constitute a legitimate exercise of the police power, a legislative enactment had to bear a reasonable relationship to the public interest intended to be protected, and the means adopted had to be a reasonable method of accomplishing the desired objective. The court found that the purpose of para. 20(a)(3) was to subject arsonists to a more severe penalty when their conduct resulted in personal injury to firemen or policemen than when it resulted in property damage only. The court ruled that because aggravated arson did not require an unlawful purpose in setting a fire the statute swept too broadly by punishing innocent as well as culpable conduct in setting fires. The court found that para. 20(a)(3) violated the guarantee of due process in Ill. Const. art. I, § 2 and affirmed the judgment of the appellate court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court reversing defendant's conviction for aggravated arson and in holding that the statute in question violated due process.

 

203 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Krull


No. 60629


Supreme Court of Illinois


107 Ill. 2d 107; 481 N.E.2d 703; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 248; 89 Ill. Dec. 860



July 17, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Martin F. Hogan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found that § 5-401(e) of the Illinois Vehicle Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 5-401(e) (1981), was unconstitutional and granted defendants' motion to suppress evidence found during a warrantless search of a business.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with various violations of the Illinois Vehicle Code (Code) after a search of the premises revealed the presence of several stolen motor vehicles. Defendants sought to suppress the evidence seized during the search. The circuit court granted defendants' motion, holding that the search was conducted without probable cause and without a warrant, there was no valid consent, and § 5-401(e) of the Code was unconstitutional. The appellate court vacated and on remand the circuit court again found § 5-401(e) unconstitutional. The state appealed directly to the supreme court. The supreme court affirmed the circuit court. The court found that the administrative search authorized by § 5-401(e) was a search within the meaning of the Fourth Amendment. However, the court found that § 5-401(e) vested the state officials with too much discretion and did not provide for the regularity and neutrality required by the Fourth Amendment. The court held that good faith reliance on § 5-401(e) did not cure the illegal search because the statute was procedural. The circuit court's determination that there was no valid consent was not unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment granting defendants' motion to suppress.

 

204 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


In re Marriage of Semmler


No. 60950


Supreme Court of Illinois


107 Ill. 2d 130; 481 N.E.2d 716; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 250; 89 Ill. Dec. 873



July 17, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County, the Hon. Michael O'Brien, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff husband appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which granted defendant wife's motion to dismiss one count in the husband's petition for dissolution of marriage which was filed under § 401(a)(2) of the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 401(a)(2) (1984 Supp.).


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed count II of the husband's petition for dissolution of marriage on the grounds that the no-fault provision for dissolutions found in § 401(a)(2) of the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 401(a)(2) (1984 Supp.), was unconstitutional as applied in the instant case. The court reversed, holding the no-fault provision to be a valid enactment because 1) there was no violation of the ex post facto clauses in U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 or Ill. Const. art. I, § 16 (1970); and the impairment-of-contract clauses in U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 and Ill. Const. art. I, § 16 (1970) were inapplicable. The court also held that the no-fault provision did not violate the due process clause at Ill. Const. art. I, § 2, because of the legislature's intent for the no-fault provision to apply to separation periods occurring prior to the statute's enactment, as in this case, and the state interest in providing a method for no-fault dissolutions while preserving the possibility of reconciliation, via the two-year separation period requirement of the no-fault provision, outweighed the wife's private interest in staying married.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court dismissing count II of the husband's petition for dissolution of marriage from the wife and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

Felt v. Board of Trustees


Nos. 60373, 60374, 60375, 60376


Supreme Court of Illinois


107 Ill. 2d 158; 481 N.E.2d 698; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 253; 89 Ill. Dec. 855



July 17, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County, the Hon. Simon L. Friedman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed. Affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, board and members, appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which held that the 1982 amendment to § 18-125 of the Illinois Pension Code, 1982 Ill. Laws 152, 159, was unconstitutional as applied to plaintiff judges.


OVERVIEW: The judges brought complaints in the circuit court seeking administrative review of the board's calculation of their retirement annuities according to the provisions of the 1982 amendment. The judges all retired, or died, soon after the effective date of the amendment and the amendment caused their retirement annuities to be reduced. The circuit court held that the amendment was unconstitutional as it applied to the judges and defendants appealed. The court affirmed, holding that the change in the computation of the judges' retirement annuities impaired their retirement benefits in violation of Ill. Const. Art. XIII, § 5.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court judgments holding that the amendment to the Illinois Pension Code was unconstitutional as applied to the judges. That portion of one judgment holding that the amendment was valid as to persons becoming judges after the amendment was valid was not reviewed.

 

206 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Sanelli v. Glenview State Bank


No. 57935


Supreme Court of Illinois


108 Ill. 2d 1; 483 N.E.2d 226; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 256; 90 Ill. Dec. 908



July 17, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 27, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. John F. Hechinger, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, land-trust beneficiary, sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted appellee bank's motion to dismiss based on Ill. Comp. Stat. 148/81-84 (1983), in an action alleging that the bank breached its fiduciary duty to land-trust beneficiary and his wife by purchasing the trust property for its own benefit at a public sale after the beneficiaries defaulted on their loan.


OVERVIEW: The court held that (1) the retroactivity provision of ch. 148/81-84 did not unconstitutionally impair beneficiary's contract rights under the United States Constitution, (2) the retroactivity provision is valid under the Illinois Constitution, (3) because the retroactivity provision did not unconstitutionally impair beneficiary's contract rights, the provision did not deprive him of property without due process of law under either the United States Constitution or the Illinois Constitution. The court found that because the dispute between beneficiary and the bank was pending in the trial court at the time ch. 148/81-84 became effective, that dispute had yet to be decided, and therefore, applying ch. 148/81-84 did not invade the province of the judiciary or violate the principle of separation of powers established by the Illinois Constitution. The court further found that application of ch. 148/81-84 was a reasonable exercise of the legislature's authority to provide for the public welfare and to safeguard the interests of the people, and such application furthered a broad societal interest.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

207 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Perez


No. 58586


Supreme Court of Illinois


108 Ill. 2d 70; 483 N.E.2d 250; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 258; 90 Ill. Dec. 932



July 17, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 27, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County, the Hon. Robert R. Buchar, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of murdering a fellow inmate, and the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois) sentenced him to death. At a bifurcated sentencing hearing, the jury found the existence of a statutory aggravating factor under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(b)(2)) (1979), but found no mitigating factors sufficient to preclude the imposition of the death penalty. His sentence was stayed pending a direct appeal.


OVERVIEW: In a group attack, the victim received four wounds, one of which was fatal. Defendant argued that the jury could have found he did not cause the fatal wound, that aggravated battery was a lesser-included offense of murder, and that he was constitutionally entitled to an instruction on the lesser offense. On appeal, the court held that the jury could not have rationally found defendant guilty of aggravated battery. The State presented alternative theories to establish defendant's guilt: direct responsibility or accountability. Defendant was either directly responsible for the victim's death based upon defendant's statement and a doctor's statement that defendant's knife was most likely to have caused the fatal wound, or legally accountable, even if defendant's actions were spontaneous and unplanned. The State established the elements necessary for finding defendant accountable for the actions of the other inmates who took part in the attack. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. It did not err when it refused to give the jury the tendered lesser-included offense instruction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for murder.

 

208 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ruiz


No. 60303


Supreme Court of Illinois


107 Ill. 2d 19; 479 N.E.2d 922; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 240; 88 Ill. Dec. 902



June 5, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. James J. Bailey, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied his motion to reassign his request for post-conviction relief and which dismissed his request for post-conviction relief. Petitioner and a co-defendant were convicted in separate trials for the murders of three men and for armed violence and unlawful restraint.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted, and he subsequently filed a request for post-conviction relief. Because the same judge that presided over his trial was the presiding judge on the post-conviction matter, petitioner filed a motion to reassign the post-conviction matter to a different judge, which was denied. The trial court dismissed the petition. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The matter should have been reassigned under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122-8 (Supp. 1984) even though the statute was not effective until after the post-conviction petition was filed. The statute changed a procedural law, and was therefore applicable to the pending action and to petitioner's motion filed after the state was enacted.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's denial of petitioner's motion to reassign, vacated the trial court's dismissal of the request for post-conviction relief, and remanded for reassignment.

 

209 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Quinn v. Donnewald


No. 61631


Supreme Court of Illinois


107 Ill. 2d 179; 483 N.E.2d 216; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 255; 90 Ill. Dec. 898



June 5, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 27, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. David J. Shields, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizens sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted summary judgment to appellees, state treasurer and state comptroller, in appellants' action to have the Compensation Review Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 63, paras. 901-906 (1984), declared unconstitutional and to enjoin appellees from expending public funds pursuant to the Act.


OVERVIEW: The Compensation Review Board was created by the Act to recommend compensation for members of the General Assembly, judges, constitutional officers, and certain appointed officers of the state. The Board submitted an initial report of recommendations to the General Assembly. The report was disapproved. The Board submitted an amended report, which was not disapproved by a majority of both houses of the General Assembly, so funds were appropriated for the salary increases recommended. Appellants filed an action seeking a declaratory judgment that the Act violated the state constitution and enjoining appellees from expending public funds pursuant to the Act. The circuit court granted appellees' motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the Act was enacted through the law-making process and in the normal legislative manner, satisfying the constitutional directive that salaries be provided or established by law. The Act itself and the appropriations bill were passed the General Assembly and presented to the Governor for possible veto. Thus, the requirements of article IV, section 8(c), and article IV, sections 9(a) and (b) were satisfied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to appellees in appellants' action to have the Act declared unconstitutional and to enjoin appellees from expending any public funds pursuant to the Act.

 

210 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Madej


No. 57256


Supreme Court of Illinois


106 Ill. 2d 201; 478 N.E.2d 392; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 214; 88 Ill. Dec. 77



April 19, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 31, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Vincent Bentivenga, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found the defendant guilty of one count of murder and on three counts of felony murder predicated by the felonies of armed robbery, rape, and deviate sexual assault and sentenced defendant to death for the murder and three counts of felony murder, and imprisonment for armed robbery and rape.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of one count of murder, three counts of felony murder, and one count each of armed robbery, rape, and deviate sexual assault at a bench trial. Defendant waived his right to a jury for sentencing, and the trial judge sentenced defendant to death for the murder convictions and imprisonment for the other crimes. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's convictions. The court held that: (1) the death penalty statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1, was constitutional; (2) defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel because his attorney did not introduce evidence, as a choice of defense strategy did not support the claim for ineffective representation; (3) defendant was not denied effective counsel because his attorney did not present sufficient mitigating evidence during the sentencing hearing or pursue the defense of intoxication, as defendant failed to show how either would have produced a different result; (4) defendant's waiver of his right to a jury in the sentencing phase was voluntarily waived; and (5) not advising defendant that a jury's decision to impose the death sentence would have had to have been unanimous was not an error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions of murder and three counts of felony murder predicated by the felonies of armed robbery, rape, and deviate sexual assault and defendant's sentence of death for the murder and three counts of felony murder, and imprisonment for armed robbery and rape.

 

211 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Chicago Tribune Co. v. Johnson


No. 59453


Supreme Court of Illinois


106 Ill. 2d 63; 477 N.E.2d 482; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 204; 87 Ill. Dec. 505



April 19, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Joseph M. Wosik, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff newspaper appealed the judgment of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which reversed the circuit court's decision that the newspaper was exempt from liability under provisions of the Use Tax Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 439.1 et seq. (1981), and the regulations adopted by defendant Illinois Department of Revenue (Department) on the newspaper's purchase of machinery for a new printing facility.


OVERVIEW: The Department adopted a regulation, Ill. Admin. Code tit. 86, § 130.330(b)(5), which provided that the process of printing did not constitute manufacturing, and that the newspaper's purchase of machinery did not qualify for the "manufacturing-machinery" exemption under the Act. The newspaper sought review when the appellate court reversed the order of the circuit court that had held that the presses and equipment had qualified for the exemption. The court affirmed the judgment of the district court. The court found the legislative background of the manufacturing-machinery exemption indicated that printing presses were not intended to be included in the exemption. Newspaper publishers differed from other manufacturers because the legislature had made their product, newsprint, not subject to the retailers' occupation tax and use tax, so that they enjoyed a benefit that other manufacturers have not been given. Finally, the court found a rational relationship between the scope of the manufacturing-machinery exemption and the purpose for which it was enacted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court that reversed the circuit court's holding that the newspaper qualified for the manufacturing exemption of the Illinois Use Tax Act.

 

212 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Brisbon


No. 56560


Supreme Court of Illinois


106 Ill. 2d 342; 478 N.E.2d 402; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 221; 88 Ill. Dec. 87



April 19, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 31, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. Herman S. Haase, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; sentence vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant inmate was charged with the murder of another inmate. The Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois) affirmed the jury's determination that there were no mitigating factors sufficient to preclude a sentence of death. Defendant appealed the judgment of conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that a comment alluding to the fact that he would be eligible for parole if sentenced to life in prison was a reversible error because the information could have angered the jury to the point of influencing their consideration of the imposition the death penalty. He also argued that it was an error for the prosecution to argue that discontinuing capital punishment caused a sharp increase in the number of homicides in the country. The court determined that by injecting the parole consideration into the penalty determination, the jury's attention was diverted from the offense and the offender and was focused upon a speculative possibility that might or might not occur. The court held that the possibility of a parole was immaterial to the aggravating and mitigating issues of a capital sentencing hearing. After upholding the conviction, the court remanded to the trial court for a new sentencing hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder. However, the court vacated the death sentence and remanded the case for a new sentencing hearing.

 

213 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Nutrition Headquarters, Inc. v. Department of Revenue


No. 60271


Supreme Court of Illinois


106 Ill. 2d 58; 477 N.E.2d 235; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 203; 87 Ill. Dec. 488



March 29, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County, the Hon. Bill F. Green, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Illinois Department of Revenue (department) appealed from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District (Illinois) which held that plaintiff taxpayer's actions of attaching mailing labels to, sorting, and mailing catalogs which were brought into Illinois for the sole purpose of labeling and mailing the material for delivery throughout the U.S. was exempt from taxation.


OVERVIEW: The court explained that the Service Use Tax Act taxes the privilege of using in Illinois real or tangible personal property acquired as an incident to the purchase of a service from a serviceman. 120 Ill. Comp. Stat. § 439.33 (1979). While the taxpayer acknowledged that its catalogs are tangible personal property acquired incident to the purchase of services, it maintained that the temporary storage exception to the act precluded taxation of the material sent out of state and that a contrary result would unconstitutionally burden interstate commerce. The taxpayer maintained, and the appellate court held, that the exception applied because the catalogs were merely labeled in Illinois before continuing their interstate journey. The state argued that the catalogs were used in Illinois before their return to the stream of commerce. The court affirmed, finding that the exception for property which, after being brought into the state and stored here temporarily, was physically attached to other property (the mailing labels) and used solely outside the state covered the taxpayer's activities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the holding in favor of the taxpayer and against the department.

 

214 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Herget Nat'l Bank v. Kenney


No. 59673


Supreme Court of Illinois


105 Ill. 2d 405; 475 N.E.2d 863; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 188; 86 Ill. Dec. 484



February 22, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Tazewell County, the Hon. John A. Gorman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois) reversed the circuit court's issuance of a writ of mandamus. The writ directed defendant, the Director of the Department of Conservation, to institute eminent domain proceedings in order to determine compensation due to plaintiff landowner for the taking. The landowner's petition for leave to appeal was granted. The appellate court determined that the circuit court had no jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The landowner owned real estate. The land was submerged by a lake as a result of the state's building of causeways across the lake. The lake was later drained and immediately refilled and restocked with fish. Upon the state's refusal to purchase the property, the landowner instituted a proceeding for mandamus to make the director of the department institute eminent domain proceedings in order to determine just compensation. The court found that there was a physical invasion and taking of the property. Therefore, as guaranteed by Ill. Const. art. I, § 15 (1970), the landowner was entitled to a determination of its damages. The failure of the director to institute such proceedings violated the Illinois Constitution. As such, the landowner's action was not an action against the state, but was, rather, against the unconstitutional conduct of a state official. Therefore, the issuance of a writ of mandamus, which would compel the director to institute eminent domain proceedings, was proper. The circuit court had the jurisdiction to issue such writ.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's reversal of the circuit court's decision. The court then affirmed the circuit court's issuance of the writ of mandamus in favor of the landowner.

 

215 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Del Vecchio


No. 52800


Supreme Court of Illinois


105 Ill. 2d 414; 475 N.E.2d 840; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 189; 86 Ill. Dec. 461



February 22, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 29, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Louis Garippo, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), in which he was sentenced to death, as well as to a term in prison, upon his conviction for murder pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(a)(2) (1977), rape pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-1 (1977), deviate sexual assault pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-3 (1977), and burglary pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 19-1 (1977).


OVERVIEW: As an initial matter, the court rejected defendant's contention that he was entitled to a reversal on the basis of ineffective assistance of counsel with respect to his attorney's withdrawal of a purportedly meritorious insanity defense and the attorney's alternative reliance upon an intoxication defense. The court found that such an assignment of error was without merit where defendant failed to establish that he was substantially prejudiced by his counsel's alleged ineffectiveness. The court similarly found no impermissible prejudice from the alleged improper comment from opposing counsel or the alleged improper admission of testimony that defendant had committed adultery. The court further found that the trial judge's refusal to grant a mistrial or to excuse veniremen who overheard a juror state her personal opinion of defendant was proper where there was no evidence that the single, isolated comment impacted the jury's ability to reach a verdict based solely upon the evidence. The court affirmed, concluding that no error was demonstrated in either the refusal to excuse a death-qualified juror or in the procedures used to sentence defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's criminal conviction and death sentence.

 

216 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Collins


No. 55659


Supreme Court of Illinois


106 Ill. 2d 237; 478 N.E.2d 267; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 216; 87 Ill. Dec. 910



February 22, 1985, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 31, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Thomas J. Maloney, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) entered a judgment of conviction against defendants for armed robbery, aggravated kidnapping, and murder. Defendants were sentenced to death, and the trial court imposed concurrent 60-year prison sentences for the armed robbery and aggravated kidnapping convictions. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, along with several others, were involved in the murder of three individuals. Defendants claimed there was insufficient evidence for the jury to find them guilty of the murders beyond a reasonable doubt because the prosecution's chief witness' testimony was unreliable. They also contended that the trial court erroneously admitted evidence that caused them prejudice and deprived them of a fair trial. Defendants also alleged ineffective assistance of counsel and prosecutorial misconduct. The court held that: (1) there was sufficient evidence to support the jury's verdict; (2) photos obtained from a garbage bag outside one defendant's apartment were properly admitted because the search of the garbage bag was constitutionally permissible; (3) evidence that certain witnesses were in protective custody or relocated was not prejudicial and did not deprive defendants of a fair trial; (4) there was no abuse of discretion in allowing certain methods of cross-examination and prosecutorial remarks that did not constitute reversible errors; and (5) defendants failed to establish that their convictions would have turned out differently but for the alleged errors of their counsel.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences entered against defendants for murder and armed robbery were affirmed. The convictions for aggravated kidnapping were affirmed. The sentences for aggravated kidnapping were reduced to 30 years.

 

217 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Coldwell Banker Residential Real Estate Services, Inc. v. Clayton


No. 59511


Supreme Court of Illinois


105 Ill. 2d 389; 475 N.E.2d 536; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 187; 86 Ill. Dec. 322; 1986-1 Trade Cas. (CCH) P66,991



February 22, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant director of the Department of Registration and Education sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted plaintiff broker's motion for summary judgment, finding that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111, para. 5732(e)(20) (1981) was unconstitutional. Plaintiff cross-appealed from the circuit court's finding that its marketing plans violated the statute.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff broker filed an action against defendant director of the Department of Registration and Education, alleging that plaintiff's marketing plans were not violative of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111, para. 5732(e)(20) (1981) of the Real Estate Brokers and Salesmen License Act. Plaintiff also claimed the statute was unconstitutional. The trial court found that plaintiff's marketing plans were prohibited by the statute, but the statute was unconstitutional because it violated the due process clause, Ill. Const. art. I, § 2. Upon appeal by both parties, the court affirmed. The court found that both of plaintiff's marketing plans were prohibited by the statute because they both offered incentives to induce buyers or sellers to enter into real estate transactions. The court held that the statute was unconstitutional because the state failed to establish that its interest in protecting consumers was directly advanced by the statute. The court noted that a more limited speech regulation that specifically prohibited the use of deceptive or misleading offerings as inducements would have been an appropriate limitation on commercial speech.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order that granted plaintiff broker's motion for summary judgment and found that a statute prohibiting the use of prizes and free gifts by real estate brokers to induce buyers or sellers to enter into real estate transactions was unconstitutional. The court held the statute was unconstitutional because the state failed to establish that its interest in protecting consumers was directly advanced by the statute.

219 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Steppan


No. 59978


Supreme Court of Illinois


105 Ill. 2d 310; 473 N.E.2d 1300; 1985 Ill. LEXIS 179; 85 Ill. Dec. 495



January 23, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. Robert A. Nolan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed directly the finding of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 19(1)(b) (1981) was unconstitutional. Defendant appealed to the appellate court his convictions for burglary and possession of burglary tools and his sentence for the latter, which was to be served consecutively with sentences in unrelated cases. The court granted defendant's motion to transfer his appeal to the court.


OVERVIEW: The court held that a person could properly be convicted of burglary under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 19(1)(a) (1981) when, without authority, he knowingly entered a motor vehicle with the intent to steal the vehicle itself. Since defendant did not dispute the sufficiency of the evidence establishing his unlawful entry and his intent to steal the entire vehicle, the court affirmed the burglary conviction. The court held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 19(1)(b) (1981), under which the sentence for theft from a vehicle could possibly be greater than would be imposed if the whole vehicle and its contents were stolen, did not violate Ill. Const. art. I, §§ 2 and 11. The court affirmed the imposition of the consecutive sentence for possession of burglary tools, believing that the trial court complied with § 5(8)(4)(b) of the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005(8)(4)(b) (1981), which prohibited imposition of a consecutive sentence unless a court believed that such a term was required to protect the public from further criminal conduct by the defendant, the basis for which the court was to set forth in the record.


OUTCOME: The decision of the circuit court was affirmed in part and reversed in part. The cause was remanded to the circuit court for sentencing on defendant's burglary conviction.

 

220 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Dornfeld v. Julian


No. 59841


Supreme Court of Illinois


104 Ill. 2d 261; 472 N.E.2d 431; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 378; 84 Ill. Dec. 471



November 30, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. Edmund Bart, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged a judgment of the Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois), heard on appeal from the circuit court's decision that held the two-year limitation in the § 4 of the Illinois Paternity Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1354 (1981), to be unconstitutional, but held that the balance of the Act was valid and denied the father's motion to dismiss appellee mother's paternity suit.


OVERVIEW: The mother brought a paternity suit claiming the father was the father of her child born out of wedlock. The father sought to dismiss the complaint because the action was not brought within two years of the birth of the child. While the case was pending, the two-year limitation period was determined to be unconstitutional. The circuit court ruled that although the two-year limitation was unconstitutional, the balance of the Act was valid and denied the father's motion to dismiss. The court affirmed. It found that the objective of the Act was to provide for the paternal support, maintenance, and education of children born of unwed parents, thereby converting a father's moral obligation of support into a legal one, and preventing such children from becoming public charges. As the balance of the Act met its legislative objectives and policy considerations indicated that the legislature intended the Act to remain a valid statute, even with the limitation period excised, the court found the balance of the Act was constitutional and remanded the matter for trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's decision holding the balance of the Act to be constitutional and denying the father's motion to dismiss the mother's paternity action.

 

221 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Stewart


No. 56332


Supreme Court of Illinois


105 Ill. 2d 22; 473 N.E.2d 840; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 402; 85 Ill. Dec. 241



November 30, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 1, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County, the Hon. John E. Sype, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) that convicted him of murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murdering two people during the robbery of a grocery store. He was sentenced to death, and he appealed. The court affirmed. In his appeal, defendant raised several arguments. Several of his arguments focused on the search warrant affidavits. Defendant contended that factual misstatements were intentionally inserted into the affidavits to deceive the magistrate and therefore the evidence obtained pursuant to the warrants should have been suppressed under Franks. The statements contained within a search warrant affidavit were presumed valid. To overcome the presumption of validity, appellant was required to make a substantial preliminary showing that false statements were deliberately included in the affidavit, or included with a reckless disregard for the truth, and that the statements were necessary to a finding of probable cause. If these conditions were met, appellant was entitled to an evidentiary hearing. Defendant was provided this hearing; however, he failed to prove by a preponderance of the evidence that there was a deliberate falsehood and to show, even if the misstatements were omitted, that probable cause was lacking.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant of murder and sentencing him to death was affirmed.

People v. Mack


No. 55370


Supreme Court of Illinois


105 Ill. 2d 103; 473 N.E.2d 880; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 404; 85 Ill. Dec. 281

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was granted direct appeal after he was convicted at a bench trial by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of three counts of murder, Ill. Rev. Stat. 1977, ch. 38, para. 9-1(a)(1) - (3), and armed robbery Ill. Rev. Stat. 1977, ch. 38, para. 18-2, based on the shooting of a security guard during a bank robbery. Defendant contended the consultation was a constitutionally impermissible abuse of prosecutorial discretion and that it made the death penalty arbitrary and freakish. The court held that the state was not barred from consulting the victim's family in a capital case. Defendant also challenged the excusal for cause of prospective jurors who were against the death panel, the racial makeup of the jury, and claimed that the statute unconstitutionally vested the jury with unlimited discretion to determine nonstatutory aggravating factors and that he was denied effective assistance of counsel, who failed to show the shooting was accidental. The court rejected these arguments, affirmed the conviction and sentence for intentionally killing the guard, vacated the other two murder convictions, and set an execution date.

224 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. Partee


No. 59736


Supreme Court of Illinois


105 Ill. 2d 186; 473 N.E.2d 944; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 408; 85 Ill. Dec. 345



November 30, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 1, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Joseph Wosik, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city challenged a ruling from the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which reversed the injunctive relief and summary judgment that the circuit court granted to the city in the city's action against defendant telephone company regarding certain charges relating to its municipal utility tax.


OVERVIEW: The city instituted a municipal utility tax pursuant to the Public Utilities Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 2/3, para. 36(a). The telephone company billed the city for certain tax-related charges. The city filed suit to enjoin the telephone company from billing the city for the charges and for the recovery of such sums that the telephone company previously collected from the city. The city prevailed at the trial level, but the judgment was reversed in the lower appellate court. The city appealed further. The court reversed the judgment of the lower appellate court and affirmed the judgment of the circuit court. The court held that the only "customer" not subject to the additional charge authorized by para. 36(a) was the taxing municipality. A common sense construction of para. 36(a) precluded the requirement that the taxing municipality pay the tax and thereafter pay a service charge to the utility for having received the tax money and then refunding it. Elimination of the billing of the additional charge to the city presented no burdensome accounting problems because para. 36(a) provided that the additional charge was to be shown separately on each customer's utility bill.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower appellate court and affirmed the circuit court's injunction and judgment in the city's favor in the city's action against the telephone company for elimination of additional charges related to the city's municipal utility tax. The court held that the city was the only "customer" that was not subject to the statutory additional charge.

OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision denying defendant's petition for post-conviction relief.

 

226 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Fernetti


Nos. 59263, 59295 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


104 Ill. 2d 19; 470 N.E.2d 501; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 356; 83 Ill. Dec. 375



October 19, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 59263. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Fulton County, the Hon. William L. Randolph, Judge, presiding.

No. 59295. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Kenneth Gillis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit courts vacated; causes remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Two defendants appealed decisions of the Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois) and the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), arguing that involuntary manslaughter could not serve as a predicate felony to support their armed-violence convictions.


OVERVIEW: The first defendant was found guilty of involuntary manslaughter and armed violence. Since both charges were based on the same act, the trial court entered judgment only on the greater offense, armed violence. The second defendant was found guilty of involuntary manslaughter and armed violence based on involuntary manslaughter. His involuntary-manslaughter conviction was vacated, and he was sentenced on the armed-violence conviction. Each challenged the use of involuntary manslaughter as a predicate felony for armed violence under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33A-2 (1981). The court held that involuntary manslaughter, just as voluntary manslaughter, could not be enhanced to a Class X felony under the armed-violence statute. This was so because the legislature did not intend the Class X consequences of armed violence to apply to a nondeliberate act. Involuntary manslaughter involved no intent that could be deterred by enhanced punishment for use of a weapon.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decisions below. The first defendant's conviction was vacated, and the circuit court was directed to enter judgment based upon its original finding that she was guilty of involuntary manslaughter. The second defendant's conviction was vacated, and the circuit court was directed to reinstate its judgment of conviction for involuntary manslaughter.

 

227 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Flores


No. 59424


Supreme Court of Illinois


104 Ill. 2d 40; 470 N.E.2d 307; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 359; 83 Ill. Dec. 349



October 19, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Vermilion County, the Hon. James K. Robinson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's case was on direct appeal from the Circuit Court of Vermilion County (Illinois) because Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1404 (1975), which was the basis for his conviction of the delivery of a substance represented to be a controlled substance was ruled unconstitutional. Defendant challenged the trial court's finding that a part of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-4.1 (1977) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in finding para. 115-4.1 unconstitutional because it did not violate the separation of powers clause in the Illinois Constitution of 1970. The part of the statute that was ruled unconstitutional provided that the trial court was required to wait two days before proceeding with defendant's trial in his absence. In reviewing the statute, the court determined that to dictate how long a trial judge was required to wait before proceeding with a trial, when a defendant had willfully absented himself from his trial once it commenced, unconstitutionally infringed upon the trial judge's authority to control his docket. The court concluded that the statute was permissive rather than mandatory and thus, was not unconstitutional. Because the statute was permissive, whether to proceed with the trial was within the trial judge's discretion. The court determined that the trial judge did not violate the statute when he refused to wait two days before proceeding with defendant's trial in his absence. Defendant waived his right to be present at trial because he voluntarily absented himself from the trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court reversed the part of the trial court's judgment, which held that the statute was unconstitutional. The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Ostergren v. Forest Preserve Dist.


No. 59237


Supreme Court of Illinois


104 Ill. 2d 128; 471 N.E.2d 191; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 368; 83 Ill. Dec. 892



October 19, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 30, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County, the Hon. Charles P. Connor, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant district appealed from the judgment of the Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois), which reversed a trial court judgment that dismissed plaintiff snowmobiler's action against the district and others for injuries sustained while he was snowmobiling in the park. The issue was the constitutionality of a provision of the Snowmobile Registration and Safety Act.


OVERVIEW: The snowmobiler was injured when his snowmobile struck a trench in the park. The snowmobiler brought an action against the district, and others, for his injuries. The trial court granted the district's motion to dismiss, and the snowmobiler appealed. The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment and the district sought further review. The issue was whether the Snowmobile Registration and Safety Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 605-1(I) (1981), which provided that an owner of premises owed no duty to keep the premises safe for snowmobiling, violated the equal protection and due process provisions of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, Ill. Const. art I, § 2. The court held that: (1) the Act was a reasonable exercise of police power; (2) the different standard of care for tort liability in snowmobile accidents was justified due to the inherent danger of snowmobile operation; and (3) the Act did not deprive the snowmobiler of a remedy but merely restricted the liability of landowners who would otherwise have to undertake massive repairs to make their property safe for snowmobiling.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment and affirmed the judgment of the trial court which had dismissed the snowmobiler's complaint against the district.

Illinois Pure Water Committee, Inc. v. Director of Public Health


No. 56315


Supreme Court of Illinois


104 Ill. 2d 243; 470 N.E.2d 988; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 376; 83 Ill. Dec. 568



October 19, 1984, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County, the Hon. Ronald Niemann, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the Director of Public Health (DPH), the Director of the Environmental Protection Agency (EPA), and a water company, appealed a decision from the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois). The DPH and the EPA were enjoined from enforcing a fluoridation statute. The company was enjoined from fluoridating its water supply. Plaintiff, a committee for pure water, filed an action claiming that the fluoridation act was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The committee's complaint alleged that fluoride in public drinking water was dangerous to health and that its use did not prevent tooth decay. The circuit court held that § 7a of "An Act to provide for safeguarding the public health by vesting certain measures of control and supervision in the Department of Public Health over public water supplies in the state," Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para. 121g1 (1981), was unconstitutional. They argued that the statute's enforcement might not be enjoined merely on the showing that it was debatable whether requiring fluoridation was a valid public health measure. The committee argued that the rights to life and health were placed in jeopardy without due process of law, and the validity of the statute could be upheld only if a compelling state interest was shown that required it. On appeal, the court found that the committee did not sustain its burden of showing that the fluoridation statute was so unreasonable as to be invalid. The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court. The court could not say that the evidence was sufficient to declare that the fluoridation statute was an unreasonable exercise of the police power.

Kalodimos v. Morton Grove


No. 58467


Supreme Court of Illinois


103 Ill. 2d 483; 470 N.E.2d 266; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 350; 83 Ill. Dec. 308



October 19, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Albert Green, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee village enacted an ordinance, banning the possession of all operable handguns. Appellant residents filed an action against the village, seeking an injunction and a declaratory judgment that the ordinance violated Ill. Const. art. I, § 22, and was an unreasonable exercise of the police power. The trial court granted summary judgment to the village, and the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) affirmed. The residents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The village ordinance completely banned the possession of handguns, with exceptions for security guards, law enforcement, and inoperable weapons. On appeal, the court analyzed the ordinance under the Illinois constitution. The court found that the ordinance was valid under the home rule statutes of Illinois because the village's interest did not implicate a state concern. Further, under Ill. Const. art. I, § 22, the court analyzed the "right to bear arms" provision of the state constitution and determined that it was the framers' intent that some classifications of firearms could be banned altogether, just not firearms as a whole. Finally, the court entertained the notion that the ordinance violated police powers. However, the court determined that the ordinance did not infringe upon a fundamental right and thus passed muster under a "rational basis" test. The court concluded that there was a rational basis, safety, for the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision, which affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the village.

People v. J.S.


Nos. 59319, 59320, 59556 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


103 Ill. 2d 395; 469 N.E.2d 1090; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 342; 83 Ill. Dec. 156

DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state, in three consolidated cases, appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which held para. 702--7(6) of the Juvenile Court Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 701--1 et seq. (1983), unconstitutional. The paragraph provided that minors who were at least 15 at the time of one of the following offenses were to be charged as adults: murder, rape, deviate sexual assault and armed robbery with a firearm.


OVERVIEW: In arguing that the trial court erred in holding para. 702--7(6) of the Juvenile Court Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 701--1 et. seq. (1983), unconstitutional, the state claimed that in setting apart for adult prosecution specific offenders (those 15 and older) and offenses (rape, murder, deviate sexual assault, and armed robbery with a firearm), the legislature drew a rational distinction within its authority which did not violate either equal protection or due process. Defendants, on the other hand, claimed that the distinction was arbitrary and discriminatory and thus violated both procedural and substantive due process and equal protection. The court noted that the legislature created the juvenile court system and that it was within its power to establish statutory classifications as long as they bore a rational relationship to a legitimate state interest. The court found that the limited nature of the exception to juvenile court jurisdiction was rationally based, both on the age of the offender and on the threat which the particular offense posed on the community.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments that held unconstitutional a provision of the Juvenile Court Act that provided that individuals who were 15 or older at the time of commission of specific offenses be treated as adults. Accordingly, the dismissal of the accusatory instrument against each defendant was reversed, and the cases were remanded to the trial court.

 

235 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Board of Comm'rs v. County of Du Page


No. 59581


Supreme Court of Illinois


103 Ill. 2d 422; 469 N.E.2d 1370; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 344; 83 Ill. Dec. 224



October 3, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. John S. Teschner, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a previous appeal in the action, the court determined that appellant county's practice of retaining the interest on tax funds it collected from appellee library district was unconstitutional. The circuit court found upon remand that the library district was not entitled to retroactive relief. The county sought review of the judgment of the Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois), which reversed the circuit court.


OVERVIEW: The issue before the court was whether the library district was entitled to retroactive relief in the form of a refund of the interest that the county had earned on taxes collected from the district. The court's previous ruling, on the first appeal of the case, was that the statute upon which the county relied to retain the interest was unconstitutional. It remanded the case to the circuit court, which held that the district was not entitled to retroactive relief. The appellate court reversed. The court reversed the appellate court, affirming the circuit court's judgment. The court held that retroactive relief was not appropriate because the county had reasonably relied upon existing law for its authority to retain the interest, and the new principle of law established in the first appeal had not been clearly foreshadowed. The court further held that the purpose of its earlier decision would be best served if it did not impose a burden that pre-dated its finding that the statute was unconstitutional. Lastly, it would be inequitable to impose a retrospective burden on the county. Thus, the court held that interest should be awarded prospectively from the date of the first appeal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's decision and affirmed the circuit court's judgment that the library district was not entitled to retroactive relief in the form of a refund of interest on taxes the county collected from the district.

 

236 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


General Tel. Co. v. Johnson


No. 58864


Supreme Court of Illinois


103 Ill. 2d 363; 469 N.E.2d 1067; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 340; 83 Ill. Dec. 133



October 3, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County, the Hon. Simon L. Friedman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois) granted a temporary injunction enjoining appellant tax authorities from transferring money from a protest fund. However, before a hearing on the merits was held, the Messages Tax Act (MTA), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 467.1 et seq. (1981), was amended. Thus, the trial court granted summary judgment in appellee taxpayer's favor, and the authorities appealed.


OVERVIEW: In its protest action, the taxpayer sought a judicial determination of whether the MTA authorized the use of combined apportionment, a computation that reduced the taxpayer's apportionment factor and accordingly reduced its invested-capital tax liability. The amendment, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 467.1 (1982), prohibited the use of combined apportionment for purposes of the MTA. The trial court concluded that, insofar as the amendment retroactively prohibited combined apportionment, it violated the due process principles of the federal and state constitutions. On appeal, the court upheld the validity of the amendment and reversed the summary judgment granted to the taxpayer. The court held that the taxpayer had no vested right in the continuance of a taxing statute and that the retroactive tax measure did not violate the taxpayer's due process rights. The court considered the nature of the measure and the circumstances leading to its adoption. That court found that the taxpayer did not change its position in reasonable reliance on the prior law and that the taxpayer should have foreseen the possibility that its proposed use of combined apportionment would have been disapproved.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of the taxpayer. The court remanded for further proceedings.

Chicago Gravel Co. v. Rosewell


No. 59414


Supreme Court of Illinois


103 Ill. 2d 433; 469 N.E.2d 1098; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 345; 83 Ill. Dec. 164



October 3, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Earl Arkiss, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county treasurer sought review of the judgment of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which reversed the trial court's judgment that appellee landowner was liable for payment of taxes that had not been assessed in prior years due to a clerical error.


OVERVIEW: Due to a clerical error in the assessor's office in copying the acreage of the landowner's property as 10.8 acres rather than 70.8 acres, the landowner's property was under taxed. Three assessments occurred without discovery of the error. The error was first discovered when the landowner appealed the proposed valuations on all the parcels that it owned. The county treasurer then began administrative back tax proceedings against the landowner. The landowner filed a complaint to restrain the further assessment and collection of additional taxes. The trial court found in favor of the county treasurer and the landowner appealed. The appellate court reversed, and the county treasurer appealed. The court affirmed. The court held that if property was not assessed at all, it could be assessed in later years as omitted property, but where an assessment had been made too low due to clerical error, it could not be reassessed in subsequent years as having been omitted. The court determined that the parcel was under assessed so, pursuant to Illinois law (Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 701 (1979)), the taxing authorities could not collect back taxes, interest, or penalties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court reversing the judgment of the trial court. The court affirmed the judgment that the landowner was not liable for payment of taxes that had not been assessed in prior years due to a clerical error.

In re Marriage of Logston


No. 58631


Supreme Court of Illinois


103 Ill. 2d 266; 469 N.E.2d 167; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 332; 82 Ill. Dec. 633



September 20, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County, the Hon. Dennis J. Jacobsen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband sought review of the judgments from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which found appellant was in contempt of court for his failure to pay a maintenance obligation in a dissolution-of-marriage case and that denied appellant's motion to reconsider. The issue raised was whether Ill. Rev. Stat. 1983, ch. 110, para. 12 -- 1001 constituted a defense to the contempt order.


OVERVIEW: To enforce the maintenance provision of a dissolution-of-marriage judgment, appellee wife initiated contempt proceedings against appellant husband. Following the orders that found appellant was in contempt of court, appellant challenged the decisions, contending that Ill. Rev. Stat. 1983, ch. 110, para. 12 -- 1001 constituted a valid defense to the contempt order and that the trial court abused its discretion. The orders were affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that the trial court neither abused its discretion nor reached a decision contrary to the manifest weight of the evidence when it rejected appellant's defense of inability to pay. Additionally, the court held that Ill. Rev. Stat. 1983, ch. 110, para. 12 -- 1001 was not so vague as to violate the constitutional principals of due process. The court also found that Ill. Rev. Stat. 1983, ch. 110, para. 12 -- 1001 was not a defense to the contempt order. Further, it was determined that on remand the contempt order had to be revised to correct the problem that neither order provided for appellant's release from jail if he paid the arrearage after he was incarcerated.


OUTCOME: The orders that found appellant husband in contempt for his failure to pay a maintenance obligation to appellee wife and that denied appellant's motion to reconsider were affirmed in part because the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it rejected appellant's defense of inability to pay. Additionally, the court reversed in part because the personal property exemption statute was not so vague as to violate the constitution.

People v. Singleton


No. 59645


Supreme Court of Illinois


103 Ill. 2d 339; 469 N.E.2d 200; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 338; 82 Ill. Dec. 666



September 20, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of McLean County, the Hon. Wayne C. Townley, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court affirmed in part and reversed in part; sentence vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois), which affirmed defendant's sentence for aggravated battery consecutive to a prior misdemeanor sentence under the provisions of § 5-8-4(d) of the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-4(d) (1981).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated battery, a felony. The trial court sentenced defendant to a 3-year term for the aggravated battery, to be served consecutively to a 10-month term that he was already serving for a prior, unrelated misdemeanor. In affirming defendant's sentence, the appellate court held that para. 1005-8-4(d) did not require merger of the felony and misdemeanor sentences. The court granted defendant's petition for leave to appeal from the appellate court's order, and reversed the judgment of the appellate court. Under the plain language of para. 1005-8-4(d), defendant's misdemeanor sentence was required to be merged in and run concurrently with the felony sentence. The court interpreted the term "shall" as mandatory rather than directory. Para. 1005-8-4(e) was irrelevant to defendant's case, as it concerned multiple sentences imposed at the same time for related crimes. The court found that para. 1005-8-4(d) was a mandatory limitation on the trial court's discretion in para. 1005-8-4(a), which generally allowed concurrent or consecutive sentences to be imposed by the trial court. Finally, defendant's failure to object in the trial court did not waive the error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court insofar as it affirmed the sentence imposed by the trial court. The court vacated the sentence imposed by the trial court and remanded the cause to the trial court with directions to resentence defendant for the offense of aggravated battery in accordance with the court's opinion.

People v. Heinrich


No. 59239


Supreme Court of Illinois


104 Ill. 2d 137; 470 N.E.2d 966; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 369; 83 Ill. Dec. 546; 68 A.L.R.4th 1003



September 20, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 30, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McLean County, the Hon. William DeCardy, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by information with two counts of criminal defamation under the Ill. Rev. Stat. 1981, ch. 38, para. 27-1. The Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois) dismissed the information on the basis that the statute contravened the First and Fourteenth amendments to the United States Constitution. The state filed an appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant distributed, in public view, a leaflet that stated that the complainant was an unfit mother due to her promiscuity, deviate sexual behavior, illicit drug habit, and four pregnancies out of wedlock. The leaflet gave the name of the complainant and her parents' names and address. Defendant was charged with criminal defamation under Ill. Rev. Stat. 1981, ch. 38, par. 27-1. He moved to dismiss the information, and the circuit court declared the criminal defamation statute unconstitutional and dismissed the charges. The state contended that the statute was constitutional. The defendant maintained that the criminal defamation statute was overly broad. The court reversed the decision because (1) the circuit court did not make an explicit finding that the statute was too broad; rather, it ruled the statute unconstitutional on the basis of the qualified-truth defense, (2) the statute was not overly broad, as it applied only to those words which by their very utterance tended to incite an immediate breach of the peace, and (3) truth was not an absolute defense in a prosecution for criminal defamation of a private person.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's dismissal of defendant's indictment for criminal defamation and holding that the criminal defamation statute was unconstitutional.

People v. Dillon


No. 58912


Supreme Court of Illinois


102 Ill. 2d 522; 468 N.E.2d 964; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 322; 82 Ill. Dec. 310



June 29, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 28, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Daniel P. Glecier, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The prosecution sought review of an order of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) that upheld an order granting defendant's motion to suppress cocaine evidence seized from him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was pulled over because his rear license plate light was out. The police officers discovered there was a warrant for defendant and arrested him. The arresting officer began to process defendant, instructing him to empty his pockets and place his personal belongings on a table. Cocaine was discovered during the process and defendant was charged with possession of cocaine. Defendant's motion to suppress the cocaine evidence was granted and affirmed on appeal. The court reversed the order upholding the order suppressing the cocaine evidence. The court held that the search was part of a lawful inventory search. Probable cause existed for defendant's arrest and detention, and the police properly listed defendant's personal belongings so as to avoid false claims regarding the property when defendant was released. There was no less intrusive way to conduct the inventory. Further, the search of defendant's wallet and its contents were proper subjects of a search incident to a lawful arrest. The case was remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The order upholding the order granting defendant's motion to suppress evidence was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Tumminaro


No. 58029


Supreme Court of Illinois


102 Ill. 2d 331; 465 N.E.2d 90; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 305; 80 Ill. Dec. 299



June 6, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. Edward W. Kowal, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion to dismiss an amended complaint charging him with the offense of operating a motorcycle on one wheel in violation of § 11-1403.2 of the Illinois Vehicle Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-1403.2 (1981). Defendant's motion was based on his claim that para. 11-1403.2 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: In holding para. 11-1403.2 unconstitutional, the trial court found that it mandated a conviction for reckless driving for conduct that might not otherwise constitute that offense. On appeal from that decision, the court disagreed and reversed. Paragraph 11-1403.2 created an absolute liability and its validity had to be determined in light of the authorities relevant to that type of legislation. To constitute a legitimate exercise of the police power, a legislative enactment had to be reasonably related to the public interest intended to be protected and the means adopted had to be reasonable in light of the desired objective. The court held that the Illinois Legislature could have reasonably found that one-wheel motorcycle driving was dangerous and that strict punishment of drivers who operated motorcycles on one wheel was necessary for protection of the public interest. Thus, there was no basis for striking the statute as unreasonable or arbitrary in its classifications. Further, para. 11-1403.2 was not special legislation, nor was it an express amendment to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-503. Thus, it was not unconstitutional for failing to fully set forth para. 11-503.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter for further proceedings.
