People ex rel. Bosworth v. Lowen


Nos. 58718, 58719, 58725 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


102 Ill. 2d 242; 464 N.E.2d 1053; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 297; 80 Ill. Dec. 70



May 25, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeals from the Circuit Court of Will County, the Hon. Michael A. Orenic, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tax collector and intervenor school district appealed from the decision of the Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois) affirming the order granting summary judgments for defendant pollution control facilities. The collector and school district also appealed from the order affirming the trial court's order dismissing the complaint against defendants, Department of Revenue of the State of Illinois (department) and director.


OVERVIEW: The tax collector filed complaints against the pollution control facilities based on tax assessments. The trial court granted summary judgments for the pollution control facilities and the appellate court affirmed. The tax collector and school district filed a complaint against the department and director seeking a declaration that § 21a(3) of the Revenue Act of 1939, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 502a(3) (1981) was unconstitutional. The trial court dismissed the complaint and the appellate court affirmed. The appeals were consolidated. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgments. Section 21a(3) was a method of valuation and did not provide an impermissible reduction in valuation resulting in an invalid exemption. It was recognition from the legislature that the pollution control facilities were not necessarily economically productive and should be valued at their productive earning capacity. Section 21a(3) did not violate Ill. Const. art IX, § 4(b) because the legislature had the power to classify property for tax purposes. The tax collector and school district could only pursue review on the constitutionality issue because they did not pursue their administrative remedies.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court granting summary judgments in favor of the pollution control facilities in the tax collector's action based on tax assessments. The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court dismissing the complaint of the tax collector and school district in their action against the department and director challenging the validity of the Revenue Act of 1939.

 

249 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Jenkins v. Wu


No. 58791


Supreme Court of Illinois


102 Ill. 2d 468; 468 N.E.2d 1162; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 318; 82 Ill. Dec. 382



May 25, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 28, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Myron T. Gomberg, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, hospital board of trustees, challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which ordered it to produce documents requested by plaintiff patient in her malpractice action against defendant physician and nurses. The circuit court held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 8-2101, which rendered the documents privileged, violated the Equal Protection Clause and the prohibition against special legislation.


OVERVIEW: Hospital board contended that it was not required to produce the medical committee review documents because § 8-2101 was not unconstitutional. The court agreed. The exception under § 8-2101, which allowed a physician to gain access to review committee information only in the limited circumstance of a proceeding deciding staff privileges, was necessary in order to protect the due process rights of physicians. However, the court held that the issue in a due process challenge to revocation of staff privileges was not the same as the issue in a medical malpractice action. And, the statute was not one-sided because it provided for the discovery of patient's own records which were the source of her claim. Moreover, the classification of physicians and medical malpractice plaintiffs was rationally related to the state's interest of improving health care through confidential peer review. Accordingly, § 8-2101 offended neither the Illinois nor Federal Equal Protection Clause. In addition, the court held that because the exemption represented an attempt to safeguard the physician's right to due process, the characterization of the legislation as "special" was also erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court and held that the statutory privilege for medical committee review documents was not unconstitutional.

Schlessinger v. Olsen


Nos. 58581, 59169


Supreme Court of Illinois


102 Ill. 2d 497; 468 N.E.2d 1158; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 320; 82 Ill. Dec. 378



May 25, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Modified on Denial of Rehearing September 28, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 58581. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Richard L. Curry, Judge, presiding.

No. 59169. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County, the Hon. Lawrence Inglis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded. Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court reconsidered its denial of a motion to consolidate appeals of two cases, one from the Circuit Court of Cook County and one from the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), challenging whether the unlawfully retained monies collected prior to amendment of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 1003 (1978) should be transferred to the General Revenue Fund of the State Treasury or refunded to those individuals who actually paid the tax.


OVERVIEW: The provision in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 1003 (1978) providing for the retention by the counties, as a distribution of the tax, of 50 percent of the real estate transfer taxes was declared unconstitutional. The section was amended and two cases were brought to decide whether the unlawfully retained monies should have been transferred to the state or refunded. The lower court in Cook county declared the statute unconstitutional in its entirety and concluded in its memorandum opinion that the individuals who paid the transfer tax were entitled to the monies unlawfully retained. The court dismissed the action from Lake County as premature because the lower court in Lake County failed to make any express written finding that there was no just reason for delay, and reversed the judgment of the lower court in Cook County. The court held that the funds in controversy should have been delivered to the appropriate county officers.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal from Lake County as premature and reversed the judgment from Cook County against the county.

People v. Taylor

Supreme Court of Illinois

Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-1(a)(1)(c) (1981). The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants murdered two victims and were convicted of murder and armed violence. The trial court sentenced defendants to natural life imprisonment under § 5-8-1(a)(1)(c) of the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-1(a)(1)(c) (1981), which set natural life imprisonment as the mandatory sentence for murdering more than one victim. On the state's appeal from the appellate court's judgment vacating and remanding the sentence, the court reversed and affirmed the trial court's sentence of natural life imprisonment. II, § 1, respectively.

252 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


SANELLI v. GLENVIEW STATE BANK


Docket No. 57935


SUPREME COURT OF ILLINOIS


1984 Ill. LEXIS 270



April 27, 1984 



DISPOSITION:  [*1] Reversed and remanded, with directions. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff beneficiaries appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendant bank's amended motion to dismiss the beneficiaries' class action complaint. The complaint alleged that the bank, which served as land trustee, had breached its fiduciary duty by purchasing the trust property for its own benefit at public sale and held the property in constructive trust for the beneficiaries.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether the retroactivity provision of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 148, para. 81-84 (Supp. 1982) (Act) violated the separation of powers established by the Ill. Const. art. II, § 1 (1970) and the impairment of contracts prohibition of the U.S. Const. art I, § 10 and Ill. Const. art. I, § 16 (1970) or the various provisions of the state and federal constitutions. The beneficiaries had entered into a land trust agreement with the bank, gave a collateral assignment of their beneficial interest as collateral, and the bank sold the property at allegedly below market price after they defaulted. The court found that the Act dictated that the rights and duties of the bank were unaffected by the fact that they served both as land trustee and secured creditor. The statute stated that it did not affect the trustee's duties, the bank's extension of credit was not a breach of duty, and there were no damages due. However, because the Act attempted to change the law retroactively, the court found that the statute violated the principle of separation of powers and was unconstitutional. The court reversed and remanded the case to the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and held that the retroactivity section of the Act was invalid and could not be applied to land trust agreements that existed on or before the effective date of the Act. The court remanded the case to the trial court with orders to reinstate the beneficiaries' complaint.

Hayen v. County of Ogle

Supreme Court of Illinois


101 Ill. 2d 413; 463 N.E.2d 124; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 271; 78 Ill. Dec. 946; 27 Wage & Hour Cas. (BNA) 89; 114 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P56,203

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of the judgment of the Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois), which had entered a judgment in a wage dispute in favor of appellee union representatives.


OVERVIEW: The issue before the court concerned the Prevailing Wage Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, paras. 39s --1 to 39s --12 (1981). Union representatives had filed objections to the prevailing wage that was determined by the county. The union representative filed suit and argued that the county had failed to follow the Act because it included wages paid on private construction projects in its calculation of the prevailing wage rate. The lower courts upheld the constitutionality of the statute at issue. The union representatives contended that the county had no standing to contest the constitutionality of a state statute under the due process clause. The court did not address this issue because it was not raised below. Contractors had intervened in the action and argued that the Act was arbitrary and irrational. The court did not address the arguments raised by the contractors because it believed the issues raised should have been addressed by the legislature. The court affirmed and held that the Act did not violate the due process clause because it bore a rational relationship to a legitimate state interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court and held that the Prevailing Wage Act did not violate the due process clause.

People ex rel. Bernardi v. Roofing Systems, Inc.


No. 58096


Supreme Court of Illinois


101 Ill. 2d 424; 463 N.E.2d 123; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 272; 78 Ill. Dec. 945; 27 Wage & Hour Cas. (BNA) 95



April 19, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Ogle County, the Hon. John L. Moore, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the people ex relator, the Director of the Illinois Department of Labor (director), sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Ogle County (Illinois), which, sua sponte, declared that the Prevailing Wage Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, paras. 39s-1 to 39s-12 (1981), was unconstitutional for requiring public bodies to pay workers on construction projects more than they would without the Act. The complaint was dismissed.


OVERVIEW: The director filed a complaint against defendant employer to compel compliance with the Act. The director alleged that the employer was performing a public works construction project and that the employer was, therefore, required to pay the prevailing wage under the Act. The director sought a declaratory judgment, a permanent injunction, and access to the employer's wage and hour records. The director appealed after the circuit court decided that the Act was unconstitutional and dismissed the complaint, on the ground that the Act violated the Due Process and Equal Protection Clauses of the state and federal constitutions, Ill. Const. art. I, § 2; U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1. On appeal, the court reversed the dismissal of the action because the Act was previously found constitutional under the minimum-rationality standard of the Due Process and Equal Protection Clauses. The Act did not violate the Due Process Clause because the Act bore a rational relationship to a legitimate state interest. That interest was to assure that people working on public works projects received decent wages so that the work would be completed without interruptions or delay by workmen of average skill.


OUTCOME: The court agreed with the director and reversed the circuit court's conclusion that the Act was unconstitutional. The cause was remanded for further proceedings.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois), which affirmed his conviction of felony murder and armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a 13-year old boy, admitted to the stabbing murder of an employee at a local dry cleaner. In addition, the trial court's denial of defendant's challenges for cause was erroneous in that a prospective juror who was exposed to and remembered highly significant information, or other incriminating matters that were not admissible evidence, or inflammatory material was subject to challenge for cause and disqualification was automatic.


OUTCOME: The decision of the appellate court was affirmed as modified, and the judgment of the circuit court was reversed.

People v. Owens


No. 56453


Supreme Court of Illinois


102 Ill. 2d 88; 464 N.E.2d 261; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 285; 79 Ill. Dec. 663



April 4, 1984, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County, the Hon. Herman S. Haase, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois) that convicted him of murder and, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(d) (1979), sentenced him to death by electrocution. The appeal was authorized pursuant to Ill. Const. art. VI, § 4(b) (1979), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(i) (1979), and 87 Ill. 2d R. 603.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised numerous arguments on appeal including that he did not voluntarily waive his Fifth Amendment rights or his Sixth Amendment right to counsel and that admitting evidence of unrelated factors during the sentencing phase of the trial resulted in an arbitrary and capricious administration of the death penalty. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence. The court found that defendant was familiar enough with the Miranda warnings to understand what a waiver meant. Because he knew the severity of the charges against him charges and that the charges included murder, the court found that defendant voluntarily waived his right to counsel when he gave his statement without first asking for an attorney. The court found no error in admitting evidence that defendant had been convicted of a prior murder. The court held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(c) (1979) allowed the court to consider any aggravating and any mitigating factors relative to the imposition of the death penalty. The court reasoned that both the State and defendant were allowed considerable leeway to present evidence as long as it was reliable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence.

CASE SUMMARY:

Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 269 et seq. (1981), violated the Privileges and Immunities Clause of the United States Constitution and dismissed the department's action against appellees, village of Roanoke and the construction company, under the Act.


OVERVIEW: The village of Roanoke (village) entered into an agreement with the construction company to paint and repair the village's water tower. The department filed a complaint against appellees alleging violations of the Act. Appellees filed a motion to dismiss, arguing that the Act violated the Privileges and Immunities Clause of the United States Constitution. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court to dismiss the department's action against the village and the construction company under the Preference Act because the Preference Act.

 

261 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Matkovick


No. 58014


Supreme Court of Illinois


101 Ill. 2d 268; 461 N.E.2d 964; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 257; 78 Ill. Dec. 130



March 23, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. Bruce R. Fawell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which held that § 404(b) of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1404(b) (Supp. 1982), was unconstitutional and granted defendant's motion to dismiss the charge. Defendant filed a motion to strike certain portions of an appendix to the state's brief because it was not made part of the record in the circuit court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with unlawful distribution of a look-alike substance. The trial court granted his motion to dismiss on the ground that § 404(b) of the Act was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded for further proceedings. The court denied defendant's motion to strike a report from the state's brief because the report was a public record of which judicial notice could be taken. The court held that § 404(b) did not violate due process because it discouraged illicit traffic in narcotics and was reasonably related to the protection of the public health, safety, and welfare. Defendant did not succeed in demonstrating that § 404(b) was impermissibly vague in all of its applications. Because the statute did not involve First Amendment freedoms, the vagueness challenge had to be examined in light of the facts of defendant's case. The charge against defendant alleged conduct to which the statute clearly applied. Defendant lacked standing to attack the sentencing provisions of the Act because there had been no adjudication of guilt and no sentence imposed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion to strike challenged reports from the state's brief was denied. The court reversed the judgment dismissing the charge against defendant for unlawful distribution of a look-alike substance and remanded for proceedings consistent with its opinion.

 

262 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Roanoke Agency, Inc. v. Edgar


No. 58735


Supreme Court of Illinois


101 Ill. 2d 315; 461 N.E.2d 1365; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 263; 78 Ill. Dec. 258



March 23, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, Illinois corporation (corporation), delivered amendments to its articles of incorporation to appellant, the Secretary of State of Illinois (Secretary). The Secretary refused to approve and file the amendments. The corporation filed a writ of mandamus and the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) entered judgment for the corporation and ordered the Secretary to file the articles of amendment. The Secretary appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Secretary refused to approve and file the articles of amendment, contending that section 28(c) of the Business Corporation Act (statute), Ill. Rev. Stat. 1981, ch. 32, para. 157.28(c), which allowed permissive alternatives to voting rights was invalid as violative of applicable constitutional section in that it failed to preserve the traditional cumulative voting rules for Illinois corporations that were in existence before the effective date of the Illinois Constitution of 1970. The court held that the applicable constitutional section guaranteed to all shareholders of corporations in existence prior to July 1, 1971, the right to vote cumulatively for corporate directors, notwithstanding the acquisition dates of such shares. However, such rights were able to be waived upon the unanimous approval of all shareholders entitled to vote at an election of directors. Thus, the statute was constitutional in that the elimination or limitation of such voting rights was conditioned upon such unanimous approval. Because the corporation satisfied this unanimity requirement, the Secretary erroneously refused to approve and file the articles of amendment tendered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and ordered the Secretary to file the tendered articles of amendment upon payment of the appropriate filing fee as provided by law.

264 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Fitzsimmons v. Swailes


No. 57711


Supreme Court of Illinois


101 Ill. 2d 458; 463 N.E.2d 431; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 276; 79 Ill. Dec. 90



March 23, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 4, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. Bruce R. Fawell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State of Illinois sought the resignation of appellee county board member on the grounds that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 102, para. 4.11 (1982) (law) made it unlawful to simultaneously hold the position of county board member and township assessor in the board member's county. The Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) found that these positions were compatible and declared the law unconstitutional. The state sought review.


OVERVIEW: The state alleged that the trial court erred in holding that the offices of township assessor and county board member were compatible as a matter of common law and thereby also erred in holding that the law was unconstitutional. The court held that the common law rule of incompatibility focused on two offices held by the same person, where one of those offices was subordinate to the other in some important and principal duty and subject to the other's revisory power. The court found that a county board member had the authority to act on the appointment, salary, and budget of the supervisor of assessments. The court also found that county board members reviewed and were able to revise township assessments made by the township assessor. Because the township assessor's position was subordinate to the supervisor of assessments and because a county board member voted on who would be the supervisor of assessments, the court held that there was a possible conflict. Thus, the court reversed the lower court and held that the law was constitutional because the offices of township assessor and county board member were incompatible and the same person could not hold these positions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court judgment that the law was unconstitutional and remanded with instructions that the county board member be ousted from office.

People v. Silagy


No. 53776


Supreme Court of Illinois


101 Ill. 2d 147; 461 N.E.2d 415; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 250; 77 Ill. Dec. 792



February 22, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 30, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Vermilion County, the Hon. Paul M. Wright, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Vermilion County (Illinois), which convicted him of murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was convicted of capital murder, represented himself at the sentencing hearing and asked that the death penalty be imposed. The trial court appointed counsel to represent him on the direct appeal of the jury's death sentence. The court affirmed the conviction and, after considering the evidence, held that the death penalty was not unwarranted. Defendant's challenges to the constitutionality of the capital sentencing scheme were rejected, and it was held that the qualification of jurors did not result in a conviction-prone jury or deny defendant a jury from a fairly chosen cross section of the community. The evidence supported the jury's determination that the State had satisfied its burden of proving beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was sane when the offense was committed. The waiver of counsel at sentencing did not frustrate the policy of providing the sentencing body with all relevant mitigating evidence because the waiver was freely made and the jury was required to consider all mitigating evidence in the trial record.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment, including the sentence of death, and directed the clerk of the court to enter an order setting the date for execution of the sentence.

 

267 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Stewart


No. 54451


Supreme Court of Illinois


101 Ill. 2d 470; 463 N.E.2d 677; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 277; 79 Ill. Dec. 123



February 22, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 4, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Jack Arnold Welfeld, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) to the murders of two persons, the attempted murder of a third person, and the armed robbery of a jewelry store. When he was sentenced to death on the murder convictions, he filed a motion to withdraw his guilty plea, which was denied. Defendant then appealed, seeking a reversal of his conviction and a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty and then, after being sentenced to death, sought to withdraw his plea. The trial court denied the motion and defendant appealed. The court affirmed. It found that no constitutional violation resulted from the plea proceedings, which substantially complied with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 402. The court also held that defendant's conduct at the hearing demonstrated that he understood the charges against him as well as the consequences of a guilty plea and that his plea was knowing and voluntary. The court rejected claims that the trial court, where an "associate" judge was presiding, lacked jurisdiction, that the trial court abused its discretion in denying a defense motion for a mental examination, and that defendant was entitled to actually receive the presentence report prior to the convening of the sentencing hearing. The court also found that defendant failed to meet his burden to show that he was denied effective assistance of counsel and rejected a claim that the trial court erred in finding that there were no mitigating factors sufficient to preclude a death sentence. The court also rejected a frontal attack on the constitutionality of the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to withdraw his guilty plea, affirmed his conviction, and denied him a new trial.

People v. Albanese


No. 57069


Supreme Court of Illinois


102 Ill. 2d 54; 464 N.E.2d 206; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 284; 79 Ill. Dec. 608



February 22, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 4, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McLean County, the Hon. Henry L. Cowlin, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois) convicted defendant of the murder of his father and his wife's grandmother by arsenic poisoning. Defendant was also convicted of the attempted murder of his brother. Defendant was sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and attempted murder after it was shown that all three victims were poisoned, and it was clear that defendant had the motive and opportunity to poison each. Additional evidence supported defendant's conviction as well, including the fact that defendant had recently purchased large amounts of arsenic and the fact that defendant's financial turmoil provided defendant with a dire situation, which he apparently solved by killing those from whom he would inherit property in the case of death. On appeal from defendant's convictions and death sentence, the court found no merit to defendant's claims of trial court error. Testimony not offered for the truth of the matter asserted was properly admitted as non-hearsay, and an expert was properly allowed to testify regarding his interpretation of complex financial documents, which showed defendant's financial turmoil. The court also found that jury confusion over information contained in a jury handbook did not warrant a new trial, and the comments made by the prosecutor during closing were proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Crocker v. Finley


Nos. 58056, 58062, 58085 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


99 Ill. 2d 444; 459 N.E.2d 1346; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 232; 77 Ill. Dec. 97



February 1, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Joseph M. Wosik, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant clerk of court (clerk) and intervenors, state, women's group, and shelter group, appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied the clerk's motions to dismiss and for summary judgment. Instead, it granted plaintiff class's motion for summary judgment and ordered certain filing fees collected by the clerk, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 25, paras. 27.1(a)(3), 27.2(1)(d) (1981), to be refunded to class.


OVERVIEW: The dissolution litigant brought a class action against the clerk challenging the validity of a statute requiring the class to pay an additional filing fee to support a domestic violence fund and shelter. The circuit court granted the class's motion for summary judgment, ordered a trustee to prepare a plan to pay the refund to the class, and stayed judgment pending the clerk's appeal. The court affirmed the order because it found that: (1) a tax may be imposed on litigants when it is collected for court related purposes, (2) the fee was an improper tax on litigation because it bore no relationship to the services rendered and interfered unreasonably with access to the courts, (3) there was no significant relationship between the domestic violence services, (4) the legislature's choice to tax litigants was an arbitrary use of police power, and (5) there was no rational basis for imposing the tax only on dissolution litigants.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the class that the statute was an arbitrary use of police power and violated due process.

 

270 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Rolfingsmeyer


No. 58659


Supreme Court of Illinois


101 Ill. 2d 137; 461 N.E.2d 410; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 249; 77 Ill. Dec. 787



February 1, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 30, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Clinton County, the Hon. Arthur G. Henken, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Clinton County (Illinois), which found the implied consent statute of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11, §§ 501.1, 501.2(c) (1981), unconstitutional on defendant's motion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's refusal to submit to a breath test upon his arrest for driving under the influence of alcohol resulted in an automatic six-month suspension of his license. Defendant claimed that the implied consent statute was unconstitutional because it was contrary to the separation-of-powers provision of the state constitution and it violated an accused's constitutional privilege against self-incrimination. The court reversed and held that the statute was not violative of the separation-of-powers clause because it simply provided that an accused's refusal to submit to a breath test was admissible as evidence at his trial. The legislature had the power to prescribe methods of proof. The right to remain silent was not equivalent to the right to refuse a breath test, thus evidence of a refusal was not constitutionally protected.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that declared the implied consent statute unconstitutional and remanded the case.

People v. Eddmonds


No. 53669


Supreme Court of Illinois


101 Ill. 2d 44; 461 N.E.2d 347; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 243; 77 Ill. Dec. 724



January 20, 1984, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 30, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. John J. Crowley, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) which convicted him of murder and deviate sexual assault and sentenced him to death and 40 to 80 years' imprisonment respectively.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for sexually assaulting and smothering to death a nine-year-old boy. He was sentenced to death for the murder conviction and 40 to 80 years' imprisonment for the sexual assault conviction. On appeal, the court affirmed. The trial court did not err by proceeding to trial without conducting a fitness hearing because at the time of trial, the most recent psychiatric reports showed that defendant was fit for trial, defendant testified lucidly at his trial, and the only evidence of his unfitness was a report by one doctor who subsequently changed his opinion and another doctor's report made two years before trial. The trial court did not err by refusing to suppress statements defendant made to police because prior to the time he made the statements, the officers had probable cause to arrest defendant. Defendant was not under arrest because he voluntarily met with and accompanied the officers to the police station and therefore would have believed he was free to leave. The court overruled defendant's challenges to the death penalty's constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant of murder and deviate sexual assault and sentencing him for those crimes was affirmed.

 

273 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Cardunal Sav. & Loan Ass'n v. Kramer


No. 57740


Supreme Court of Illinois


99 Ill. 2d 334; 459 N.E.2d 929; 1984 Ill. LEXIS 221; 76 Ill. Dec. 794



January 20, 1984, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County, the Hon. John A. Krause, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, county sheriff and treasurer, sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) finding in favor of plaintiff bank and ruling that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 53, para. 37 (1979), which allowed payment of commissions to sheriffs out of revenue collected from the sale of foreclosed property, was unconstitutional. The bank cross-appealed the trial court's denial of certification of the action as a class action.


OVERVIEW: The bank filed suit against defendants, alleging that the sheriff collected illegal commissions from judicial sales of foreclosed property and paid them over to the county treasurer. The bank argued that the statute that authorized the collection of such commissions, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 53, para. 37 (1979), was unconstitutional because Ill. Const. of 1970, art. VII, § 9(a) prohibited the collection of such fees. The bank sought the enjoinment of the further collection of such fees and an accounting of such fees collected. The trial court ruled that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 53, para. 37 (1979) was unconstitutional and ordered the sheriff and the treasurer to account for all fees collected. The sheriff and the treasurer appealed, arguing that the action was an invalid collateral attack on valid court orders. The court modified the order, holding that the fact that a statute upon which an order was based was void did not deprive a court of jurisdiction. Judgments in a civil proceeding could only be collaterally attacked where there was a total want of jurisdiction. Thus, the sheriff and the treasurer were only required to account for fees received where a court had not approved the fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court. However, it modified the order of the trial court and ordered that the sheriff and the treasurer were only required to account for those funds received as fees on sales not thereafter approved by orders of the court. The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the bank's request for certification of the suit as a class action. The case was remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Frias


No. 57585


Supreme Court of Illinois


99 Ill. 2d 193; 457 N.E.2d 1233; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 513; 75 Ill. Dec. 674



December 16, 1983, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Robert L. Sklodowski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed a decision by the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which reversed the conviction entered against defendant for armed violence based on having committed murder while armed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant was charged with murder and armed violence based on having committed murder while armed. The trial court, upon a jury verdict, acquitted the defendant of murder but convicted him of the second offense. The appellate court reversed the conviction, finding that it was improper because the state failed to prove the predicate felony of murder, an essential element of the armed violence offense. The state appealed and the court affirmed, finding that the verdicts were not legally inconsistent. The court determined that under Ill. Const. art. VI, § 6 (1970) no appeal was permitted on the murder charge because defendant had already been acquitted thereon and it remained a final determination on that issue. The court concluded that collateral estoppel prevented the retrial on the armed violence charge alone because to retry defendant on that charge alone would unconstitutionally require him to relitigate the element of murder, an element on which defendant had already been acquitted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that reversed the conviction of defendant for armed violence based on having committed murder while armed.

People v. Mathey


Nos. 57731, 57765 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


99 Ill. 2d 292; 458 N.E.2d 499; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 523; 76 Ill. Dec. 99



December 16, 1983, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 27, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Roger L. Kiley, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from judgments of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found § 10 of the Cannabis Control Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 704(d) (1981), to be unconstitutional in two criminal cases in which defendants were charged with possession of marijuana.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that § 10 violated the assurances of due process and equal protection by precluding sentencing of defendants to "first offender" probation where defendants were convicted of possession of 30 to 500 grams of marijuana, despite the fact that defendants found guilty of possessing 200 grams or less of amphetamines, barbiturates, or peyote qualified for first offender probation. The trial court found that the classification of marijuana was arbitrary and irrational. Reversing, the court held that marijuana and the drugs barbiturates, amphetamines, and peyote were not similarly situated, and by placing marijuana in a separate statute, the legislature identified it as constituting a particular social concern. The court found that the classifications were not irrational or contrary to legislative purpose.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's judgments.

Malone v. Cosentino


No. 57492


Supreme Court of Illinois


99 Ill. 2d 29; 457 N.E.2d 395; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 495; 75 Ill. Dec. 401



December 1, 1983, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Anthony J. Scotillo, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city, and state and county officials, appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted plaintiff individual's motion for judgment on the pleadings and held that the fee and penalty assessment statutes, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-9-1 (1981) and Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 34, para. 429.27 (1981), were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff individual, who had pleaded guilty to two traffic violations, filed a class action against defendants, city, and state and county officials, alleging that the fees and penalties assessed against him pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-9-1 (1981) and Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 34, para. 429.27 (1981) were unconstitutional. After allowing the circuit court's judgment to become final, plaintiff was barred from raising the constitutional issue in an ad hoc collateral proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment granting plaintiff individual's motion for judgment on the pleadings and denying the motion by defendants, city, and state and county officials, to dismiss the complaint, holding that the civil class action was an impermissible collateral attack on the criminal conviction, and plaintiff was thus barred from raising the constitutionality of the fee and penalty assessment statutes in an ad hoc collateral proceeding.

George D. Hardin, Inc. v. Mt. Prospect


No. 57968


Supreme Court of Illinois


99 Ill. 2d 96; 457 N.E.2d 429; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 505; 75 Ill. Dec. 435



December 1, 1983, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Albert Green, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff special-assessment bondholders instituted an action seeking a declaration of an express trust and an accounting from defendant village for certain special assessments. The village sought to dismiss, citing § 1, 1.1 of "An Act in relation to delinquent taxes and special assessments" (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 891.1 (1981). The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) found the Act unconstitutional and the village appealed.


OVERVIEW: The bondholders alleged that the funds collected had been commingled or improperly transferred and that the village had not paid to them all of the sums that it had collected. The village countered by citing the Act, which permitted the cancellation of certain bonds that had been delinquent for over 30 years. The trial court found § 1, 1.1 of the Act were unconstitutional impairments of contractual obligations in violation of the federal and state constitutions. On the village's appeal, the court affirmed. The court first held that, in applying the doctrine of severability, the bond-cancellation provisions of the Act could not stand alone. The challenged sections of the Act did not become part of the bondholders' contracts because only statutes in force at the time a contract was made were incorporated therein. The justifications offered by the village, simplifying municipal record keeping and eliminating the possibility of stale claims, were simply insufficient bases for upholding a statute which, without notice of any type, permitted cancellation of valid bonds and conversion of undisbursed funds in violation of the federal and Illinois constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which had found certain sections of the Act unconstitutional in the bondholders' action against the village for a declaration of an express trust and for an accounting.

Sayles v. Thompson


No. 59032


Supreme Court of Illinois


99 Ill. 2d 122; 457 N.E.2d 440; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 508; 75 Ill. Dec. 446



December 1, 1983, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. James H. Felt, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, governor and corrections director, sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiff inmates who alleged that transfers of prisoners to out-of-state prisons under the Interstate Corrections Compact (compact), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1003-4-4 (1981), violated the transportation clause in Ill. Const. art. I, sec. 11 (1970) (transportation clause).


OVERVIEW: The inmates brought a class action against the governor and director on behalf of all Illinois prisoners subject to the compact. The inmates sought a declaration that transfers of inmates to out-of-state prisons under the compact violated the transportation clause. The inmates also sought an injunction prohibiting enforcement of the compact. The circuit court denied the governor and director's motion to dismiss the complaint and entered an order granting summary judgment in favor of the inmates. On appeal, the court reversed the order. The court held that: (1) the transportation clause was violated only if and when the transportation of prisoners constituted cruel and unusual punishment; (2) the objective of the compact was to serve the best interests of the inmatesby alleviating security and health problems associated with overcrowding in Illinois prisons; (3) although out-of-state transfers involved certain hardships to the inmates and made visitation more burdensome, such transfers were neither unusual nor cruel in the constitutional sense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting summary judgment in favor of the inmates who alleged that transfers of prisoners to out-of-state prisons under the compact violated the transportation clause.

People v. Ramirez


No. 52354


Supreme Court of Illinois


98 Ill. 2d 439; 457 N.E.2d 31; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 486; 75 Ill. Dec. 241



November 10, 1983, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Louis B. Garippo, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which sentenced defendant to the death penalty after he was convicted of attempted armed robbery and murder. Defendant contended that the lower court committed reversible error during the sentencing hearing and that the death penalty statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for attempted armed robbery and murder, but vacated the death sentence due to the cumulative impact of the errors in the sentencing hearing. Defendant's Fifth Amendment right to remain silent was violated because the judge refused to instruct the jury that it should not consider defendant's silence as evidence of his guilt. In addition, the prosecutor's statements concerning defendant's silence were highly prejudicial. The prosecutor improperly called the deceased's widow to the stand because she had no evidence of probative value concerning sentencing. Instead, she was used to elicit sympathy from the jury. The prosecutor prejudiced defendant in his closing argument by repeatedly referring to the deceased as a police officer because the deceased's status was not a factor to be taken into account for deciding whether to impose the death penalty. The court affirmed the admission of defendant's other crimes and his trial testimony at the sentencing hearing. The court did not address defendant's argument that the death penalty statute was unconstitutional because it reversed his sentence on other grounds. The court remanded for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction but vacated the death penalty sentence. The court remanded for resentencing.

Miller v. Lockett


No. 57318


Supreme Court of Illinois


98 Ill. 2d 478; 457 N.E.2d 14; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 487; 75 Ill. Dec. 224; 41 A.L.R.4th 1017



October 21, 1983, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Thomas J. O'Brien, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured persons challenged the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed their complaint for personal injuries against defendant trucking company with prejudice on the ground that the Illinois Limitations Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 83, paras. 1-12a and 13-27, made applicable a time limitation for suits contained in the Tennessee statute of limitations, which barred the action.


OVERVIEW: The injured persons filed their action for personal injuries after they returned to Illinois after being involved in an automobile accident with a vehicle driven by the trucking company's employee in Tennessee. The injured persons were Illinois residents and the trucking company was an Oklahoma corporation registered to do business in Illinois. There was no service on the driver of the trucking company's vehicle who was not an Illinois resident. After their action was dismissed, the injured persons appealed directly pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 302(a)(1), 73 Ill. R. 302(a)(1). The court held that the "borrowing provisions" of the Illinois Limitations Act did not contain a prohibited discrimination. The court determined that the apparent and legitimate purpose underlying the residential provision was to deter forum shopping by nonresidents. The court ruled that the legislature's decision to apply Illinois' limitations standards to actions involving Illinois residents, while applying the statute of limitations of the locus in actions involving nonresidents, was not an irrational exercise of power.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court that dismissed with prejudice the injured persons' action for personal injuries against the trucking company, and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

McKenzie v. Johnson


Nos. 56867, 56878 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


98 Ill. 2d 87; 456 N.E.2d 73; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 458; 74 Ill. Dec. 571



October 21, 1983, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County, the Hon. George S. Miller, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property taxpayer sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) which granted summary judgment for defendants, Director of Revenue and county board of review, upholding the constitutionality of the property tax exemptions for parsonages and fraternity and sorority houses. Defendants appealed the grant of summary judgment for plaintiff, holding the homestead-improvement exemptions unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff property taxpayer filed an action against defendants, Director of Revenue and county board of review, challenging the constitutionality of the property tax exemptions for parsonages, fraternity and sorority houses, and homestead improvements. Plaintiff alleged that the statutes authorizing the fraternity, parsonage, and homestead-improvement exemptions, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, paras. 500.1, 500.2. 500,23-2, 500.23-3 (1981) violated the provisions of Ill. Const. art. IX, §§ 4(a), 6. The trial court granted the parties' motions for summary judgment, holding that the homestead-improvement exemptions were not constitutional while the parsonage and fraternity exemptions were. The court, however, reversed the trial court's judgment that the homestead-improvement exemption was unconstitutional because the homestead improvement exemptions were permissible "homestead exemptions."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment for defendants, Director of Revenue and county review board, that property tax exemptions for parsonages and fraternity and sorority houses were within the scope of the constitutional exclusive-use requirement if used primarily for exempted purposes. The court reversed the summary judgment for plaintiff property taxpayer, finding that the homestead improvement exemption was permitted.

People v. Caffrey


No. 56901


Supreme Court of Illinois


97 Ill. 2d 526; 455 N.E.2d 60; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 445; 74 Ill. Dec. 30



October 4, 1983, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Lawrence I. Genesen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed a charge against defendant for syndicated gambling under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 28-1.1 (1981).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested and charged with syndicated gambling after he was accused of accepting numerous bets on the results of football and basketball games. The circuit court granted defendant's motion to dismiss on the grounds that the syndicated-gambling statute was unconstitutionally vague. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court found that it was possible to conjure up situations so remote and unique as to render nearly every statute violative of constitutional protections, but that was not a valid reason to end the criminal prosecution of a defendant whose conduct clearly fell within the bounds set by § 28-1.1. Defendant maintained that time limits were essential to prevent the aggregation of small bets over a lifetime to produce a felony. However, the fact that were borderline cases with a degree of uncertainty did not render the statute unconstitutional as to conduct about which no uncertainty existed.


OUTCOME: A judgment of the lower court dismissing charges against defendant for syndicated gambling was reversed and remanded.

People v. Rink


No. 57134


Supreme Court of Illinois


97 Ill. 2d 533; 455 N.E.2d 64; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 446; 74 Ill. Dec. 34



October 4, 1983, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. Bruce Fawell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which held § 104-28(a) of an act to add §§ 104-10 through 104-29 to the Code of Criminal Procedure of 1963 (act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 104-28(a) (1980 Supp.) to be unconstitutional. The section held to be invalid established procedures whereby defendant had been found to be unfit to stand trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for the murder of his father and for aggravated battery upon his mother. A mental health report was prepared on defendant, and it stated that defendant had been at a mental health center for the past nine years. Acting on requests by defendant and the state, a discharge hearing was held. The lower court found that the state had proved that defendant was sane at the time and was guilty of murder beyond a reasonable doubt. It also found that defendant was in need of treatment. Defendant's motion that his sentence for treatment be reconsidered was denied, and § 104-28(a) was held unconstitutional. The state argued that the section was unconstitutional because it was a legislative grant of amnesty that encroached upon the executive branch's power to pardon. The court did not perceive how the statute would be any more vulnerable than a statute of limitations or a speedy-trial statute. Therefore, the lower court erred in holding the provision to be unconstitutional. The evidence was overwhelming that defendant committed the crimes. As to sanity, there was competent, expert testimony that defendant could not have been considered insane on the night of the killing.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court was reversed and remanded, and the lower court was directed, on remand, to vacate the order for extended treatment and conduct further proceedings.

People v. Ziltz


No. 57428


Supreme Court of Illinois


98 Ill. 2d 38; 455 N.E.2d 70; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 453; 74 Ill. Dec. 40

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. Patrick M. Coolahan, Judge, presiding.

Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501(a)(1) (1981) because the statute violated due process.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested and charged with operating a motor vehicle with a blood alcohol concentration in excess of ten percent in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501(a)(1) (1981) and with driving under the influence of alcohol in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501(a)(2) (1981). When the lower court granted defendant's motion to dismiss the first count, the prosecution appealed. The court found that (1) defendant had standing to challenge the constitutionality of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501(a)(1) (1981), (2) the issue was ripe for judicial determination where defendant would suffer harm if convicted of the criminal offense with which he had been charged, (3) the statute did not create a due process violation because the legislature had permissibly determined that the ten percent blood alcohol concentration constituted impairment, and (4) because the statute did not impermissibly shift the burden of proof, the court reversed the lower court's judgment and remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment, held the statute in question constitutional, and remanded the case for further proceedings consistent with the judgment.

People v. Gurell


No. 56904


Supreme Court of Illinois


98 Ill. 2d 194; 456 N.E.2d 18; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 467; 74 Ill. Dec. 516



October 4, 1983, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 2, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Kenneth J. Cohen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state initiated criminal prosecution under the Nursing Home Care Reform Act of 1979 (act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para. 4151-101 et seq. (1979), against appellee nursing home operators. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) held that the act and regulations thereunder were unconstitutional. The state and the nursing home operators appealed.


OVERVIEW: The nursing home operators where charged with misdemeanor violations of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para. 4153-318 (1979), after they had failed to correct certain violations under the act. The trial court concluded that the act was unconstitutional. On appeal the court held that: (1) the right to carry on one's business was not a fundamental right and the act was constitutional if it had a rational relationship to a legitimate state purpose, (2) there was a rational basis for nursing home regulation, (3) the act was not special legislation and was not void for vagueness or because it constituted an unlawful delegation of authority, (4) the act was not a bill of attainder because the crimes charged were for failure to correct an administrative offense, (5) the act and regulations were not violative of due process because they permissibly regulated but had not prohibited the nursing operators business.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court to the extent that it held that portions of the nursing home regulatory statute were unconstitutional. The court affirmed that portion of the order of the trial court that upheld parts of the nursing home regulation statute and parts of the rules and regulations. The cause was remanded to trial court.

 

287 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Yarger v. Board of Regents


No. 57688


Supreme Court of Illinois


98 Ill. 2d 259; 456 N.E.2d 39; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 472; 74 Ill. Dec. 537



October 4, 1983, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 2, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County, the Hon. Simon L. Friedman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff booksellers appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois) that granted defendant board of regents' (board) motion to dismiss the booksellers' complaint to enjoin the board from leasing out university space for use as a bookstore. In granting the motion to dismiss, the trial court held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 144, para. 251 (1981) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The booksellers filed a complaint that sought an injunction against the board to prevent it from leasing out space on a university campus to a retail bookstore. The complaint alleged that the lease was illegal under § 251. The trial court granted the board's motion to dismiss and held that § 251 was unconstitutional. The booksellers appealed, and the court affirmed. To determine whether § 251 was properly enacted, the court applied the journal-entry rule, which presumed that a statute signed by the presiding officers of each branch of the general assembly and approved by the governor was enacted in accordance with constitutional requirements. The presumption afforded by the journal-entry rule could be overcome by clear and convincing proof that the constitutional procedure was not followed. Here, the journals did not show compliance with the constitutionally mandated procedure for enactment. Rather, they presented clear and convincing evidence that the bill that was passed by both houses was not the bill that the governor approved.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment granting the board's motion to dismiss the booksellers' complaint that sought an injunction against the leasing of university space for use as a bookstore.

 

288 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Fagiano v. Police Bd. of Chicago


Nos. 57313, 57315


Supreme Court of Illinois


98 Ill. 2d 277; 456 N.E.2d 27; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 474; 74 Ill. Dec. 525



October 4, 1983, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 2, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeals from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, various boards and departments of the City of Chicago, Ill., appealed two judgments of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which affirmed the circuit court's decisions that Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code ch. 25, § 30 was unconstitutionally vague and that Chicago, Ill., Police Dep't. R. 25 was invalid. The ordinance and the rule set forth residency requirements for municipal employees. The court consolidated the appeals.


OVERVIEW: In the first case, the personnel board ordered the discharge of plaintiffs, two firefighters and a water department engineer, for violating the ordinance, which required civil service employees to be "actual residents" of the City. In the second case, plaintiff police officer was discharged for violations of the rule, which was based on the ordinance. The rule required the police officer "to actually reside" within the City limits. The appellate court reversed both decisions because it found the ordinance to be unconstitutional. Upon consolidated appeal by defendants, the court reversed and held that the appellate court erred in holding that that the word "residence" was too vague to guide agencies. The court held that the word "residence" was intended to be synonymous with "domicile." The enactments required the employees to establish their principal residence, that is, their domicile, in the City. Accordingly, the rule and the ordinance were not constitutionally infirm for not setting out strict guidelines to follow in determining residence. While there may have been "merely erroneous action," the court found no evidence of intentional discrimination by the personnel board.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgments. It remanded the causes to the appellate court for consideration of the question of the sufficiency of the evidence because the appellate court, having found the rule and the ordinance to be unconstitutional, did not reach the other objections of plaintiffs to their discharges. The court did not decide whether the denial of attorney fees to one firefighter was proper as the constitutional holdings were in error.

First Nat'l Bank v. Kusper


No. 57171


Supreme Court of Illinois


98 Ill. 2d 226; 456 N.E.2d 7; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 469; 74 Ill. Dec. 505



September 23, 1983, Filed

The trustee sought to redeem the property by tendering the amount of the bid on the property at the sale, plus interest and costs. The clerk refused the tendered amount, based on an amendment to the statutory and constitutional provisions in effect at the time of the sale. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 747 (1981).


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated and the case dismissed for mootness. The court did not determine the correctness of the lower court judgment or express an opinion on it.

People v. Kaeding


No. 57288


Supreme Court of Illinois


98 Ill. 2d 237; 456 N.E.2d 11; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 470; 74 Ill. Dec. 509



September 23, 1983, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 2, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. Carl Henniger, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which sentenced defendant to nine years imprisonment for taking indecent liberties with a child, ordered the state to provide the defendant with psychotherapy, required the state to file a treatment plan with the trial court within 60 days, and held that a portion of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-2-6 (1981) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The trial court sentenced defendant to nine years imprisonment for taking indecent liberties with a child, ordered the state to provide the defendant with psychotherapy, and required the state to file a treatment plan with the trial court within 60 days. The trial court held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-2-6 (1981) was unconstitutional because it discriminated between the treatment of incarcerated and nonincarcerated defendants by requiring a course of mental treatment for incarcerated defendants. The state appealed. On appeal, the court reversed, remanded, and held that para. 1005-2-6 (1981) did not deprive individuals of equal protection of the laws. The difference in the way incarcerated and nonincarcerated defendants were treated was only in the entity which was empowered to make the determination as to what course of medical treatment would have been appropriate. By vesting the Illinois Department of Corrections with the power to determine the defendant's needs and to implement treatment, the statute reflected the well-established view that the judiciary was ill equipped to supervise and evaluate the treatment of incarcerated defendants.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which sentenced the defendant and held a sentencing statute to be unconstitutional, and remanded the case for resentencing of the defendant.

Lane v. Sklodowski


No. 58601


Supreme Court of Illinois


97 Ill. 2d 311; 454 N.E.2d 322; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 426; 73 Ill. Dec. 462


July 12 and July 15, 1983, Argued and Announced  
August 29, 1983, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original action for mandamus, prohibition, or supervisory order.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff director of corrections sought a writ of mandamus and prohibition or a supervisory order directing defendant judges to dismiss numerous proceedings that had been initiated against him by several state attorneys in connection with his actions in releasing prisoners for good time served under § 3--6--3(a)(3) of the Unified Code of Corrections, codified at Ill. OVERVIEW: The proceedings brought against the director sought a rule to show cause why he should not have been held in contempt regarding his application of the statute in question. In re Application of Rosewell


No. 55907


Supreme Court of Illinois


97 Ill. 2d 434; 454 N.E.2d 997; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 441; 73 Ill. Dec. 748



July 6, 1983, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 30, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Joseph Schneider, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tax collector sought review of the judgment of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which on appeal by certain owners of real property with delinquent taxes reversed the trial court's order removing some real estate parcels from its judgment of sale. The appellate court held the Illinois Scavenger Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 716a (1979), required sale of property with delinquent taxes.


OVERVIEW: The tax collector filed an application for judgment and order of sale under the Act that included all parcels in the county for which real estate taxes remained unpaid for at least five years. The tax collector moved the court to amend its judgment to exclude from it the parcels whose owners were named in civil tax collection suits. The trial court granted the motion and some of the owners of the real property with delinquent taxes objected. The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment, and held that the language in the Act required the sale for all properties that had unpaid taxes for at least five years. The court reversed the appellate court judgment, and affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court ruled that, consistent with the terms of the Act and its legislative intent, the circuit court had discretionary authority to withhold parcels from the delinquent property sale. The court found that the trial court was not required to enter judgment and an order of sale regardless of circumstances or regardless of whether the public interest would be served.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court and affirmed the order of the trial court that removed certain tax-delinquent parcels from a judgement and order of sale that had been applied for by the tax collector under the Act. The court found that the trial court was vested with discretionary authority to withhold property from a delinquent property tax sale under the terms of the Act and its legislative intent.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which imposed the death penalty following his conviction of murder, attempted murder, armed violence, armed robbery, aggravated battery, rape, aggravated kidnapping, deviate sexual assault, taking indecent liberties with a child, and conspiracy.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he was denied a fair hearing on the motion to suppress the identification testimony. People v. Davis

Supreme Court of Illinois


97 Ill. 2d 1; 452 N.E.2d 525; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 408; 72 Ill. Dec. 272



June 17, 1983, Filed

OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant contended that he was deprived of his right to a speedy trial, that he was denied effective assistance of counsel, that the State failed to establish that defendant voluntarily made certain statements indicating his complicity in a number of murders and other offenses, that he was denied his Sixth Amendment right to confrontation by the admission into evidence of his co-defendant's statement, that the death penalty statute was unconstitutional, that the death sentence could not be imposed where the murder conviction was premised upon a theory of accountability, and that the jury was improperly informed at the sentencing hearing that he had previously received the death penalty for an unrelated murder. People v. Holder


No. 56383


Supreme Court of Illinois


96 Ill. 2d 444; 451 N.E.2d 831; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 398; 71 Ill. Dec. 677; 100 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P55,449



June 9, 1983, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County, the Hon. Robert C. Gill, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois) reversed defendant's trial court conviction on charges of intimidation in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12 -- 6 (a)(3) (1979) after finding that statute (the intimidation statute) unconstitutionally overbroad. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a union representative contacted by certain employees who hoped to obtain union representation. Defendant obtained the employees' consent and then went to the employer's office and threatened to shut down the employer's operation through strike unless the union representation was recognized. On that basis, defendant was charged and convicted under the intimidation statute and, on appeal to the Second District, the conviction was reversed and the intimidation statute was found overly broad and unconstitutional. On appeal from that ruling, the court reversed and found the intimidation statute was broad, but was not so broad so as to be deemed unconstitutional. Defendant claimed that the statute was overbroad because it made it a criminal violation to engage in uninhibited discussion and effectively prohibited speech that was clearly protected by the First Amendment. The court found, to the contrary, that while under the intimidation statute one could be prosecuted for threatening to picket in front of a city hall without a permit, any such conceivable impermissible applications were dwarfed by the statute's legitimate reach in prohibiting threatened criminal activity.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the Second District ruling after finding the intimidation statute constitutional and remanded the action for further proceedings.

Carbondale v. Yehling


No. 56984


Supreme Court of Illinois


96 Ill. 2d 495; 451 N.E.2d 837; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 404; 71 Ill. Dec. 683



June 9, 1983, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County, the Hon. Richard E. Richman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city filed several petitions for condemnation based on its eminent domain power. Appellee landowners filed motions to dismiss the petitions. The Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois) granted the motions to dismiss and the city appealed the order.


OVERVIEW: The city passed ordinances for the purpose of urban redevelopment of the city's business district and sought to accomplish redevelopment by exercising the power of eminent domain. The landowners argued that the ordinances were void because they constituted an improper use of home rule authority, were not authorized by state law, and were unconstitutional under both the United States and Illinois constitutions. The ordinances sought to define the notice procedures of the courts, duties of parties in court, and specific remedies available in court proceedings. The court held that the city was attempting to set forth rules for the state judiciary to follow and that was a matter of state concern, not a local function that pertained to the home rule unit's government and affairs. The court held that the ordinances did not pertain to the government and affairs of the city and were not local in character. The court held that although the city's purpose in enacting the ordinances pertained to local government and affairs, the method of enforcement prescribed to carry out the eminent domain proceedings was impermissible.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that dismissed the city's petitions for condemnation.

 

297 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Greene


No. 56830


Supreme Court of Illinois


96 Ill. 2d 334; 450 N.E.2d 329; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 385; 70 Ill. Dec. 856



May 27, 1983, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Ogle County, the Hon. John L. Moore, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Ogle County (Illinois), which held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 24-1(a)(7) (1979) was unconstitutional in a prosecution against defendant for the unlawful use of weapons in violation of that section.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a consent search, police found a homemade bomb in defendant's home and charged defendant with unlawful use of weapons in violation of para. 24-1(a)(7). The trial court held that para. 24-1(a)(7) was unconstitutional because of the disparity in punishment for a violation of that statute as compared to para. 24-1(a)(3), which prohibited similar conduct. The State sought review, and the court noted that while para. 24-1(a)(7) clearly referred to explosive devices, para. 24-1(a)(3) referred to any device, including a bomb, containing noxious liquid gas. The court concluded that the legislature intended to differentiate between explosives and other devices and that there was a sufficient difference between the devices to justify the difference in penalties without violating defendant's due process rights. The court noted that the disparate treatment was reasonable because of the greater capacity for injury from an explosive than from tear gas. The court finally noted that the fact that para. 24-1(a)(7) could have been held unconstitutionally vague in other cases did not affect its validity with respect to defendant's conduct, which was clearly proscribed by the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter for further proceedings.
