People v. Williams


No. 53240


Supreme Court of Illinois


97 Ill. 2d 252; 454 N.E.2d 220; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 425; 73 Ill. Dec. 360



May 27, 1983, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 30, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. James Strunck, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) to charges of murder, armed robbery, rape, and aggravated kidnapping. After a bifurcated sentencing proceeding defendant was sentenced to death for murder. The circuit court denied a motion by defendant to vacate the pleas, and defendant took a direct appeal under Ill. Const. 1970, art. VI, § 4(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with kidnapping, murder, and rape, and entered a plea of guilty after pretrial motions were denied. In a direct appeal, the Illinois Supreme Court affirmed the conviction and sentence, holding that the death penalty statute was constitutional, and that the procedures for selecting the jury did not violate due process nor result in a jury which was not impartial or a fair representation of the community. It was proper to deny the right to call witnesses to challenge the propriety or effectiveness of the death penalty in general. It was not improper for a defendant's attorney to testify as to defendant's demeanor, as demeanor was not a confidential communication. Communications to a probation officer preparing a pre-sentence report for the judge were not privileged. Defendant had no right to make a statement on his behalf to a jury considering the imposition of the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and death sentence, and fixed a date for defendant's execution.

Board of Comm'rs v. County of Du Page


No. 57184


Supreme Court of Illinois


96 Ill. 2d 378; 450 N.E.2d 332; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 391; 70 Ill. Dec. 859



May 27, 1983, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. John Teschner, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county appealed a decision by the Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois), which reversed a circuit court decision dismissing plaintiff city library district's action for a declaratory judgment that § 2 of the Illinois Investment of Public Funds Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para. 902 (1981), controlled the question of entitlement to interest earned on investments of tax funds collected by the county and undistributed.


OVERVIEW: The library district brought an action against the county for a declaration that § 2 of the Illinois Investment of Public Funds Act (Investment of Public Funds Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para. 902 (1981), rather than § 6.1 of the Illinois County Treasurers' Act (County Treasurer's Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 36, para. 22.1 (1981), controlled the question of which public entity was entitled to the interest earned on invested tax funds collected by, but undistributed by, the county. The court affirmed a decision reversing the dismissal of the action, remanded the case for further proceedings, and found that Ill. Const. art. VII, § 9(a) (1970) prohibited the county treasurer from retaining interest earned on the investment of monies collected for other taxing districts because it would have resulted in the charging of fees for the collection of the taxes. As a result, adopting the county's argument that § 6.1 of the County Treasurers' Act included the interest earned on funds owned by other units of local government would have rendered the County Treasurers' Act unconstitutional. Section 2 of the Investment of Public Funds Act controlled the entitlement to the investment proceeds.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and remanded for further proceedings a decision reversing an order dismissing the library district's action for a declaration that the Illinois Investment of Public Funds Act controlled the determination of which entity was entitled to interest on invested tax funds that the county had collected, but had not distributed.

 

300 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Brownell


No. 55192


Supreme Court of Illinois


96 Ill. 2d 167; 449 N.E.2d 1318; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 366; 70 Ill. Dec. 714



May 18, 1983, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Boone County, the Hon. Robert C. Gill, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Sentence vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the death sentence imposed by the Circuit Court of Boone County (Illinois) in connection with defendant's convictions for murder, aggravated kidnapping, and rape.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder, aggravated kidnapping, and rape and sentenced to death. Upon defendant's initial appeal, the death sentence was vacated because the court found that one of the aggravating factors did not exist. At resentencing, defendant asked the trial court to preclude a capital sentencing hearing based upon a promise of the prosecutor not to ask for the death penalty. The trial court denied the motion and defendant was again sentenced to death. Defendant appealed, and the court reversed, finding initially that the issue of whether the prosecutor was precluded from asking for the death penalty was not waived. Although the issue was not raised in the first direct appeal, the trial court did consider the issue on remand; thus, it was properly before the court on appeal. The court found that when defendant was arrested the state's attorney told defendant's counsel that he would not seek the death penalty if defendant confessed to the murder. Defendant confessed early the next morning without the offer having been revoked. The state offered no justification for not abiding by the promise. Due process required that the state's attorney be bound by his promise.


OUTCOME: The death sentence imposed on defendant for his convictions for murder, aggravated kidnapping, and rape was vacated. The cause was remanded for resentencing with directions that the death penalty was not to be considered.

Harris Trust & Sav. Bank v. Duggan

302 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Warrior v. Thompson


No. 57897


Supreme Court of Illinois


96 Ill. 2d 1; 449 N.E.2d 53; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 352; 70 Ill. Dec. 179



March 14, 1983, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 27, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Albert S. Porter, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, Governor of Illinois and related government agencies, appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted injunctive relief to plaintiff aid recipients and intervenors, hospitals and hospital association, in plaintiffs' action alleging that defendants illegally eliminated a public medical aid program and limited the amount of benefits paid to health care facilities on behalf of the program's recipients.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to provisions of the Emergency Budget Act, Pub. Act 82, 1038 S.B. 1652, defendants suspended the operation of programs to aid the medically indigent and limited the amounts paid to providers for in-patient hospital treatment. The trial court granted plaintiffs' request for a preliminary injunction prohibiting defendants from going forward on the plan. On appeal pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 302(b), the court reversed and remanded with directions to dismiss plaintiffs' complaints, holding that the emergency rules promulgated by defendants were in compliance with the Illinois Administrative Procedure Act. Defendants acted within the scope of their statutorily conveyed discretionary and intervenors failed to show that a preliminary injunction was necessary in order to prevent irreparable harm. Defendants did not exceed their powers in determining that, during the specified period, no portion of the appropriated funds would be paid for aid to the medically indigent. There was no constitutional defect in the program and plaintiffs were not denied the equal protection of the laws.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court in favor of plaintiffs and intervenors, and remanded with instructions to dismiss the complaint.

People v. Wisslead


No. 55818


Supreme Court of Illinois


94 Ill. 2d 190; 446 N.E.2d 512; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 293; 68 Ill. Dec. 606



February 18, 1983, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of McDonough County, the Hon. U.S. Collins, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of McDonough County (Illinois), which dismissed the charge of armed violence against defendant and held the Illinois armed-violence statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33A-2 (1979) unconstitutional as applied to the Illinois unlawful-restraint statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 10-3(a) (1979), in the state's prosecution of the defendant for violations of those two statutes.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with commission of the offenses of unlawful restraint and armed violence, based on the underlying felony of unlawful restraint. The state's criminal information alleged that defendant, while armed with a revolver, detained his estranged wife without legal authority. The trial court dismissed the charge of armed violence and held that the Illinois armed-violence statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33A-2 (1979), was unconstitutional as applied to the Illinois unlawful-restraint statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 10-3(a) (1979). The state appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the sentences which were available for the offense of armed violence based on unlawful restraint with a Category I weapon and for the more serious offense of aggravated kidnapping were unconstitutionally disproportionate. The sentencing scheme violated the constitutional assurances of proportionate penalties and due process because the penalty for forcible detention was less than that for armed violence based on unlawful restraint although unlawful restraint was a lesser included offense of forcible detention.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the charge of armed violence against defendant in the state's prosecution of the defendant for committing armed violence and unlawful restraint.

 

304 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Manuel


Nos. 56482, 56662, 56663 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


94 Ill. 2d 242; 446 N.E.2d 240; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 297; 68 Ill. Dec. 506



February 18, 1983, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Circuit Court of Jackson County, the Hon. Richard E. Richman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated action, the State appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois) that granted defendants' motion to dismiss drug charges against them, holding that § 404 of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1404 (1979), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The trial court ordered that the drug charges brought against three defendants pursuant to § 404 of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act be dismissed. The State appealed, and the court affirmed the decision. It agreed that because § 404 punished delivery of a non-controlled substance more severely than delivery of a controlled substance, it was not reasonably designed to remedy the evil that the legislature determined to be a greater threat to the public. As such, § 404 constituted a violation of the due process clause of the Illinois Constitution. Furthermore, at the time of these offenses, § 404 had not yet been amended; therefore, prosecution of the three defendants was precluded. Finally, the court held that to the extent People v. Johnson, 106 Ill. App. 3d 759 (1982), was inconsistent, it was expressly disapproved.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision was affirmed.

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with murder, and the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois) convicted him and sentenced him to death. Defendant's post-trial motions were denied, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed, among other things, that the State's use of peremptory challenges denied his right to a fair and impartial trial, that he was denied a speedy trial, that his Fourth Amendment rights were violated, that the indictment was insufficient to support the death sentence, that there was insufficient proof of aggravating factors, and that he was denied a fair sentencing hearing. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 103 -- 5(f) (1977) had not run.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Celotex Corp. v. Pollution Control Bd.


No. 55848


Supreme Court of Illinois


94 Ill. 2d 107; 445 N.E.2d 752; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 286; 68 Ill. Dec. 108; 20 ERC (BNA) 1137; 13 ELR 20586



February 4, 1983, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on a petition for review of an order of the Pollution Control Board.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Pollution Control Board (board) challenged an order of the Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois), which declared that Ill. P.C.B. Rules & Regs. ch. 2, R. 202 was invalid and reversed the board's decision to deny plaintiff corporation's application to renew its operating permit because it failed to comply with the rule promulgated under the Illinois Environmental Protection Act (Act).


OVERVIEW: The agency denied the corporation's application for a renewal of its operating license because to failed to comply with Rule 202 requiring the production of certain information. The board affirmed the decision and the appellate court reversed the board, declaring Rule 202 invalid. The board sought review. The court affirmed the appellate court and remanded the case to the board to determine the corporation's compliance with other valid rules. The court found that § 29 of the Act provided an additional method to challenge the board's regulations and was not an exclusive procedure and the corporation's previous compliance with rule 202 did not estop it from challenging its validity because any acceptance of the rule's validity was involuntary. The court determined that the relationship between rules 202 and 103(g)(1) was close and substantial and required the invalidation of rule 202 because the board made no separate determination that rule 202 was economically reasonable. The court held that rule 202 was invalid as applied to sources regulated by rule 203(g)(1), that the corporation was such a source, and that rule 202 could not be used to deny the renewal of its operating permit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's reversal of the board's decision denying the renewal of the applicant's operating permit and remanded the case to the board to consider whether all the necessary information submitted and certified by the applicant as current was sufficient to show compliance with the remaining valid rules of the board.

People v. Boykin


No. 57393


Supreme Court of Illinois


94 Ill. 2d 138; 445 N.E.2d 1174; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 288; 68 Ill. Dec. 321



February 4, 1983, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Allan Lane, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court affirmed; circuit court vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a decision by the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which held that supervision could have been imposed on defendant following a finding of guilt after trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty, after trial, of a misdemeanor offense of battery. She was sentenced to six months' probation. Defendant filed a motion to reduce her sentence, requesting supervision in lieu of probation. The trial court denied the motion and defendant appealed. The appellate court reversed and found that defendant was eligible for supervision under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-6-1(c) (1981). The state appealed and the court affirmed. The sole issue concerned the construction of § 1005-6-1(c), which empowered a court, upon a plea of guilty or stipulation by defendant of facts that supported the finding of guilt, to defer further proceedings and enter an order for supervision. The state contended the statute applied only if defendant pleaded guilty or stipulated to facts supporting her guilt. Defendant argued that it also applied if she was found guilty after trial. The court found that the statute was ambiguous and referred to the legislative history to aid in the statute's construction. The court concluded that the statute was not intended to change the prior practice, which was to allow supervision upon a finding of guilty after trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a decision that supervision could have been imposed on defendant following a finding of guilt after trial on the state's criminal charge.

People v. McCarty


Nos. 55923, 55971 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


94 Ill. 2d 28; 445 N.E.2d 298; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 277; 67 Ill. Dec. 818



January 24, 1983, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Kankakee County, the Hon. John F. Michela, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed that portion of the judgment of the Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois), which remanded his case for further proceedings after reversing the judgment of the circuit court, which had revoked defendant's probation and sentenced him to two years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with felony theft and tampering with a motor vehicle. The charge was enhanced to a felony because of defendant's prior conviction for armed robbery. Defendant pleaded guilty to felony theft in exchange for dropping the charge of tampering with a motor vehicle. While on probation, defendant was charged with attempted retail theft. He pleaded guilty and the state filed a petition to revoke defendant's probation on the basis of his theft conviction. The circuit court revoked defendant's probation and sentenced him to two years in prison. The appellate court held that robbery could be used to enhance a misdemeanor theft to a felony, but agreed with defendant that his probation could not be revoked on the basis of a guilty plea entered without the assistance of counsel. The appellate court remanded the case. The court held that robbery was not an aggravated form of theft capable of enhancing a misdemeanor theft to a felony. The court held that because defendant could not have been convicted of felony theft, the order of probation based on the conviction was void, and the two-year prison sentence based on revocation of his probation was likewise void.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court in so far as it reversed the circuit court's opinion revoking defendant's probation and sentencing him to two years in prison. The court reversed the appellate court in so far as it remanded the case.

 

310 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Gill v. Miller


No. 56817


Supreme Court of Illinois


94 Ill. 2d 52; 445 N.E.2d 330; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 279; 67 Ill. Dec. 850



January 24, 1983, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County, the Hon. John C. Layng, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Director of the Department of Public Aid (director) and an interest group, sought review of a judgment entered by the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which entered summary judgment in favor of appellees, a county clerk and a circuit court clerk. The circuit court held that Public Act 82-645 (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 2401 et seq. (1981), violated the Illinois Constitution.


OVERVIEW: The Act provided that a portion of the fees paid for marriage licenses and dissolutions, which were collected by county clerks and circuit court clerks, were to be deposited into a domestic violence fund by the county clerks. The county clerk and circuit court clerk challenged the constitutionality of the Act. The circuit court held that the Act was unconstitutional because it required the county clerks, not the county treasurers, to deposit the funds. That judgment was appealed by the director and the interest group. The court reversed the circuit court's judgment and remanded the matter. Courts were required to presume that the legislature intended to enact a constitutional statute. While Ill. Const. art. VII, § 9 required that fees collected by a unit of local government be deposited with its treasurer, the court concluded that the Act's reference to the county clerk was simply an error given the legislature's obvious awareness of the Illinois Constitution. Furthermore, courts were permitted to substitute one word for another when it was necessary to carry out the obvious intent of the legislature. Therefore, the Act, as originally enacted, was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment, which found that the Act was unconstitutional. The matter was remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Free


No. 52775


Supreme Court of Illinois


94 Ill. 2d 378; 447 N.E.2d 218; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 299; 69 Ill. Dec. 1



January 24, 1983, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 8, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. William V. Hopf, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted for murder under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1 (1977) and attempted rape under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-4 (1977) of one victim, and for the attempted murder and attempted rape of another victim. The Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) convicted defendant upon a jury verdict on all counts and sentenced him to death after a death penalty hearing. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the imposition of the death penalty. The court held that there was sufficient evidence to establish probable cause for issuance of the search warrant. Prior entries into defendant's house were reasonable, necessary, and justified as valid "protective sweeps" because there was a high potential for danger surrounding the arrest. The police knew that a gun was used in the offense, that defendant did not have it when he was captured, and that someone in the house could possibly have access to the weapon. The court held that defendant was not entitled to use the insanity defense because toxic psychosis induced by voluntary intoxication was not a mental disease or mental defect under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 6-2(a) (1977). The admission of certain physical evidence and photographs was not prejudicial because they were relevant to establish the existence of a material fact that defendant was familiar with guns and to connect defendant with the murder weapon. The indictment sufficiently informed defendant that the death penalty could be sought because he was charged with murder and attempted rape.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in convicting defendant of murder and attempted rape, and in imposing the death sentence.

The court held that the identification procedure was proper because each potential witness was interviewed separately and shown a photo display without any other person in the immediate vicinity. The court held that the state's death sentence was not unconstitutional and that defendant was properly sentenced to death because of aggravating factors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The court held that defendant's various contentions were without merit.

Illinois C. G. R. Co. v. Department of Local Government Affairs


No. 55942


Supreme Court of Illinois


95 Ill. 2d 111; 447 N.E.2d 315; 1983 Ill. LEXIS 310; 69 Ill. Dec. 98



January 24, 1983, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 8, 1983.

DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review from the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which held that the county could not assess and tax nine parcels of land owned by appellee railroad. Initially, the Department of Local Government Affairs (department) determined that the county could assess the taxes against the railroad, but a circuit court reversed the department's decision. The appeals court then affirmed the circuit court's ruling.


OVERVIEW: The county wanted to assess and tax nine parcels of land owned by a railroad company, but the appellate court held that the parcels were exempt from local property tax for 1971-72 under § 22 of the Illinois Central Charter, Ill. Rev. Stat. § 22, ch. 120, para. 374 (1971), and that for the tax years 1973-78 the parcels were "operating property" and were not assessable by local authorities pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 498, 560(2), 561, 562 (1971). On appeal, the court reversed and concluded that the Department of Local Government Affairs (department) was correct when it found that the railroad's nine parcels in the terminal area were subject to assessment by the county. The court held that the act creating the department was constitutional and that it did not violate the prohibition against amendment by reference. The court stated that the parcels were not "operating property" under § 79(2) of the Revenue Act of 1939, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 560(2) (1971), and that the property was not "necessary and indispensable" to the operation of the railroad. The court held that the parcels were "non-carrier real estate" under and were subject to assessment and taxation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court.

DISPOSITION: Motion allowed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent certified elected candidates filed a motion with the court to strike a petition for a state election contest. Petitioner candidates filed objections to the motion to strike.


OVERVIEW: Candidates filed a petition to challenge the certified results of a state election for a governor and a lieutenant governor. Respondents filed a motion to strike the petition and petitioners filed objections to the motion. The court allowed respondent's motion to strike the petition. The court held the petition was insufficient where the candidates failed to show they were entitled to any increase in their vote because of ballots with distinguishing marks. In addition to the specificity requirements, the court found that the petition was deficient because it failed to contain a necessary allegation or claim that an election contest would have changed the result of the election or allegations of fact showing such a result.


OUTCOME: The court allowed respondent's motion to strike the petition for a state election contest. The court noted that if any party wanted to petition for rehearing they needed to do so within ten days from the date of its order.

People v. Ruiz


No. 53415


Supreme Court of Illinois


94 Ill. 2d 245; 447 N.E.2d 148; 1982 Ill. LEXIS 400; 68 Ill. Dec. 890



December 17, 1982, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 28, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. James M. Bailey, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of murder, armed violence, and unlawful restraint and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant claimed that insufficient evidence supported his conviction, that the imposition of the death penalty was improper under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9--1(c)(5) (1978 Supp.), or alternatively, that it was unconstitutional to impose death based on accountability. Defendant also claimed that he was denied a fair trial. The court affirmed the lower court's conviction of defendant and its imposition of the death penalty, holding that sufficient evidence showed that defendant was guilty of murder, armed violence, and unlawful restraint under the principal of accountability. Defendant was a principal character in a common enterprise to commit acts of violence, from which defendant did not withdraw. Moreover, defendant received a fair trial even though simultaneous trials with multiple juries were conducted, such that both juries would be present for the testimony of any defendant. Nor did that modified severance procedure violate the Constitution. Finally, § 9--1(c)(5) permitted imposition of the death penalty based on accountability, and did not violate the Eight Amendment for doing so based on judicial consideration of defendant's intent and culpability.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's conviction of defendant for murder, armed violence, and unlawful restraint, and affirmed its sentence of defendant to death.

The inquiry into defendant's past misconduct contained in a presentence investigation report was within reasonable bounds. The court found no reversible error as to the murders of two of the victims. However, the sentence imposed for the murder of another victim was vacated for the imposition of a sentence other than death because nothing in the record showed that defendant killed, attempted to kill, or intended to kill that victim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, vacated in part, and remanded in part the lower court's decision that imposed the death penalty for each of three murders.

People v. Carter


No. 56106


Supreme Court of Illinois


97 Ill. 2d 133; 454 N.E.2d 189; 1982 Ill. LEXIS 404; 73 Ill. Dec. 329



December 17, 1982, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 30, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Robert J. Collins, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State was given leave to appeal as a matter of right the judgment of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which held that § 12, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 121 1/2, para. 712 (1977), of the Franchise Disclosure Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 121 1/2, para. 701 et seq. (1977), was unconstitutional. The appellate court overturned the defendant's conviction for violations of the Act.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of violating various provisions of the Act, such as failing to provide proper disclosure documents, failure to place receipts into escrow, and failure to register all franchise sales persons. The appellate court reversed the judgment. The court reversed the appellate court and reinstated the circuit court conviction. The court rejected the argument that the Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 121 1/2, para. 712 (1977) provided an unintelligible standard in that it stated the agency could provide exemptions from certain provisions of the act if it found that it was "in the public interest" to do so. The court held that the standard had to be read in context, and, in the context of the purposes of the act, the standard survived constitutional scrutiny. The statute did not violation the Due Process and Equal Protection Clauses because regulations passed pursuant to the statute provided that the agency had to follow procedural due process before permitting such exemptions and all final orders of the agency were subject to review. Thus, the agency's power was not exercised arbitrarily or without restrictions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court holding that a section of the Franchise Disclosure Act was unconstitutional.

 

318 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Illinois Bell Tel. Co. v. Allphin


No. 54753


Supreme Court of Illinois


93 Ill. 2d 241; 443 N.E.2d 580; 1982 Ill. LEXIS 382; 66 Ill. Dec. 654



December 17, 1982, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Earl J. Arkiss, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee telephone company claimed that appellant Department of Revenue (DOR) was not permitted to collect taxes on certain revenues because they were exempt under the Messages Tax, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, paras. 467.1 et seq. (1979). After the trial court exempted intrastate charges but included interstate charges in taxable revenues, the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) ruled for the company on all claims. The DOR appealed.


OVERVIEW: The company claimed that the tax could not be imposed on certain revenues. When the appeals court agreed, the DOR appealed. The court affirmed. It held that the language and history of the tax statute did not permit imposition of the tax on interstate messages, because the law that prevailed at the time the statute was adopted prohibited occupation taxes on interstate commerce, because the interpretation was consistent with historical administrative interpretations, and because tax laws were to be strictly construed against the state. The court also affirmed a ruling that no tax was payable on revenues which, while they were reflected in the company's records, actually were attributable to and transmitted to other local phone companies under division-of-revenue formulas. The court found that the only reason that those amounts were reflected in the company's records was because the company served as an "administrator" for all of the local phone companies and was responsible for calculating and redistributing revenues based on actual usage of the constituent phone lines, and that the tax was to be imposed only on that portion of billings that the company retained under the formula.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appeals court exempting the subject revenues from the Messages Tax.

 

319 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Daley v. Schreier


No. 56191


Supreme Court of Illinois


92 Ill. 2d 271; 442 N.E.2d 185; 1982 Ill. LEXIS 334; 65 Ill. Dec. 874



October 22, 1982, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original action for mandamus.



DISPOSITION: Writ awarded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state sought the issuance of a writ of mandamus, or in the alternative a supervisory order, directing respondent trial judge of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) to sentence respondent convicted individuals in accordance with the court's mandate in a named case. The cause had been remanded to the trial court with directions to resentence the convicted individuals in accordance with law.


OVERVIEW: The convicted individuals were indicted for the offense of knowingly delivering more than 30 grams of a substance containing cocaine. The offense was a Class X felony, the penalty for which was a minimum of six years' imprisonment. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005 -- 8 -- 1(a)(3) (1979). Following a bench trial, the trial judge found both convicted individuals guilty in the "manner and form" charged in the indictment. Based on another case, the trial judge concluded that the statutory classification was unconstitutional; he sentenced the convicted individuals as Class 3 felons. The court reversed the appellate court decision in the other case, and remanded the instant case to the trial court with directions for resentencing in accordance with law. The convicted individuals filed another motion for a new trial, which the trial judge granted. The court held that a writ of mandamus was to issue directing the trial judge to comply with the court's prior mandate for resentencing. The trial judge's order failed to comply with the court's earlier mandate, and for that reason the trial judge lacked jurisdiction to enter his order granting a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court held that a writ of mandamus was to issue directing the trial judge to comply with the court's prior mandate and to resentence the convicted individuals as Class X felons.

 

320 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Mobil Oil Corp. v. Johnson


No. 55329


Supreme Court of Illinois


93 Ill. 2d 126; 442 N.E.2d 846; 1982 Ill. LEXIS 372; 66 Ill. Dec. 285



October 22, 1982, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 10, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County, the Hon. Simon L. Friedman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Department of Revenue (department) and plaintiff oil corporation sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which ordered a refund to the oil corporation, holding that the department violated the Administrative Procedure Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 127, para. 1001 et seq. (1979) when it developed methods to calculate the use taxes, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 127, para. 170 et seq. (1977).


OVERVIEW: The oil corporation purchased crude oil and refined it. No oil was left over, but not all products had market value. After paying use taxes on all the oil, the oil corporation filed an action for a refund. The trial court ordered a refund on the ground that the department violated the Administrative Procedures Act (APA), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 127, paras. 1001 et seq. The department appealed and the oil corporation filed a cross-appeal, alleging the Use Tax Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 439.1 et seq., was unconstitutionally ambiguous. The court reversed the decision of the trial court. The court determined that the crude oil purchased by the corporation was a "sale at retail" and tax rules permitted taxation of the entire sale when only part of the property is for "use," that the intra-agency memorandum on taxing calculations was not a rule under the APA so the department did not violate the act, and that there was no constitutional infirmity because the rule only memorialized existing case law so the corporation had notice of the law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court that had granted a use tax refund to the oil corporation. The court determined that the crude oil purchased by the corporation was a retail sale and even the products left over from refining were taxable, and that the corporation had notice and the policy and method of taxation did not violate the constitution.

 

321 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Davis


Nos. 55318, 55335 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


93 Ill. 2d 155; 442 N.E.2d 855; 1982 Ill. LEXIS 374; 66 Ill. Dec. 294



October 22, 1982, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 24, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeals from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hons. Paul A. O'Malley and Earl E. Strayhorn, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: One defendant was convicted of voluntary manslaughter. The other defendant was convicted of rape and robbery. In a consolidated appeal, the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) affirmed the convictions and sentences of both defendants. Defendants appealed, both contending that the trial court failed to state its reasons for imposing a particular sentence as required by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 1005-4-1(c); 1005-8-1(b).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the right to a statement of reasons was waived on appeal if defendant failed to demand compliance with the statute in the trial court. The court determined that a construction that would hold §§ 1005-4-1(c) and 1005- 8-1(b) to constitute a mandatory requirement would clearly render the provisions an unconstitutional invasion of the inherent power of the judiciary. The statute was not mandatory, therefore there was no independent duty upon the trial court to give a statement of reasons. Instead, the right was purely personal to defendants. The court held that because defendants had failed to request statements of reasons for their particular sentences, they had waived the issue. The statute did entitle defendants to statements of reasons for their sentences and it would be error for the trial court to refuse to make statements if requested.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court, which upheld the convictions and sentences of both defendants.

 

322 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


In re Marriage of Cohn


No. 54978


Supreme Court of Illinois


93 Ill. 2d 190; 443 N.E.2d 541; 1982 Ill. LEXIS 377; 66 Ill. Dec. 615



October 22, 1982, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County, the Hon. John J. Kaufman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Motion denied; judgment affirmed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner wife filed a petition to dissolve her marriage to respondent husband. The trial court dissolved the marriage, but reserved property disposition, maintenance, and child custody issues for future consideration. The trial court thereafter denied the wife's motion to vacate the judgment of dissolution. The Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois) reversed. The husband contested the judgment on appeal.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that under the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act, specifically Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 401(3) (1977), appropriate circumstances had to exist before a trial judge could enter a judgment of dissolution and reserve questions of child custody, support, maintenance, or property disposition. The husband disagreed and also argued that a legislative amendment to the statute retroactively validated the trial court's action. The amendment attempted to validate prior bifurcated judgments of dissolution like the one here. The court upheld the appellate court's judgment and held that the amendment was unconstitutional. First, the trial court could not under the original statute enter a bifurcated judgment of dissolution in the case. Second, although the legislature may change the law as interpreted by the courts prospectively, it cannot retroactively alter a statute to overrule a decision of a reviewing court. Here, the amendment was an unconstitutional attempt to invalidate retroactively the action of the appellate court. The legislature contravened the principle of separation of powers set forth in the Illinois Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court and remanded the cause to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

People v. Devin


No. 53175


Supreme Court of Illinois


93 Ill. 2d 326; 444 N.E.2d 102; 1982 Ill. LEXIS 388; 67 Ill. Dec. 63



October 22, 1982, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 28, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the circuit court of Du Page County, the Hon. Bruce R. Fawell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; sentence vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which, after a jury trial, entered a conviction for murder and sentenced defendant to death in accordance with the jury's findings under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9 -- 1(d) (1979).


OVERVIEW: After an inmate was hung by a rope and killed, defendant was convicted of murder and sentenced to death in accordance with the jury's determination that there were no mitigating factors to preclude a sentence of death. The court affirmed defendant's murder conviction, holding that no error resulted from the failure of defendant to be present when the jury viewed the jail premises and there was no evidence to support defendant's tendered instruction on involuntary manslaughter. The court vacated defendant's death sentence, determining that the jury was permitted to consider certain information without adequate limiting instructions. The jury heard numerous witnesses testify that defendant discussed numerous ways to kill or torture people and made several confessions of murder. Because defendant's sociopathic personality may have produced such fantasies and there was no evidence of such crimes, the circuit court erred by failing to provide a cautionary instruction that there was no corroborating evidence which tended to prove that any of the conduct had occurred. The court remanded the case to the circuit court for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of murder but vacated the sentence of death. The court remanded the case to the circuit court for further proceedings.

 

324 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Koeppel v. Ives


No. 56239


Supreme Court of Illinois


92 Ill. 2d 523; 442 N.E.2d 176; 1982 Ill. LEXIS 356; 65 Ill. Dec. 865



October 22, 1982, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County, the Hon. Charles W. Wilson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county clerk sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois), which held that § 162a of the Revenue Act of 1939, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 643a (1979), was unconstitutional on the ground that it conflicted with Ill. Const. art. VII, § 11 (1970).


OVERVIEW: A county board adopted a resolution pursuant to § 162a calling for a referendum on a proposal to increase the tax-rate. The question was to be voted upon in November. A month later, respondent taxpayer filed a petition pursuant to § 162a calling for an election on a proposal to decrease the tax-rate, which was held in March of the same year. The taxpayer argued that § 162a limited elections on tax rates to one per year and that the first tax-rate election held in a calendar year would supercede any tax-rate election already scheduled for later in the year. The court found that § 162a was constitutional and disagreed with the taxpayer's interpretation of the section. The court held that the legislature intended that the party who first properly initiated a request for a tax-rate election to be held in a calendar year had priority over parties subsequently requesting a tax-rate election for the same year. The taxpayer's submission of a tax-rate proposition conflicted with § 162a because it was initiated a month after the county board requested a tax-rate election in the same year. The court held that the results of the March election were void and of no effect.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the circuit court and remanded the case for further proceedings.

In re Marriage of Eltrevoog


No. 54798


Supreme Court of Illinois


92 Ill. 2d 66; 440 N.E.2d 840; 1982 Ill. LEXIS 313; 64 Ill. Dec. 936

DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-wife sought review of judgment entered by the Circuit Court of La Salle County (Illinois), which found that the ex-wife had proved the charges in her petition for separate maintenance filed pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 402 (1979), and that appellee ex-husband had proved the charges in his petition for dissolution and then entered a judgment for dissolution.

326 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Brown


No. 54984


Supreme Court of Illinois


92 Ill. 2d 248; 442 N.E.2d 136; 1982 Ill. LEXIS 331; 65 Ill. Dec. 825



September 17, 1982, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 24, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. William Cousins, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged the judgment of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which affirmed the circuit court's grant of the motion to dismiss the indictment of defendant, who was charged with murder, on the grounds that defendant's right to speedy trial was violated.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that a writ of mandamus filed in another simultaneously pending case did not toll a 160-day limitations period in the prosecution of defendant, since there was no relationship demonstrated between the mandamus action and the delay in the subject prosecution. Also, the court held that the 160-day period within which defendant was required to be tried was not tolled by any delay attributable to defendant in a simultaneously pending case, particularly where the delay which occurred in the simultaneously pending case was not demonstrated to be related to the delay in bringing defendant to trial. Further, the trial court's dismissal of the indictment on the 158th day of 160-day statutory term did not constitute reversible error, where the source of miscalculation was the State. There was nothing to indicate that either party was aware of the two-day discrepancy, and there was no bad faith or subterfuge in connection with this error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court and appellate court.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State charged defendant with possession of LSD contrary to Ill. Rev. Stat., ch. 56 1/2, par. 1402(b) (1979). The Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois) reversed the trial court's denial of motion to suppress evidence. The State appealed.

OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court.

First Federal Sav. & Loan Asso. v. Walker


No. 54494


Supreme Court of Illinois


91 Ill. 2d 218; 437 N.E.2d 644; 1982 Ill. LEXIS 278; 62 Ill. Dec. 956



June 1, 1982, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Harold A. Siegan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff bank appealed a decision of the Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois), which granted to defendant debtors the right to reinstate their mortgage after a third default. The trial court held that the reinstatement statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95, para. 57 (1979), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Debtors defaulted on their mortgage and the bank sought foreclosure of their home. The debtors asserted that the bank had waived enforcement of the once-in-every-five-years limitation contained in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95, para. 57 (1979) because it had previously allowed them to reinstate their mortgage twice in two years. The court on appeal first found that the statute did not violate equal protection because the class of persons who have never defaulted was rationally different than those who have previously defaulted and was related to a legitimate state interest in allowing a debtor plagued once by problems to keep his home. The court further found that the right to reinstate a mortgage was unknown at common law was purely statutory and could thus be limited by the legislature. The court also ruled that the statute did not infringe on the equitable powers of the court, again, because no common law rights were involved. Finally, the court found that the bank had not waived enforcement of the statute because to hold otherwise would encourage more foreclosures.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the debtors and remanded for relief in favor of the bank.

McHenry State Bank v. Harris


No. 55989


Supreme Court of Illinois


89 Ill. 2d 542; 434 N.E.2d 1144; 1982 Ill. LEXIS 259; 61 Ill. Dec. 547



April 16, 1982, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County, the Hon. Simon L. Friedman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff banks sought a declaratory judgment that Public Act 82--21, which amended portions of the Bank Holding Company Act of 1957 and the Illinois Banking Act, was unconstitutional and also to enjoin defendant Commissioner of Banks and Trust Companies from taking any action under the amendments. The Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois) dismissed with prejudice the banks' action for declaratory judgment and injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: The court held that because the effect of the Public Act (act) did not authorize branch banking, it did not require, pursuant to Ill. Const. art. XIII, § 8, a three-fifths majority in each house of the general assembly. Additionally, the court held that the act did not confer powers on the Federal Reserve Board that it did not already have under the Federal Bank Holding Company Act. The act included a provision that automatically incorporated all future amendments to the Federal Bank Holding Company Act into the act. The court held, however, that in view of the express limitations under 12 U.S.C.S. § 36(c) (1976) and the express reservation of rights to the states contained in 12 U.S.C.S. § 1846 (1976), there was no necessity to abolish the distinction between branch banking and the operation of facilities such as those authorized in the act. Accordingly, the judgment finding that the act was constitutional was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court, finding that the act amending portions of the Bank Holding Act and the Illinois Banking Act was constitutional, was affirmed.

 

330 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Davis v. Vazquez


Nos. 55050, 55365


Supreme Court of Illinois


92 Ill. 2d 132; 441 N.E.2d 54; 1982 Ill. LEXIS 321; 65 Ill. Dec. 262



April 16, 1982, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 27, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original action for mandamus.



DISPOSITION: Writs denied; cause remanded. Writ denied; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state filed original mandamus actions, challenging the authority of the juvenile court system to set bail for two juveniles charged with murder and held in juvenile facilities, pending the state's appeal of the denial of its motions to have the juveniles tried as adults.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the juveniles were entitled to be admitted to bail. The court first noted that the Juvenile Court Act made no provision either for interlocutory appeals or for bail. Case law indicated that the state was permitted to take an interlocutory, pre-adjudication appeal from a juvenile court's order denying a motion to prosecute a minor as an adult, but that the minor had no right to an immediate appeal of an order permitting transfer to adult court. Nothing in the case law or the Act itself required that a juvenile be released without bail pending the state's appeal. However, this did not mean that the minor could be held without a reasonable bail being set. The state constitution granted the right to bail for all but capital offenses, and this guarantee applied to juveniles as well as to adults. While, in general, the standards that applied to the determination of a reasonable bail for juveniles were the same that applied to adults, in the circumstance where the juvenile was detained pending the state's appeal, it was up to the state to show compelling reasons necessitating holding the minor to bail before bail could be required.


OUTCOME: The writs of mandamus were denied. The juvenile court had the authority to set bail.

 

331 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. One 1979 Pontiac Grand Prix Auto.


No. 55567


Supreme Court of Illinois


89 Ill. 2d 506; 433 N.E.2d 1301; 1982 Ill. LEXIS 256; 60 Ill. Dec. 934



March 29, 1982, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Kankakee County, the Hon. John F. Michela, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged the judgment from the Appellate Court (Illinois), which reversed the circuit court's order denying appellee purchaser's motion to strike and allowing the state to affix a new vehicle identification number (VIN) to an automobile with a defaced VIN number and to sell it.


OVERVIEW: After the purchaser bought the vehicle, the state confiscated it and declared it as contraband pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4-107(i) (1979) because the VIN on the vehicle was false, and the confidential VIN was so badly mutilated that it was impossible to determine the true VIN. The circuit court entered an order allowing the state to sell the vehicle. The appellate court reversed the order. This appeal followed. The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment. Here, the effect of § 4-107(i) was to strip the purchaser of all rights to the vehicle by declaring it as contraband even though he was completely innocent and had no way of discovering any wrongdoing. Although there was a presumption of validity attached to the exercise of the state's police power, the classification of the vehicle as contraband per se was unconstitutional. It did not appear that depriving the innocent purchaser of his property furthered either purpose of the statute. The purchaser took the necessary steps to assure that the VIN located at the place required by regulations matched the VIN on the title, and that was all that was constitutionally required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment, which reversed the circuit court's order allowing the state to sell the purchaser's vehicle.

Drury v. County of McLean


No. 54591


Supreme Court of Illinois


89 Ill. 2d 417; 433 N.E.2d 666; 1982 Ill. LEXIS 243; 60 Ill. Dec. 624



March 16, 1982, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of McLean County, the Hon. Wayne C. Townley, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county appealed a decision of the Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois), which reversed the decision granting summary judgment in favor of plaintiff former criminal defendants as to the amount of court costs paid to the county which were to be refunded to the former defendants, but denying summary judgment in their favor for the reimbursement of fine money.


OVERVIEW: Former criminal defendants had been convicted under the Uniform Narcotic Drug Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 22 -- 1 et seq. (1969), and paid a fine and court costs. The statute was declared unconstitutional and all those convicted had a right to the expungement of their convictions and the return of any fine money and court costs attributable to such convictions. The court of appeals reversed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the former defendants for the court costs and the denial of summary judgment with regard to the fines. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the clerk of the circuit court was not a county official and money received by the clerk could not be said to be received by the county. Although the former defendants might have been legally entitled to the fine money, the clerk never received it. The county could not be held liable as the fine money was not collected by one of its officers and the money was never received in the county treasury.


OUTCOME: The judgment that reversed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the former criminal defendants as to the amount of court costs paid to the county which were to be refunded to the former defendants and denied summary judgment in their favor as to the reimbursement of fine money was reversed.

Appanoose v. County Supervisor of Assessments


No. 55229


Supreme Court of Illinois

March 16, 1982, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Hancock County, the Hon. Stephen G. Evans, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Department of Revenue challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Hancock County (Illinois) that agreed with plaintiff townships that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 482 (1979) et seq., was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The townships filed suit, seeking to have the Act, which consolidated townships for tax assessment purposes, declared unconstitutional. The trial court agreed that the Act was unconstitutional. The Department appealed. On review, the townships argued that the Act violated Ill. Const. Art. Thus, the argument that the consolidation of the assessor's positions was without merit. Further, the Act did not affect the entirety of the township scheme.

334 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wagner


No. 54434


Supreme Court of Illinois


89 Ill. 2d 308; 433 N.E.2d 267; 1982 Ill. LEXIS 235; 60 Ill. Dec. 470



February 19, 1982, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 25, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County, the Hon. Kenneth J. Juen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Appellate Court for the Fifth District (Illinois) affirmed a judgment of conviction entered against defendant after he was found guilty by a jury of having violated § 404 of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1404 (1977), by delivering .4 grams of a substance represented to have been heroin and the imposition of a two-year imprisonment sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of violation of § 404 of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act (Act), codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1404 (1977) for delivering a substance he represented as being heroin. The appellate court affirmed. On appeal, the court reversed, finding that § 404 of the Act was unconstitutional as violative of Ill. Const. art. I, § 2 (1970) because it was not reasonably designed to remedy the evil which the legislature determined to have been a greater threat to the public. Specifically, the court found that defendant was subject to a greater penalty for delivery of .4 grams of a harmless brown powder than a person who would have actually delivered any amount of a schedule IV or V controlled substance under § 401(e), (f) of the Act. Because the legislature clearly intended the delivery of actual controlled substances to have been more of a threat than the delivery of noncontrolled substances fraudulently represented as controlled substances, the statute should not have punished the latter offense more severely than the former. Defendant had standing to challenge the statute because he was among the group of persons aggrieved by its constitutional defect.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of conviction and the judgment affirming the conviction.

 

335 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Commercial Nat'l Bank v. Chicago


No. 55457


Supreme Court of Illinois


89 Ill. 2d 45; 432 N.E.2d 227; 1982 Ill. LEXIS 216; 59 Ill. Dec. 643


November 16, 1981, Argued and Announced  
January 25, 1982, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Richard L. Curry, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, business entities and professionals, filed suit against defendant City of Chicago (city) to enjoin the service-tax ordinance in Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code § 200.5--1 et seq. (1981). The circuit court granted the city's motion to dismiss holding that the ordinance was not unconstitutional and dissolved its preliminary injunction. The business entities and professionals sought review.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code § 200.5--1 et seq. (1981), which taxed services with certain exceptions. The business entities and professionals filed suit and sought a declaratory judgment that the service tax ordinance was invalid and sought an injunction to stop enforcement of the tax. The circuit court initially granted a preliminary injunction pending final resolution. The circuit court subsequently granted the city's motion to dismiss, held that the ordinance was constitutional and dissolved the preliminary injunction. On appeal, the court reversed and held that (1) the service-tax ordinance was unconstitutional as an attempt to impose a tax upon occupations without authorization of the Illinois General Assembly, contrary to Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6(e), (2) exclusion of certain professions from the tax was unconstitutional under Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2, (3) the severability or saving clause in the ordinance did no save the remainder of the ordinance, and (4) the city, as a home rule unit, did not possess extraterritorial powers to tax services outside the city pursuant to Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6(a).


OUTCOME: The circuit court reversed the circuit court's judgment that dismissed the suit because the service-tax ordinance was unconstitutional.

 

336 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Sierra Club v. Kenney


No. 54437


Supreme Court of Illinois


88 Ill. 2d 110; 429 N.E.2d 1214; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 403; 57 Ill. Dec. 851



December 18, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Jersey County, the Hon. Howard Lee White, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff organization brought suit against the Illinois Department of Conservation (state), seeking to enjoin the state from logging or inviting bids for logging a portion of a state park. The trial court denied the organization's request. The Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois) reversed the trial court's judgment. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court determined that the logging proposal was inconsistent with the legislative purpose for a state park. The state should have been enjoined from proceeding with its logging proposal. However, the court determined that the appellate court went too far in the injunction it issued. The court determined that the injunction should have been limited to preventing the state from its proposed timber sale. The complete ban on logging was overbroad and would have required the state to abandoned its statutory duties relating to the state park.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgments of the lower courts and remanded the case to the trial court for it to enter an injunction consistent with the court's opinion.

 

337 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Helm


No. 54507


Supreme Court of Illinois


89 Ill. 2d 34; 431 N.E.2d 1033; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 424; 59 Ill. Dec. 276



December 18, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Macon County, the Hon. Rodney A. Scott, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of an order from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion to suppress illegal drugs that were found in defendant's purse during an inventory search after defendant was arrested for domestic battery on her husband.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested in her home on a battery charge filed by her husband, and when told that she would have to go to the station, defendant dressed and grabbed her purse. At the station a female desk clerk searched the purse and discovered pill that turned out to be amphetamines in a coin pouch. Defendant was charged with possession and the trial court granted defendant's motion to suppress the pills. The state filed an appeal. On review the court found that the search of defendant's purse was made without a warrant and was banned by both the Fourth Amendment and Ill. Const. art. I, § 6 and did not fall within any of the exceptions to the warrant requirement. The court held that the officer's were in no danger at the station, and held that if the search was indeed an inventory search to preserve defendant's property, that purpose could have been more easily served by a less intrusive manner by simply locking the entire purse in a secured storage container at the station instead of having the desk clerk rummage through defendant's purse.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that suppressed the amphetamines that were seized from defendant's purse.

 

338 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Cook Associates, Inc. v. Lexington United Corp.


No. 53854


Supreme Court of Illinois


87 Ill. 2d 190; 429 N.E.2d 847; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 388; 57 Ill. Dec. 730



December 4, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Thomas J. O'Brien, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an Illinois corporation, was awarded summary judgment in a breach of contract action against appellee, a Delaware corporation. Appellant sought review after the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) reversed and held that the trial court lacked personal jurisdiction over appellee.


OVERVIEW: Appellee argued that it was not subject to personal jurisdiction in Illinois for purposes of appellant's breach of contract action because it had insufficient contacts with the State of Illinois. The court found that appellee was not subject to the Illinois long-arm statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 17 (1977), because the cause of action did not arise from a business transaction in the state. Appellant argued that a Chicago interview was the first step in the parties' negotiations, but the court was not persuaded. The court further found that appellee was not amenable to jurisdiction in Illinois under the "doing business" doctrine because its activities in the state, which consisted of one interview and three trade-show exhibits, did not occur with a fair measure of permanence and continuity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, holding that appellee was not amenable to service under the Illinois long-arm statute because the cause of action did not arise out of an Illinois transaction, and that three Chicago trade-show exhibits were not "doing business" for jurisdictional purposes.

People v. Gaines


No. 52794


Supreme Court of Illinois


88 Ill. 2d 342; 430 N.E.2d 1046; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 415; 58 Ill. Dec. 795



December 4, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 29, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Richard J. Petrarca, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of two murders, one attempted murder, and two armed robberies. In a separate sentencing proceeding, the same jury determined that there were no mitigating factors sufficient to preclude the imposition of the death sentence. The Circuit Court of Cook County then sentenced defendant to death on his murder convictions. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court held that: 1) the admission of testimony by two deputies, during the sentencing proceeding, regarding defendant's conduct outside the courtroom was not error, because they only testified to the aggravating factor, the death penalty was proper without such testimony, and defense counsel did not seek any testimony regarding the extent of the deputies' contacts with the jurors; 2) A presentence report was not necessary, because the trial court was obligated to return a death sentence after the jury found no mitigating factors; 3) defendant had no right to make an unsworn and un-cross-examined statement to the jury, and further, such denial did not adversely affect defendant as he failed to show that he would have had anything to say; 4) the jury was not required to determine whether defendant was subject to rehabilitation; 5) the jury was not required to specify the aggravating factor upon which it relied; 6) the trial court had no authority to set-aside the sentencing verdict; 7) the death penalty did not violate the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122-2 (1979).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

Scott v. Association for Childbirth at Home, International


No. 53802


Supreme Court of Illinois


88 Ill. 2d 279; 430 N.E.2d 1012; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 411; 58 Ill. Dec. 761



November 20, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 29, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County, the Hon. Simon L. Friedman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Attorney General challenged a decision of the Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois), which affirmed the dismissal of complaints to compel compliance by defendant association with an investigation under the Consumer Fraud and Deceptive Business Practices Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 121 1/2, para. 261 et seq., on the ground that the Act's prohibition of unfair acts and practices was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: The Attorney General issued an administrative subpoena and demand for verified statements to an association in an investigation of possible violations of the Act. When the association failed to comply, complaints were filed to compel responses. The trial court dismissed the complaints, and the Attorney General appealed. The district appellate court held that probable cause was not required for the issuance of an administrative subpoena, but affirmed the dismissal because it found that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 121, para. 262, which prohibited unfair practices, was unconstitutionally vague. The court affirmed the part of the judgment relating to probable cause, reversed the vagueness determination, reversed the trial court's dismissal for failure to state a cause of action, and remanded. The Act was not void for vagueness because it was sufficiently clear and definite to give adequate notice of the conduct it proscribed to persons of reasonable intelligence. The investigative powers granted under the Act did not violate the Fourth Amendment or Ill. Const. art. I, § 6 because they were restricted to demands for reasonably definite information relevant to the Act's purposes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's decision in part and reversed it in part, reversed the trial court's decision, and remanded the case.

1981 Ill. LEXIS 426; 58 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1809

342 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Wilson v. All-Steel, Inc.


No. 54046


Supreme Court of Illinois


87 Ill. 2d 28; 428 N.E.2d 489; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 369; 56 Ill. Dec. 897; 28 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 35; 28 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P32,474



November 13, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County, the Hon. John A. Krause, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former employee and intervenor Department of Human Rights (Illinois) appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which dismissed the employee's complaint against defendant employer and held that § 8.01a of the Fair Employment Practices Act, codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 858.01a (1979), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: After the employee was discharged by the employer, she filed a charge of sexual and racial discrimination with the Illinois Fair Employment Practices Commission. The Commission issued a complaint, which the Commission subsequently dismissed because it was not issued within the 180-day period required by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 858.01 (1977). The employee then filed suit under para. 858.01a, which created a new cause of action for certain persons whose claims had been barred by administrative delay. The substance of para. 858.01a was later codified at § 9-102(B) of the Illinois Human Rights Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 68, para. 9-102(B) (1980 Supp.). The court held that the statutes constituted prohibited special legislation and violated Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13. The court reasoned that no rational basis existed for the distinction created by the statutes. The court further held that the statutes violated the employer's due process rights by attempting to revive a previously-barred cause of action. Once the claim was barred by the 180-day period, the employer acquired a vested right in the application of that limitations period that the legislature could not take away.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court order dismissing the employee's complaint.
