Board of Trustees v. Human Rights Com.


No. 54676


Supreme Court of Illinois


88 Ill. 2d 22; 429 N.E.2d 1207; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 397; 57 Ill. Dec. 844



November 13, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff board of trustees (board) and defendant human rights commission (commission) sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which held that the exemption in the Illinois Human Rights Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 68 para. 2-104(E)(1) (1980), to the compulsory retirement ban was unconstitutionally vague and that compulsory retirement at 65 was illegal.


OVERVIEW: The board brought an action in the trial court after the commission affirmed an administrative order holding its plan for compulsory retirement at 65 illegal under the Illinois Human Rights Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 68, para. 2-102(A) (1980). The trial court found that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 68, para. 2-104(E) (1980), which permitted employers to apply different, non-discriminating standards of compensation or conditions of employment to older employees, was unconstitutionally vague and that the exemption did not apply to the board's plan. Both parties sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court but found that the exemption was not vague. The court held that the exemption permitted employers to treat older employees differently so long as that the treatment did not produce a discriminatory effect and provided examples of permissible actions, but that compulsory retirement before 70 was impermissible.


OUTCOME: The court found that the exemption to the Illinois Human Rights Act's prohibition on compulsory retirement before age 70 was not unconstitutionally vague, but that it was inapplicable to the board's compulsory retirement plan. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court because it had reached the same result.

 

344 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lewis


No. 52338


Supreme Court of Illinois


88 Ill. 2d 129; 430 N.E.2d 1346; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 404; 58 Ill. Dec. 895



November 13, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 29, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Macon County, the Hon. Robert J. Steigmann, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois) which convicted him of the offenses of armed robbery, aggravated kidnapping, and murder, and imposed the death penalty pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1 (1977).


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction for the armed robbery of a bank, kidnapping, and the murder of the bank's security guard, asserting numerous errors including that the death penalty statute was impermissibly vague, that the jury erred in finding no mitigating factor sufficient to preclude the death penalty, and that his trial counsel was incompetent. The court rejected defendant's contentions, finding that the death penalty statute was not invalid because the language of the statute concerning mitigating factors was not overly broad. The court noted that mitigating factors were not as precisely defined as aggravating factors because the latter were utilized to determine whether the death penalty was applicable. The court ruled that testimony that the security guard reached for his gun before defendant fired was not a mitigating factor that precluded the death penalty because the statute did not require such a finding. The court ruled that the alleged incidents of attorney incompetence were insufficient to establish defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel claim because there was no reasonable possibility that the incidents contributed to the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction. The court held that the death penalty statute was not unconstitutional because there was no reason to assume that the mitigating factors language was construed or applied in a manner that rendered the provision overly broad.

 

345 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Grobsmith v. Kempiners


No. 53272


Supreme Court of Illinois


88 Ill. 2d 399; 430 N.E.2d 973; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 417; 58 Ill. Dec. 722



November 13, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 29, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County, the Hon. Herman S. Hasse, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant directors of state departments, boards, and commissions (directors) appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which held unconstitutional § 8b.18 of the Illinois Personnel Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 127, para. 63b1083.18 (1979) (statute), after plaintiff civil service employees challenged the statute.


OVERVIEW: The employees brought an action for declaratory judgment and injunctive relief, challenging the statute as unconstitutional. The circuit court held that the employees were vested with a statutorily created property right that could not be terminated as provided in the statute. The circuit court found the statute unconstitutional and the directors appealed. The court reversed. The court held that the general assembly had the power to subject certain civil service positions to term appointments. Civil service status was not a vested right because it had been created by the general assembly and therefore could be changed by legislative action. There was no constitutional impediment to the general assembly's power to change the duration of the term of the appointments. The statute did not violate equal protection because there was a reasonable basis for the classification and the court declined to substitute its own judgment for that of the general assembly. Finally, the statute did not violate the prohibition against retrospective application of legislation because the general assembly retained the power to alter or abolish the employees' job status. The statute was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court, which had held unconstitutional a provision of the Illinois Personnel Code after the employees brought a challenge to the statute.

Goldblatt Bros. v. Indus. Com

Supreme Court of Illinois

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent employer sought review from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which confirmed a modification award by the Industrial Commission that provided that the employer was required to pay weekly support to a minor child of a deceased employee who had sustained accidental injuries that caused his death.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner divorced spouse of decedent filed a claim for support of the decedent's minor child, whom he was paying child support for at the time of his death. The employer challenged the constitutional validity of §§ 7 and 8(b)(2) of the Workmen's Compensation Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, paras. 138.7 and 138.8(b)(2) (1977), contending that they set up an arbitrary classification of employee survivors. There was no abandonment of this action by the filing of a petition for compensation in another state because there was no threat of double compensation and there was no election of remedies. Lastly, the court held that the definition of "child" in § 7(a) of the Workmen's Compensation Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 138.7(a) (1977), was not too indefinite. The award was confirmed.

People v. Searle


No. 53514


Supreme Court of Illinois


86 Ill. 2d 385; 427 N.E.2d 65; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 353; 55 Ill. Dec. 945



September 30, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Woodford County, the Hon. William T. Caisley, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Woodford County (Illinois), which ordered the State to return appellee motorcyclist's motorcycle to him after the State seized it for lack of a manufacturer's identification number. The State sought to recover storage fees for the motorcycle.


OVERVIEW: The police stopped the motorcyclist for a traffic violation, found that the engine of his motorcycle did not bear a legible manufacturer's identification number as required by law, and seized the motorcycle. The motorcyclist was found guilty of unknowingly possessing a vehicle without a required identification number. However, the case was subsequently dismissed because it was brought in the wrong county. The circuit court ordered the police to stamp the number on the motorcycle and return it to the motorcyclist. The State appealed, contending that the motorcyclist was required to pay storage fees under § 4-207 of the Illinois Vehicle Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4-207 (1977). The court affirmed, holding that para. 4-207 did not apply. All the legal proceedings arose under article I of the Code involving anti-theft laws, and para. 4-207 was part of article II of the Code involving abandoned, lost, stolen, or unclaimed vehicles. The payment of towing and storage fees under para. 4-207 was limited to vehicles released to the owner under para. 4-207, which implied that vehicles could be released under other parts of the Code without such payment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

 

352 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Green v. Advance Ross Electronics Corp.


No. 53951


Supreme Court of Illinois


86 Ill. 2d 431; 427 N.E.2d 1203; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 356; 56 Ill. Dec. 657



September 30, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 25, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Joseph M. Wosik, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee brought an action against defendant employers for breach of an employment contract. The employers counterclaimed and also brought a motion to join the employee's father, also a former employee, as an additional counter-defendant. The employee's father contested jurisdiction, and the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) affirmed the circuit court's refusal to join him as a party. The employers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employers contended that an out-of-state resident submitted to the jurisdiction of Illinois when he committed a tort which caused a diminution of the funds of a corporation organized or headquartered in Illinois. The court held that the substantive matter with which the appeal was concerned was a Texas dispute. The court held that the tortious acts, if any, and the losses or injury were completed when they occurred in Texas. Accordingly, the court held that Texas was the place of the wrongs, and their commission could not reasonably or justifiably be transferred to Illinois by the rationale that their consequence reduced the amount of corporate assets in Illinois. The court held that the employee was subject to Illinois jurisdiction because the employee chose it, but the court found that no matter how much more convenient and economical it was to adjudicate the counterclaim against the employee, and the similar claim against the employee's father, in the same action in Illinois, the employee's father could not be brought under the authority of Illinois courts. The court held that the connection of the employee with Illinois was not attributable to the employee's father.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying the employers' motion to join the employee's father as an additional counter-defendant.

Phillips v. Graham


Nos. 53366, 53625, 53719


Supreme Court of Illinois


86 Ill. 2d 274; 427 N.E.2d 550; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 342; 56 Ill. Dec. 355



September 30, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Circuit Court of Madison County, the Hon. William E. Johnson and Edward Ferguson, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In separate actions, the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois) granted injunctions to appellee harness drivers (drivers), barring appellants, the Illinois Racing Board and race track owners (collectively board), from enforcing orders excluding the drivers from all racetracks under the board's jurisdiction. The board appealed.


OVERVIEW: The drivers were excluded from the racetracks after being indicted by grand juries for bribery. The drivers attacked on due process grounds the constitutionality of § 9(e) of the Illinois Horse Racing Act of 1975 (Act), codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 8, para. 37 -- 9(e) (1979), which authorized the board to issue the exclusion orders. The court held that because the drivers attacked the constitutionality of the Act, they were not required to exhaust any administrative remedies. In analyzing whether due process required an evidentiary hearing prior to the deprivation of the property rights, the court found: 1) the economic harm claimed was not irreparable, because while the drivers were precluding from racing in Illinois, they could train and race their horses using other drivers and could participate in races outside of the state; 2) the grand jury indictments were just cause for the exclusions; and 3) there was a valid governmental interest in protecting the integrity of horse racing. Because only property rights were involved, mere postponement of judicial inquiry did not violate due process. Section 9(e) was held constitutional, and the injunctions should not have been issued.


OUTCOME: The decision of the lower court in issuing the injunctions against the board was reversed.

 

354 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Schlessinger v. Olsen


No. 54227


Supreme Court of Illinois


86 Ill. 2d 314; 427 N.E.2d 122; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 344; 56 Ill. Dec. 42



September 30, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Raymond K. Berg, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant officials sought review of a decision of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which vacated a judgment that had dismissed plaintiff taxpayers' suit challenging the constitutionality of a real estate transfer tax.


OVERVIEW: The officials argued that the appellate court below erred when it raised, sua sponte, the fact that the cause had not yet been certified as a class action and ordered that the circuit court make that determination prior to making any final judgment on the merits. The reviewing court agreed and overturned the ruling. Where a motion to dismiss is made by a defendant, thereby placing in issue the sufficiency of a complaint, a trial court need not delay deciding the motion until the class certification question has been resolved. There is no requirement that the class certification be entertained first; a motion to dismiss for failure to state a cause of action is not dependent on a decision on the class certification issue, since no class action can proceed unless a cause of action is stated.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

 

355 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Oak Lawn v. Marcowitz


No. 53765


Supreme Court of Illinois


86 Ill. 2d 406; 427 N.E.2d 36; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 355; 55 Ill. Dec. 916



June 26, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Modified on Denial of Rehearing October 19, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Thomas Walsh, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff village filed a complaint charging defendant doctor with operating an ambulatory surgical treatment center without a license in violation of a village ordinance. The doctor filed a motion to dismiss, alleging the ordinance was unconstitutional, and the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) so held. The village appealed.


OVERVIEW: The doctor urged that the ordinance was an unconstitutional restriction upon the decision by a woman and her doctor to obtain a first-trimester abortion; that it violated equal protection requirements; and that the ordinance was so vague and indefinite that he was unable to determine what type of conduct was proscribed. The court held that the portion of the definition of an ambulatory surgical treatment center which related to abortions was unable to stand because it severely restricted the fundamental privacy right to secure a first-trimester abortion, and it did so in a manner not uniformly applicable to medically analogous surgical procedures. The court found nothing unreasonable in the provisions concerning minimum standards for health care of all patients, including the additional requirements for obstetrical and gynecological procedures, considering the state's interest in protecting the health and safety of all center patients. Nor was the court persuaded by the doctor's argument that the ordinance was void for vagueness because the requirements it established were sufficiently definite to allow a person of ordinary sensibilities to understand what was required.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the doctor granting his motion to dismiss on the grounds that the ordinance was unconstitutional and remanded the cause for a trial on the merits.

McCormick v. Caterpillar Tractor Co.


No. 53353


Supreme Court of Illinois


85 Ill. 2d 352; 423 N.E.2d 876; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 304; 53 Ill. Dec. 207; 23 A.L.R.4th 1134



June 26, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of McLean County, the Hon. Wayne C. Townley, Jr., Judge, presiding.
McCormick v. Caterpillar Tractor Co., 82 Ill. App. 3d 77, 402 N.E.2d 412, 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2500, 37 Ill. Dec. 522 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., 1980)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review of the judgment of the Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois), which determined that the exclusive-remedy provision of the Illinois Workmen's Compensation Act did not bar appellee employee's common law suit in tort against employer.


OVERVIEW: Employee injured his foot during the course of his employment with employer. He filed a claim under the Illinois Workmen's Compensation Act and received an award for a twenty-five percent permanent loss of use of his left foot. He then filed an action against employer and its physicians for negligence in the diagnosis and treatment of his injury. The trial court dismissed employee's complaint against employer and one physician and granted a summary judgment in favor of the other physicians. The appellate court reversed the judgment as to employer because it found that the exclusive-remedy provision of the Illinois Workmen's Compensation Act did not bar a common law suit in tort against employer. Employer appealed. The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court because the Illinois Workmen's Compensation Act provided the sole means of recovery for employee's compensable industrial injury and employer could not be sued under the dual-capacity doctrine.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court because the Illinois Workmen's Compensation Act provided the sole means of recovery for employee's compensable industrial injury and employer could not be sued under the dual-capacity doctrine.

Rock v. Thompson


No. 54408


Supreme Court of Illinois


85 Ill. 2d 410; 426 N.E.2d 891; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 308; 55 Ill. Dec. 566



June 26, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original petition for mandamus.

Announced February 9, 1981.



DISPOSITION: Writ awarded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner senators filed a petition for a writ of mandamus directing respondent governor to convene the state senate to elect from its membership a president of the senate as presiding officer. The senators also sought an injunction restraining respondent state senate president from conducting the duties of his office.


OVERVIEW: The state senators filed a petition for a writ of mandamus to direct the governor to convene the state senate for the purpose of electing a presiding officer. The court granted the writ and held that Ill. Const. art. IV, § 6 required the governor to convene the state senate to elect a president of the state senate. The court further held that the president of the state senate was required to be elected by a majority of the membership of the senate and not by a majority of a quorum. The state senate president was improperly elected because he was elected by a majority of a quorum that was declared to be present by the presiding officer and not by a majority of the membership of the senate. The court determined that a writ of mandamus was proper to direct the governor to perform his required duty under art. IV, § 6 and issued the writ.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of mandamus to the senators and ordered the governor to convene the state senate for the purpose of properly electing a presiding officer.

 

358 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Saltiel v. Olsen


No. 53137


Supreme Court of Illinois


85 Ill. 2d 484; 426 N.E.2d 1204; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 310; 55 Ill. Dec. 830



June 26, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Nathan M. Cohen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervenor attorney general and plaintiffs, prevailing taxpayers, appealed a ruling of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which awarded the taxpayers their attorney fees and costs in their suit against defendant county officials for improper use of real estate transfer taxes. The trial court found the fees proper in spite of any sovereign immunity under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 127, para. 801 (1979).


OVERVIEW: Taxpayers obtained a ruling that county officials should not retain half of all real estate transfer taxes collected. The trial court set aside the disputed funds, which were invested by a trustee, and out of the funds awarded the taxpayers $ 108,000 in attorney fees, which the taxpayers contended was too little and the attorney general contended was too much. The attorney general further argued that the fund belonged to the state and that fees could not be awarded out of it without going through the Court of Claims under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 127, para. 801 (1979). The court on appeal disagreed, finding no sovereign immunity violation. The court so held because the fund did not yet belong to the state and had been created only out of the efforts of the taxpayers. The court further noted that the class being represented was all taxpayers of the state of Illinois, who had prevailed and benefited through the efforts of the taxpayers' attorneys, and who thus could not be harmed by payment of the attorney fees out of the fund. However, the court did note that the fees awarded might be excessive, and it remanded for a determination of whether a fee of $ 250 per hour was too high.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the award of attorney fees to the taxpayers but remanded for consideration of the hourly rate awarded.

 

359 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Haron


No. 53472


Supreme Court of Illinois


85 Ill. 2d 261; 422 N.E.2d 627; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 296; 52 Ill. Dec. 625



June 4, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 6, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County, the Hon. Richard E. Richman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated cases, the State of Illinois appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois), which dismissed armed violence charges, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33A (1979), as to two defendants.


OVERVIEW: The first defendant was charged with armed violence, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33A (1979) and aggravated battery. The second defendant was charged with armed violence, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33A (1979), and illegal delivery of cannabis. The circuit court granted defendants' motions to dismiss the armed violence charges and declared Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33A-2 (1979) unconstitutional. The court affirmed the dismissal of the first defendant's armed violence charge but otherwise reversed the circuit court's judgment. The court held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33A-1 and 33A-2 (1979) did not require that a weapon facilitate the predicate offense and that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33A (1979) was not vague. However, because criminal statutes were to be construed leniently and a specific statute was given precedence over a general statute, the court concluded that the general assembly did not intend the presence of a weapon to enhance a misdemeanor. The court declined to find that the second defendant had been deprived of due process as to para. 33A's sentencing provisions because he had not been judged guilty or sentenced on the charge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the first defendant's armed violence charge and otherwise reversed the circuit court's judgment. The court remanded the cause for proceedings consistent with its opinion.

 

360 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Myers


No. 53635


Supreme Court of Illinois


85 Ill. 2d 281; 426 N.E.2d 535; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 297; 55 Ill. Dec. 389



June 4, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 19, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County, the Hon. Angelo F. Pistilli, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court affirmed in part and reversed in part; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed a decision from the Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois), which vacated defendant's conviction and sentence for attempted murder, but affirmed defendant's conviction of armed violence, armed robbery, and aggravated kidnapping.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with attempted murder, armed violence, armed robbery, and aggravated kidnapping after he threatened a man with a knife and held it to his throat in order to get the man to drive him home. Defendant later dumped the victim and his companion and took the victim's car. On appeal, the court reversed the appellate court, and affirmed the conviction in its entirety. The court found that the attempted murder was not a lesser included offense in the armed-violence charge, as the appellate court found, because the armed violence charge was based upon the underlying felony of aggravated battery. The court then found that defendant's behavior did support conviction for both attempted murder and for armed violence because there were two separate invasions of the victim's body, even though both were closely related by reason of the fact that they attacked the same area of his body and were close in time. Defendant's actions of moving the knife from the victim towards his companion amounted to an overt or outward manifestation sufficient to support a different offense, since the cutting necessarily involved a movement of some distance and would support a charge of battery.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court, and affirmed defendant's conviction for attempted murder, armed violence, armed robbery, and aggravated kidnapping in its entirety.

Kidd v. Industrial Com.


No. 53679


Supreme Court of Illinois


85 Ill. 2d 534; 426 N.E.2d 822; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 315; 55 Ill. Dec. 497



May 22, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 19, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Macon County, the Hon. Jerry L. Patton, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois) confirming the decision of appellee, the Illinois Industrial Commission (commission), that the claimant was not entitled to compensation for lost earnings under § 8(d)(1) of the Illinois Workmen's Compensation Act, (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 138.8(d)(1) (1975).


OVERVIEW: The claimant was employed by appellee tractor company as a finish painter and injured his foot when he stepped into a paint pot as he descended a ladder. After he returned to work, the claimant was assigned light duty and lost opportunity to work overtime. The commission affirmed the arbitrator's award for temporary total incapacity for work and for the permanent and complete loss of 50 percent of the use of his left foot but found that the claimant was not entitled to receive compensation for lost earnings under § 138.8(d)(1) because § 10(g) of the Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 138.10(g) (1975), barred the use of overtime earnings in computing lost earnings. The circuit court confirmed the commission's decision, and on appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the claimant's overtime earnings were not to have been included in computing his lost earnings under the express terms of § 138.10(g) and that § 138.8(d)(1) did not supersede or repeal § 138.10(g). Section 138.10(g) clearly related to earnings and unambiguously excluded overtime earnings from consideration. The court also found that § 138.10(g) was reasonable and, thus, was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying the claimant compensation for lost earnings.

United Air Lines, Inc. v. Johnson


No. 53105


Supreme Court of Illinois


84 Ill. 2d 446; 419 N.E.2d 899; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 266; 50 Ill. Dec. 631



March 31, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Earl Arkiss, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Director of Revenue of the State of Illinois and Department of Revenue, sought review of a order entered in the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which reversed an order denying a tax refund to appellee taxpayer.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer paid an Indiana seller's Indiana gross income tax liability resulting from the sale of fuel by contractual agreement. The taxpayer claimed to be entitled to an exemption from its Illinois use tax liability equal to the amount of the Indiana taxes paid, and sought a refund from the protest fund into which it had previously paid the Illinois use tax. On appeal from the appellate court's reversal of the denial of the taxpayer's request for a refund, the court ruled that the Indiana gross income tax was not a tax in respect to the sale, purchase, or use of property within the meaning of § 3(c) of the Use Tax Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 439.3(3)(c) (1977), that the mere fact that the taxpayer contracted to pay the seller's gross income tax liability did not entitle the taxpayer to an exemption from the Illinois use tax, and that the taxpayer did not meet its burden of proving that it clearly came within the statutory exemption. The court also ruled that the failure to grant the taxpayer an exemption did not discriminate against interstate commence because there were two distinct taxable events upon which the local state could properly impose a tax.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's order and affirmed the denial of a tax refund to the taxpayer.

In re B.


No. 53796


Supreme Court of Illinois


84 Ill. 2d 323; 418 N.E.2d 751; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 253; 49 Ill. Dec. 731



March 18, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Joseph Schneider, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant adoptee sought review of a decision of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which upheld a decision of the trial court that dismissed the adoptee's petition for a judgment declaring Ill Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1522 (1977) unconstitutional. The statute placed adoption records and original birth records under seal.


OVERVIEW: An adult adoptee sought information about his birth family, but the adoptee did not claim a medical or psychological need for this information. The trial court dismissed the adoptee's action to declare Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1522 (1977) unconstitutional. This was the statute that authorized sealing birth and adoption records. On appeal, the adoptee claimed that his right to know his own identity was a fundamental right. The court disagreed and found that this right did not come within any recognized category of privacy protected by the Bill of Rights. The court further found that the statute was rational in light of the state's interest in protecting confidentiality integral to the adoption process, and that it did not unconstitutionally infringe upon an adoptee's right to discover his own identity. The court also rejected the adoptee's argument that the statute violated an adoptee's equal protection rights by creating a suspect class for which there was no state justification. The court noted that adoption was a legal process, the purpose of which was to promote the best interests of the child. The court held that the adoption statute was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower courts.

 

364 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Caterpillar Tractor Co. v. Lenckos


Nos. 52818, 52828, 52903 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


84 Ill. 2d 102; 417 N.E.2d 1343; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 236; 49 Ill. Dec. 329



February 20, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 27, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County, the Hon. Stephen J. Covey, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, corporation and subsidiaries, sought review of defendant Director of Revenue's decision that denied their application of the unitary method of apportionment and certain deductions. Sixteen corporations intervened. The Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois) affirmed in part and reversed in part. The Appellate Court, Third District (Illinois) affirmed the method's applicability and reversed the deductions. The parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed separate state corporate income tax returns and then claimed refunds because they misapplied the unitary method of appointment. Plaintiffs argued that they were entitled to claim a deduction on their state returns for taxes paid to foreign governments regardless of whether they claimed a tax credit or a deduction on their federal income tax returns. Intervenors argued that the unitary reporting method was not applicable and violated due process. The director objected to the intervention of the 16 corporations. The court concluded that the circuit court did not abuse its discretion when it granted the petition for intervention and that the appellate court was correct in applying the unitary method and denying the deductions. The court analyzed the legislative history of the Illinois Income Tax Act and related income tax acts to determine that the use of the combined or unitary apportionment method was authorized and could be required in the case of unitary business groups. Plaintiffs' election to take a tax credit for foreign taxes paid on their federal income tax returns was binding on their state returns. Thus, they were not entitled to the deductions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court.

Schlenz v. Castle


Nos. 53189, 53286


Supreme Court of Illinois


84 Ill. 2d 196; 417 N.E.2d 1336; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 245; 49 Ill. Dec. 322



February 20, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 27, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 53189. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County, the Hon. Charles F. Scott, Judge, presiding.

No. 53286. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Shelby County, the Hon. Charles E. Jones, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part and remanded. Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, taxpayers, appealed the decision of the Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois), which reversed in part and affirmed in part the order of the circuit court that denied class certification of taxpayers' action. Defendant, property tax appeal board, challenged the decision of the Appellate Court for the Fifth District (Illinois), which reversed the circuit court's decision finding certain tax assessments invalid.


OVERVIEW: In the appeal from the Second District, taxpayers, purporting to act as representatives of a class, sought to have property tax officials comply with § 318.1 of the Revenue Act of 1939, codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. 1979, ch. 120, par. 799.1. Both appellate courts found § 318.1 unconstitutional. Section 318.1 was a validating act making legal and effective all assessments, irrespective of the failure to comply with timely publication. First, the court found that the relationship between the purported class representatives and the non-plaintiff class attorneys was in question. Thus, the circuit court did not abuse its discretion in refusing to certify the purported class. The court held next that § 318.1 did not violate the principle of separation of powers or the due process rights of taxpayers. The court held that the legislature could cure a defect in a tax levy where the defect was the failure to observe a requirement of the law without which the legislature would not have authorized the levy. Further the court held that Public Act 80-1471, of which § 318.1 was a part, did not violate the constitution's prohibition against more than one subject in an act.


OUTCOME: As to the Second District appeal, the court reversed the appellate court insofar as it held the real estate tax assessments invalid and affirmed insofar as it remanded to the circuit court to determine the existence of an appropriate subclass. As to the Fifth District appeal, the judgment of the appellate court was reversed and that of the circuit court was affirmed.

People v. Seymour


No. 53139


Supreme Court of Illinois


84 Ill. 2d 24; 416 N.E.2d 1070; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 228; 48 Ill. Dec. 548



February 3, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Franklin I. Kral, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from the judgment of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which affirmed the decision of the circuit court. Prior to his trial for possession of a controlled substance, defendant filed a motion to suppress the cocaine, which was taken from him following a strip search. The circuit court allowed the motion and suppressed the evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested on a weapons charge. After he was fingerprinted at the station, he entered the lockup area to wash his hands. The arresting officer strip-searched him and discovered cocaine in one of his socks. The appellate court held that the police were required to advise all arrestees charged with a misdemeanor of their right to post bail immediately, that defendant had the right to and could post bail, that the police had no right to detain him and had no need or right to conduct a search; thus, the search was unauthorized, the seizure of the drugs was illegal, and the evidence was suppressed. On appeal from that decision, the court noted that there was no requirement that defendant be orally advised by the police of his right to post bail and that defendant mentioned a prior felony conviction, which would require that the officers ascertain whether his weapons charge would be a Class 3 felony. He could not be permitted to immediately post bail for a misdemeanor and be released. The court reversed the decision of the appellate court; defendant's strip-search was incident to a lawful arrest and was proper prior to his detention to safeguard the detention facility.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the circuit court suppressing the evidence seized following the strip search of defendant, and the court reversed the judgment of the appellate court affirming the order of the circuit court.

De Bruyn v. Elrod


Nos. 52771, 53288 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


84 Ill. 2d 128; 418 N.E.2d 413; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 237; 49 Ill. Dec. 559



February 3, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Modified on Denial of Rehearing March 27, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Nathan M. Cohen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, county, sheriff, and treasurer, sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which entered judgment in favor of plaintiff judgment creditor and members of the class that paid fees pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 53, para. 71 (1977), ordered an accounting, granted a preliminary injunction that declared the fee provision of the statute unconstitutional, and dismissed plaintiff banks from the action.


OVERVIEW: The sheriff and the county challenged the trial court's judgment and the banks challenged the portion of the judgment that dismissed them from the action. The court modified the judgment and affirmed the judgment as modified. The court held that Ill. Const. art. VII, § 9(a) applied to both tax and non-tax funds, and that the funds received by the sheriff in connection with foreclosure sales, execution of judgments, and redemptions were collected funds within the contemplation of § 9(a). Therefore, the court determined that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 53, para. 71 (1977) contravened Ill. Const. art. VII, § 9(a). The court also held that the payments made to the sheriff were not voluntary, the record provided no basis on which to have invoked laches to bar the judgment creditor's action, and pecuniary harm came to certain identifiable entities that were required to have paid the fees exacted by the sheriff and there was no equitable reason to have held that reimbursement should not have been made. Finally, the court held that the funds received as commissions on sales in connection with executions and redemptions must have been accounted for by the sheriff and the county.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the judgment creditor but held that the sheriff and the county must have accounted for only those funds received as commissions on sales in connection with executions and redemptions not approved by orders of the court. The judgment was further modified to provide the judgment creditor and the class an accounting. The case was remanded for further proceedings.

Scott v. Department of Commerce & Community Affairs


No. 53998


Supreme Court of Illinois


84 Ill. 2d 42; 416 N.E.2d 1082; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 229; 48 Ill. Dec. 560



February 3, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County, the Hon. Dennis J. Jacobsen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff commissioners filed a petition seeking a temporary restraining order, a temporary injunction, a permanent injunction, and declaratory relief to prevent defendant, Department of Commerce and Community Affairs, from conducting a hearing to remove plaintiffs. The St. Clair County Circuit Court (Illinois) granted a preliminary injunction enjoining defendant from proceeding with the hearing.


OVERVIEW: Three commissioners filed an action against the Department of Commerce and Community Affairs (Department) seeking a temporary restraining order, a temporary injunction, a permanent injunction, and declaratory relief to prevent the Department from conducting a hearing to remove the commissioners. The Department wished to conduct the hearing pursuant to § 4 of the Housing Authorities Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 67 1/2, para. 4 (1979). The trial court granted a preliminary injunction on the ground that the statute had been found unconstitutional. On interlocutory appeal, the court held that a statute was presumed to be valid and the burden was on the party challenging it to establish its constitutional invalidity. The court held that the specification in the Act of the causes for removal of the commissioners of a housing authority was not impermissibly vague and certain. The court held that the hearing provided by § 4 comported with the requirements of due process because despite the commissioners' contention prehearing discovery was not constitutionally required and that there was no evidence that the hearing would not have been impartial. The court reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order from the trial court. The court held that there was no evidence that the Housing Authorities Act violated plaintiff commissioners' due process rights.

Chastek v. Anderson


No. 52943


Supreme Court of Illinois


83 Ill. 2d 502; 416 N.E.2d 247; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 219; 48 Ill. Dec. 216



January 20, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Reginald J. Holzer, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff dentist sought a permanent injunction to restrain defendant, the Department of Registration and Education (Department), from conducting a hearing against him on a pending complaint. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted the dentists motion for summary judgment. The Department appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the issues were (1) whether Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111, para. 2222(11) (1977) was vague, and thereby deprived the dentist of his constitutional right to due process, and (2) whether unprofessional conduct included conduct of the type alleged against the dentist. The Department alleged that the dentist engaged in unprofessional conduct by providing his patients with improper treatment, and they sought to revoke his dentist and orthodontist licenses on those grounds. The dentist sought and received a temporary restraining order against the Department. The trial court found the statute void and entered a permanent injunction that prevented the Department from conducting a hearing to suspend or revoke the dentist's licenses. The court reversed that decision and held that when the statute was considered in light of the goal of providing competent dental treatment for the benefit of the health, safety and welfare of the public, the legislative purpose would be frustrated if the statute did not encompass repeated acts of negligence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment.

People ex rel. Carey v. Bentivenga


No. 53850


Supreme Court of Illinois


83 Ill. 2d 537; 416 N.E.2d 259; 1981 Ill. LEXIS 223; 48 Ill. Dec. 228



January 20, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original petition for mandamus.



DISPOSITION: Writ awarded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The prosecutor filed an original petition for mandamus to compel respondent judge to expunge a judgment that he entered in defendant's bench trial on a charge of burglary. The judge convicted defendant and sentenced him to probation despite the fact that defendant had been convicted of burglary less than 10 years previously.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of burglary in a bench trial for having entered an auto parts store and taking a can of oil having a retail value of $ 1.55. At the sentencing hearing the prosecutor informed the trial court that defendant had been convicted of burglary less than 10 years previously. The trial court sentenced defendant to probation. The prosecutor brought an original proceeding for mandamus to compel the trial judge to expunge the sentence and resentence defendant. The court granted the writ and held that: (1) under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 1005-5-3(c)(2)(F), 1005-8-1(a)(5) (1979), defendant, a prior offender, was not eligible for parole; (2) the trial court was aware of the applicable statutes and there was no basis for a proceeding to correct trial errors under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 72 (1979); (3) defendant, a repeat offender, was to be treated more harshly because of his failure to correct his conduct, and not the value of the property that he took; and (4) in this mandamus action the court could not consider defendant's request for a reduced sentence under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 615, 73 Ill. 2d R. 615, because the court was limited to issues of law.


OUTCOME: The court awarded a writ of mandamus to compel the trial judge to vacate the order that granted defendant probation and to enter sentence in accordance with law.

 

371 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Difanis v. Barr


No. 52948


Supreme Court of Illinois


83 Ill. 2d 191; 414 N.E.2d 731; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 447; 46 Ill. Dec. 678



December 19, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County, the Hon. Robert J. Steigmann, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, nine city council members, challenged the judgement of the Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois), which affirmed the circuit court's judgement that the city council members violated the Open Meetings Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 102, par. 41 et seq. (1977). Appellee state's attorney filed a declaratory judgement action against them because they met and conferred privately in advance of a special meeting of the city council.


OVERVIEW: The city council consisted of 15 members. One evening, an hour and a half prior to a special meeting of the council, nine members met at the home of one of the members. Eight of the nine members were members of the county democratic party. At the meeting they discussed four of the five city council matters that were on the agenda as well as party matters. At the council meeting, three votes were taken on matters previously discussed at the private meeting. The state's attorney for the county filed a declaratory judgement action against the nine members, and sought a declaration that they had violated the Open Meetings Act (Act). The circuit court entered judgement in favor of the state's attorney, which was affirmed by the appellate court. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgement. It held that the private meeting was not merely a political caucus because public matters were deliberated at the meeting, which put it in the ambit of the Act. It held there was no denial of the nine members' rights to equal protection or due process under the U.S. Constitution or state constitution. It held that the Act did not violate their rights of freedom of speech and assembly.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgement. It held that the nine city council members constituted more than a quorum and any meeting they had where they discussed any pending city council matters was required to comply with the open meetings statute. The statute did not violate their constitutional rights.

Coalition for Political Honesty v. State Board of Elections


No. 53774


Supreme Court of Illinois


83 Ill. 2d 236; 415 N.E.2d 368; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 451; 47 Ill. Dec. 363


September 2, 1980, Argued and Announced  
December 1, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 29, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original petition for mandamus.



DISPOSITION: Writ awarded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a political coalition, were granted leave to file an original action seeking a writ of mandamus directing respondents, State Board of Elections, its members, and others, to certify a proposed constitutional amendment for an upcoming general election.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, a political coalition, proposed a constitutional amendment to the Illinois Constitution. They maintained that the reliance by respondents, State Board of Elections, on Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 46, para. 28-1.1 (1979), which required invalidation of whole sheets of signatures from consideration because of the presence of one or more nonconforming signatures, violated Ill. Const. art. XIV, § 3. The court held that the penalty provided -- the disqualification of entire sheets -- was simply too harsh. It was not the least drastic means of insuring the integrity of the initiative process. The court found that respondents failed to demonstrate that the state's interest in integrity could not be served by the less drastic penalty of disqualification of signatures of those from jurisdictions other than that of the circulatory penalty provision, which disqualified an entire sheet of 24 proper and valid signatures solely because the twenty-fifth was improper. The court held that such a penalty was a constitutionally impermissible limitation upon Ill. Const. art. XIV's right of initiative.


OUTCOME: The court ordered that a writ of mandamus issue directing respondents to certify petitioners proposition for submission to the upcoming election.

People ex rel. Carey v. Chrastka


Nos. 53754, 53778, 53803 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


83 Ill. 2d 67; 413 N.E.2d 1269; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 482; 46 Ill. Dec. 156



December 1, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original petition for mandamus.



DISPOSITION: Writs awarded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted petitioner state's petitions for leave to file original petitions for writs of mandamus in three consolidated cases. Respondent judges had held unconstitutional § 5-12 of the Juvenile Court Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 705-12 (1979) and denied the state's petitions to proceed thereunder.


OVERVIEW: The court held that given the absence of a constitutional requirement that a trial by jury be afforded in all juvenile proceedings, the Legislature had afforded sufficient recognition to the right by allowing a trial by jury when the individual was prosecuted as an habitual juvenile offender. The court held that the Juvenile Court Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para 701-1 et seq., was not constitutionally flawed simply because it did not require that trial by jury have been afforded at the two predicate adjudications. The court also rejected the judges' contention that the Act violated due process because it allowed the question of a prior adjudication to be tried by the court rather than a jury. The court held that there was no merit to the judges' argument that the individual may have been prejudiced by the impeachment usage of prior adjudications.


OUTCOME: The court issued a writ of mandamus, which directed the judges to vacate their orders, which declared a section of the Juvenile Court Act unconstitutional and denied the state's petitions to proceed under that section. The court ordered the judges to allow said petitions and proceed accordingly.

Winokur v. Rosewell


No. 52862


Supreme Court of Illinois


83 Ill. 2d 92; 414 N.E.2d 724; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 485; 46 Ill. Dec. 671



December 1, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Reginald J. Holzer, Richard L. Curry and Thomas Rosenberg, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded in Winokur v. Rosewell; reversed and remanded in Huppert v. Dunne and Hansen v. Dunne.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which ruled that raises for defendants, members of the Cook County Board (board) were valid. Another judge of the same court dismissed petitions for mandamus brought by board members, ruling that the board's action violated § 38 the Counties Act and the board president's partial line item vetoes of the raises was lawful.


OVERVIEW: After their reelection, incumbent members of the board passed salary increases for themselves. The president of the board exercised a partial line item veto, which reduced, but did not eliminate the raises. A taxpayer challenged the board's action, and the board members brought writs of mandamus to compel the president to pay the raises the board had authorized. The circuit court dismissed the taxpayer's challenge, but another circuit court judge dismissed the petitions for the writs. The three actions were consolidated for appeal. The court affirmed the dismissal of the taxpayer's challenge and reversed the dismissal of the petitions for writs of mandamus. The court concluded that the board members did not mislead the public during their campaigns for office, and the board's action was an effort to set an appropriate level of compensation. The court held that Ill. Const. art. VII, § 9(b) (1970) did not prohibit the actions taken by the board. The court also found that the president's line item vetoes were void, but this was not an appropriate case in which to decide if a president had the power to make line item vetoes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and remanded the judgment that dismissed the taxpayer's challenge to the raises the board members voted for themselves after their reelection but before the start of the new term. The court reversed and remanded the judgment that dismissed the petitions for writ of mandamus filed by the board members to compel the payment of the raises.

Illinois Polygraph Soc. v. Pellicano


No. 52905


Supreme Court of Illinois


83 Ill. 2d 130; 414 N.E.2d 458; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 487; 46 Ill. Dec. 574



December 1, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Nathan Cohen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, corporation and examiners (collectively society), filed an action against defendant examiner, seeking to enjoin the examiner from holding himself out as a detection-of-deception examiner. The trial court denied the examiner's motion to dismiss and certified an appeal. The appellate court (Illinois) reversed. The court granted the society leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: The examiner was not licensed to perform detection-of deception tests under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 202-1et seq. (1975) (Act). The examiner used a psychological stress evaluator that measured the human voice. The appellate court ruled that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111, para. 2403 (1979), was special legislation in violation of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13 (1970). Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111, para. 2403 (1979) required every examiner to use a device that measured cardiovascular and respiratory changes (i.e., a polygraph machine). The court reversed and remanded. The court held that the Act did require at least use a cardiovascular and respiratory machine and use of its results. As to special legislation, doubt as to the reliability of detection-of-deception devices allowed the state to set minimum standards and prefer one method to the exclusion of others. The Act did not give licensed examiners control over entry into the trade. The Act allowed any person to obtain an internship license by paying a fee. There was no evidence that instruction by licensed examiners was unavailable. The Act allowed judicial review of the Department of Registration and Education.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the appellate court, which reversed the trial court's order denying the examiner's motion to dismiss the society's action to enjoin the examiner from performing detection-of-deception tests. The court remanded for further proceedings.

Methodist Medical Center v. Ingram


No. 52982


Supreme Court of Illinois


82 Ill. 2d 511; 413 N.E.2d 402; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 437; 45 Ill. Dec. 924



November 18, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Tazewell County, the Hon. Charles J. Perrin, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff hospital appealed the decision of the Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois), which held that defendant township supervisor of general assistance was entitled to pay the hospital for services rendered at a per diem rate established by the Department of Public Aid. The appellate court reversed the judgment of a circuit court rendered for the hospital.


OVERVIEW: A resident of the township received medical treatment, and the supervisor determined that the resident was indigent and eligible for medical assistance under article VII of the Illinois Public Aid Code, Ill. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the appellate court which held that the supervisor was entitled to pay the hospital for services rendered at the per diem rate established by the Department of Public Aid.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant administrator sought review of a judgment of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which affirmed the order of the trial court dismissing the administrator's second amended complaint on grounds that it was time-barred by the two-year statute of limitations applicable to wrongful death actions.


OVERVIEW: The administrator filed a wrongful death action against respondent physician. The additional respondents filed motions to dismiss, which were granted. The estate representative filed a second amended complaint that the trial court dismissed on grounds that it was barred by the two-year statute of limitations applicable to wrongful death actions. Even if § 21.1 were applicable, the administrator failed to name the physicians and hospital as parties defendant until July 7, 1977, after the six-month extension granted by § 21.1 to the original two-year limitations period had expired.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court, which upheld the trial court's order granting the motions by the physicians and hospital to dismiss the administrator's complaint as time-barred.

People v. Youngbey


No. 53141


Supreme Court of Illinois


82 Ill. 2d 556; 413 N.E.2d 416; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 443; 45 Ill. Dec. 938



November 18, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Robert Sklodowski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; sentences vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, convicted for unlawful use of weapons, appealed from a determination of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which held that the statutory requirement that a presentence investigation be conducted and a report be submitted in all felony cases pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-3-1 (1979) (amendment effective February 1, 1978) constituted an unconstitutional encroachment on the judiciary's sentencing power.


OVERVIEW: Both defendants, as well as the state, waived the presentence investigation and they conducted a sentencing hearing immediately after the defendants were found guilty. The parties had not agreed on any specific sentences in connection with defendants' guilty pleas. The trial judge then, sua sponte, held Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-3-1 (1979) unconstitutional, contending that a presentence report which could not be waived was an invasion of the sentencing powers of the judiciary and also an invasion of executive authority. Defendants argued that they did not have the option of waiving the reports and that the judge could not accept their waivers. The state argued that the statute did not prevent a waiver of the reports by defendants. The court reversed the sentences and remanded, holding that the section did not constitute an unconstitutional encroachment. The court also found that the presumption that the legislature intended to change the law by deleting the provision permitting defendants to waive the presentence investigation report was not rebutted and the presentence report requirement by its language was not only mandatory, but also could not be waived by defendants.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court holding that the section governing presentence reports of the Unified Code of Corrections was unconstitutional. The court vacated the sentences imposed by the trial court and remanded the cause for a presentence investigation and report and a new sentencing proceeding.

People v. Gleckler


No. 51537


Supreme Court of Illinois


82 Ill. 2d 145; 411 N.E.2d 849; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 405; 44 Ill. Dec. 483



October 17, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County, the Hon. Harold L. Jensen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; death sentence vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) which convicted him of murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced to death for shooting two victims to death in order to steal their car to use during an armed robbery of a gas station. At trial, defendant asserted that he was ordered to kill the victims by another individual who had come up with the idea of the robbery and convinced defendant and another to participate. OUTCOME: Defendant's murder conviction was affirmed. His death sentence was vacated and the case was remanded for imposition of a sentence other than death.

 

381 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Cox


No. 52793


Supreme Court of Illinois


82 Ill. 2d 268; 412 N.E.2d 541; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 415; 45 Ill. Dec. 190



October 17, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Macon County, the Hon. Rodney A. Scott, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed; sentence vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from orders of the Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois) reducing defendants' sentences. The State contended that the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-4.1 (1979), unconstitutionally conflicted with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 615(b)(4), by modifying the standard of review of sentences and authorizing appellate courts to impose any sentence the trial court could have imposed.


OVERVIEW: The court struck down para. 1005-5-4.1 as unconstitutional. The statute was in direct conflict with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 615(b)(4), 73 Ill. 2d R. 615(b)(4), and sought to modify the standard of review for sentences and authorized appellate courts to impose any sentence that a trial court could have imposed. Under Ill. Const. art. VI, § 1 the judicial power was vested in the state courts. Judicial power was not defined in the constitution, but all such power was exclusively and exhaustively granted to the courts. If the power was judicial in character, it necessarily followed that the legislature was expressly prohibited from exercising it. It was equally clear that the state supreme court possessed the rulemaking authority to regulate the trial of cases and the authority to regulate appeals. Although it was true that the legislature had the power to enact laws governing judicial practice where it did not unduly infringe upon the inherent powers of the judiciary, where a rule of the state supreme court on a matter within the court's authority and a statute on the same subject conflicted, the rule prevailed.


OUTCOME: The orders affirming the trial court's reduction of defendants' sentences were reversed because the statute altering the standard of review for sentences and authorizing appellate courts to impose any sentence that a trial court could have imposed unconstitutionally infringed on the power of the state supreme court to regulate matters of appellate practice and procedure.

Wilson v. Bishop


No. 52136


Supreme Court of Illinois


82 Ill. 2d 364; 412 N.E.2d 522; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 425; 45 Ill. Dec. 171; 68 Oil & Gas Rep. 193



October 17, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of White County, the Hon. Henry Lewis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of White County (Illinois) in favor of defendant oil and gas owners, which denied his claim that he owned an undivided one-third interest in the oil and gas and held that the Dormant Mineral Interests Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 30, para. 197, 198 (1975), violated the due process and contract clauses of the constitutions of the state and the United States.


OVERVIEW: The property owner owned the surface area of a 72-acre tract of land. The deceased owned an undivided one-third interest in minerals beneath the surface area. When she died, such rights were transferred to the oil and gas owners under her will. The oil and gas owners failed to file written notices in the recorder's office or to preserve their ownership in any other way. Subsequently, it was discovered that commercial quantities of oil underlayed a portion of the tract of land. The property owner refused to pay the oil and gas owners any of the oil proceeds. He argued that his refusal to pay them was supported by the Dormant Mineral Interests Act (the Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 30, para. 197, 198 (1975), because their failure to preserve their ownership constituted statutory abandonment of their rights. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that oil and gas owners' severed mineral interests constituted protected property interests that were entitled to procedural due process safeguards. The court further held that the Act provided no notice nor an opportunity for the oil and gas owners to be heard, and therefore unconstitutionally violated their right to due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, which denied the property owner's claim that he owned an undivided one-third interest in the oil and gas, because the Dormant Mineral Interests Act unconstitutionally violated due process rights because it did not provide notice or an opportunity to be heard. The oil and gas owner's rights were protected property interests that were entitled to such due process.

Illinois Housing Development Authority v. Van Meter


No. 53487


Supreme Court of Illinois


82 Ill. 2d 116; 412 N.E.2d 151; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 403; 45 Ill. Dec. 18



October 10, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County, the Hon. Simon L. Friedman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, Chairman of the Illinois Housing Authority (chairman), challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which declared valid an amendment to the Illinois Housing Development Act (Act) authorizing the issuance of municipal bonds by plaintiff, the Illinois Housing Development Authority (Authority). The circuit court issued a writ of mandamus ordering the chairman to execute a notice of sale of the bonds.


OVERVIEW: The Authority adopted resolutions that authorized the issuance of municipal bonds to fund the amendment to the Act in order to raise low-interest mortgage money and that directed the chairman to publish a notice of sale inviting bids. When the chairman refused to comply, the Authority filed an action. The chairman contended that the amendment to the Act was invalid because it's wealth classification system violated equal protection standards. The circuit court declared the amendment to the Act valid and ordered the chairman to comply with the Authority's resolutions. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that such legislation based on a wealth classification infringing on a person's right to housing did not constitute a suspect classification under the equal protection clauses of either the United States Constitution or the Illinois Constitution. Thus, although the amendment to the Act may have excluded certain non-first-time home purchasers who were in greater financial need than some first-time home buyers, the classification bore a rational relationship to the legitimate legislative purpose of providing financing for housing to low- and moderate-income families.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's declaration that the amendment to the Act, which authorized the Authority to issue municipal bonds, was valid. The court upheld the trial court's issuance of a writ of mandamus ordering the chairman to sell the bonds.

In re Callas


No. 52975


Supreme Court of Illinois


82 Ill. 2d 6; 411 N.E.2d 273; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 391; 44 Ill. Dec. 304



September 29, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Disciplinary proceeding.



DISPOSITION: Respondent suspended.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A disciplinary commission recommended the suspension of respondent attorney from the practice of law for a period of 18 months and until further order of the court based upon his guilty plea to a misdemeanor criminal information for embezzlement and conversion of funds.


OVERVIEW: The attorney pleaded guilty to a criminal information that charged him with embezzlement and conversion of funds that were entrusted to a bank with which the attorney was associated. A disciplinary commission recommended that the attorney be suspended from the practice of law for a period of 18 months and until further order of the court. The court suspended the attorney for nine months. The court concluded that the attorney's conduct, taken in its totality, constituted a serious professional transgression and brought the legal profession into disrepute. The court determined that the amount of money that was actually involved was enough that conduct underlying the attorney's conviction could be considered a felony even though he pleaded guilty to an information that charged a misdemeanor. The court found that the attorney's misconduct was a serious violation of important professional responsibilities that had been entrusted to him. The attorney was a lawyer of mature and sophisticated experience and pleaded guilty to what had to be considered the misapplication and conversion of the money in question for his personal benefit.


OUTCOME: The court suspended the attorney from the practice of law for a period of nine months.

People v. Garrison


No. 52750


Supreme Court of Illinois


82 Ill. 2d 444; 412 N.E.2d 483; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 429; 45 Ill. Dec. 132



September 29, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 26, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Marion County, the Hon. Harry L. Ziegler, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Marion County, (Illinois) that had declared 38 Ill. Comp. Stat. 11/9(a)(3) unconstitutional, as argued by defendant at trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been charged with knowingly, at a public place, while standing behind a storm door, exposing his sex organ in a lewd manner in violation of 38 Ill. Comp. Stat. 11/9(a)(3). The lower court had declared the statute unconstitutional. Defendant had filed a motion to dismiss the information on the ground that it violated various amendments to the United States Constitution.
