The court held that activities which were primarily expressive were not within the scope of the statute. Defendant contended the statutes were so vague that any prosecution under them constituted a denial of due process. The court determined this argument was meritless.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court and remanded the case, because defendant's constitutional rights had not been violated and he was properly convicted for violating the public indecency statute. The court determined the statute at issue was not unconstitutional.

 

386 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Avon Prods. v. Indus. Comm'n


No. 52904


Supreme Court of Illinois


82 Ill. 2d 297; 412 N.E.2d 468; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 418; 45 Ill. Dec. 117



September 15, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 26, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. James C. Murray, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants employee and industrial commission (commission) sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which confirmed the commission's workmen's compensation award to the employee of compensation, medical expenses, attorney fees and interest, but reversed the penalties assessed under §§ 19(k) and 19(l) of the Workmen's Compensation Act.


OVERVIEW: The employee filed a claim for workmen's compensation after suffering a work-related injury. She was awarded compensation but no medical benefits. The employee appealed to the commission. The commission affirmed the compensation award and included an award for chiropractic fees. In addition, the commission awarded penalties, costs, and attorney fees pursuant to the Act, finding that the employer unreasonably delayed payment of compensation. The employer sought certiorari from the circuit court, which confirmed the compensation, chiropractic, attorney fees and interest awards but reversed the penalties assessed. The employee appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded, ruling that there was sufficient evidence to support the compensation and chiropractor awards. However, the attorney fees, costs, and penalties awarded were not warranted because the Act did not require the employer to make payment prior to a final determination of liability where reasonable grounds for challenging the liability existed. The employer's challenge was reasonable, considering the conflicting medical reports and the employee's delay in reporting the injury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded judgment in favor of the employee with directions to the commission to reinstate the award of compensation in addition to an award of chiropractor's fees and interest.

 

387 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Cook


No. 52292


Supreme Court of Illinois


81 Ill. 2d 176; 407 N.E.2d 56; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 350; 40 Ill. Dec. 825



June 30, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Warren County, the Hon. Stephen G. Evans, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois), which granted the people's motion for reimbursement of legal services provided to defendant from his bail deposit, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Code ch. 38, para. 110-7(g) (1979). He contended that the statute violated his rights to equal protection and due process under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2, and impaired his right to counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant deposited an amount in order to secure his release from jail. Counsel was appointed for him after he was found to be indigent. During the appeal of an evidence issue, he sought to recover his bail deposit. The appellate court granted the people's motion to apply the deposit to his legal services and directed the trial court to withhold the value of those services from the deposit. On appeal, the court found that § 110-7(g) was invalid. The statute violated the equal protection and due process clauses of the state and federal constitutions because only defendants posting bail were obliged to reimburse the county for the cost of their appointed counsel. The court found this violated defendant's rights to equal protection because there was no rational relationship between the statute's purpose, the reimbursement for the expense of appointed counsel, and the imposition of that obligation on only one segment of the class of indigent defendants, those posting bail. The court found that the statute's presumption that posting of bail demonstrated an ability to pay for those services could not substitute for a due process hearing to determine if a defendant was indigent.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the appellate court that required defendant to reimburse the state for the cost of providing legal services to him from the return of his bail deposit.

 

388 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Abney


No. 50636


Supreme Court of Illinois


81 Ill. 2d 159; 407 N.E.2d 543; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 349; 41 Ill. Dec. 45



June 20, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of McLean County, the Hon. Keith E. Campbell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged an order of the Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois), which affirmed a grant of defendant's motion to suppress any testimony as to a bullet that a police officer saw in plain view after entering defendant's residence without a warrant.


OVERVIEW: The intermediate court affirmed the grant of defendant's suppression motion regarding any testimony on a bullet that a police officer saw in plain view after entering defendant's residence without a warrant. The court reversed that order on appeal and remanded the case. The court found that the relevant statutes expressed an intent to permit entries to arrest if reasonable grounds or probable cause were present, and that precedent established that factors in addition to probable cause were present in each case in which the police activity was found to be reasonable within the meaning of U.S. Const. amend. IV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 6. The court also held that a warrantless entry to arrest required exigent circumstances. In addition to exigent circumstances, the officers' entry fell within the spirit of the hot-pursuit exception, that there was no deliberate or unjustified delay during which time a warrant could have been obtained, and that the officers acted on a clear showing of probable cause that was based on the type of reasonably trustworthy information that justified warrantless law enforcement activities.


OUTCOME: The court reversed an order that affirmed a grant of a motion to suppress any testimony as to a bullet that a police officer saw in plain view after a warrantless entry into defendant's home, and remanded. The court held that, in addition to the required exigent circumstances, the spirit of the hot pursuit exception applied and that there was probable cause that was based on reasonably trustworthy information.

O'Connor v. A & P Enters.


No. 52721


Supreme Court of Illinois


81 Ill. 2d 260; 408 N.E.2d 204; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 358; 41 Ill. Dec. 782



June 20, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County, the Hon. Stephen J. Covey, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action to resolve a dispute between appellant county collector and appellee objectors over property tax assessments, the Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois) determined that Illinois Public Act 80-247 was constitutional. The collector filed an application for leave to appeal. The appellate court allowed the application. The objectors filed a motion for leave to transfer the case to the court. The court granted the motion.


OVERVIEW: The objectors, each of whom owned farmland in the county, paid property taxes under protest and, upon application for judgment by the collector, objected to the assessments. The objectors relied upon Public Act 80-247, which established a new procedure for valuing farmland, farm buildings, and farm dwellings. The collector claimed that Public Act 80-247 was unconstitutional. The circuit upheld the validity of Public Act 80-247. The court affirmed, in part, and reversed, in part, holding (1) Public Act 80-247 was not unconstitutionally vague because it provided intelligible standards for the valuation and assessment of farmland, farm buildings, and farm dwellings, (2) the equalizing factors of the board of review and of the Illinois Department of Local Government Affairs (Department) were inapplicable in fixing the assessed value of farmland or improvements thereon, other than farm dwellings, and (3) farm dwellings and their appurtenances, and the real property on which they were situated, were to be valued at 33-1/3 percent of their fair cash value and the equalizing factors of the board of review and the Department were applicable thereto.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, in part, and reversed, in part, the decision of the circuit court.

Walter Peckat Co. v. Regional Transp. Authority


No. 53079


Supreme Court of Illinois


81 Ill. 2d 221; 407 N.E.2d 28; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 354; 40 Ill. Dec. 797



May 30, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 14, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Donald J. O'Brien, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed the taxpayer's complaint against defendants, the Regional Transportation Authority (RTA), the Director of Revenue of the State of Illinois, the Treasurer of the State of Illinois, and the Attorney General of the State of Illinois. The taxpayer had brought a class action against defendants.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer sought to declare that a tax imposed by the RTA was unconstitutional. The trial court disagreed, and the taxpayer appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The court held that the Regional Transportation Authority Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 2/3, para. 704.03(e) (1979), which allowed the imposition of an occupation tax on persons engaged in the business of selling tangible personal property, was constitutional. The court ruled that although Ill. Const. art. IX, §§ 9, 10 required municipalities to tax property uniformly within their jurisdictions, no such limitation applied to nonproperty taxes. The only limitation on occupation, privilege, and franchise taxes was that under § 1 they had to be uniform as to the class upon which they operated. The court held that the RTA could create different classes within its jurisdiction for the purpose of imposing a nonproperty tax. The court ruled that pursuant to § 8, the legislature authorized the RTA to use the classification and to impose the tax involved in the case. The court found that the classification was not unreasonable, and the tax imposed within each class was uniform under § 2.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which dismissed the taxpayer's complaint against defendants.

Boytor v. Aurora


No. 52051


Supreme Court of Illinois


81 Ill. 2d 308; 410 N.E.2d 1; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 362; 43 Ill. Dec. 1



May 22, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 26, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County, the Hon. John S. Page, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizen appealed a decision from the Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois), which affirmed the decision of the trial court, which had granted the pretrial motion for dismissal of defendants, city and election commission. The citizen had brought an action against defendants, which alleged violations of the election laws and sought a declaratory judgment, injunctive relief, and personal damages.


OVERVIEW: The citizen brought an action against defendants after his name failed to appear on the ballot when a nonpartisan primary was held. The trial court granted defendants' motion for dismissal and the appeals court affirmed. On review, the court affirmed the decision of the appeals court. The court held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 46, para. 28-4 (1975) imposed a minimum period of 78 days between adoption of the resolution calling for a referendum and the holding of the referendum. The court ruled that Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6(f) authorized a home rule municipality to alter the specific forms of government and officers provided in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, paras. 1-1-1 through 11-151-5 (1975). The court found that new amendments to the Election Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 46, paras. 10-3.1, 2A-1.2(c)(1), 2A-1.2(d) (1979), recognized that a municipality could choose to hold nonpartisan elections. The court held that defendants did not have to hold the nonpartisan primary on a specific day and did not have to have absentee balloting for 30 days because there was no specific statutes for the mayor aldermanic form of government.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the appeals court, which had affirmed the decision of the trial court, which had granted defendants' motion for dismissal of the citizen's action, which had alleged violations of the election laws and sought a declaratory judgment, injunctive relief, and personal damages.

 

392 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bradley


Nos. 52262, 52263, 52411, 52814


Supreme Court of Illinois


79 Ill. 2d 410; 403 N.E.2d 1029; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 312; 38 Ill. Dec. 575



April 18, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Nos. 52262, 52263. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Livingston County, the Hon. William T. Caisley, Judge, presiding.

No. 52411. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Montgomery County, the Hon. Joseph L. Fribley, Judge, presiding.

No. 52814. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Albert Green, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed. Judgment reversed; cause remanded. Judgment affirmed. Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from orders of three circuit courts (Illinois), which dismissed the charges of possession of schedule II, III, and IV controlled substances against defendants after § 402(b) of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1402(b) (1977), was found to be unconstitutional and void as a violation of the equal protection clause.


OVERVIEW: Section 402(b) of the Act imposed a greater penalty for possession of schedule IV controlled substances than that imposed by § 401(e) for delivery. The state contended that the penalty established for violations of § 402(b) did not deprive defendants of equal protection because all who were found guilty were equally subject to the penalty. The court held that § 402(b) did not violate equal protection, but did violate the due process clause of the Illinois Constitution and was invalid. The court reversed the dismissals of the charges for schedule II and III substances and affirmed the dismissals for possession of schedule IV substances. Inasmuch as § 402(b), as it was applied to charges of possession of schedule IV substances, was not reasonably designed to remedy the evil which the legislature determined to be a greater threat to the public, which was delivery, it was violative of the due process clause. The penalties for delivery of schedule II and III controlled substances were either greater than or equal to the penalty imposed for possession of those substances. Consequently, those provisions were not contrary to the purposes of § 100 of the Act and did not offend due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the charges of possession of schedule IV substances against defendants. The court reversed the judgments of dismissal of charges of possession of schedule II and III controlled substances against defendants and remanded for further proceedings.

 

393 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Carlson


No. 50890


Supreme Court of Illinois


79 Ill. 2d 564; 404 N.E.2d 233; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 327; 38 Ill. Dec. 809



April 18, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 29, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County, the Hon. Lloyd A. VanDeusen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed; death sentence vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which convicted him of two counts of murder and one count of arson and imposed a death sentence for the murder of a police officer.


OVERVIEW: Defendant murdered his ex-wife and set fire to her home. He later shot and killed a police officer. He was convicted of all three crimes. The court affirmed the convictions. The court found that defendant waived his right to assert many of the alleged errors by failing to object at the trial court level. Defendant failed to demonstrate that actual incompetence of his appointed counsel resulted in prejudice to him. Defendant was not denied a fair trial because the jury was chosen from a venire that excluded persons who could not impose the death penalty. Failure of the trial court to give the jury instruction defining "recklessly" in conjunction with the involuntary manslaughter instruction was not in error because defendant failed to tender the instruction to the trial court and the trial court was not required to sua sponte give the instruction. The court vacated the death sentence imposed for the murder of the police officer. The three crimes were all part of one unfortunate and tragic event and the trial court failed to consider as mitigating factors the absence of any prior criminal activity and whether defendant was under extreme mental or emotional disturbances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions and sentences of defendant for murder of his ex-wife and for the arson. The court affirmed the conviction of defendant for the murder of the police officer. The court set aside the penalty of death for that conviction and remanded the case to the trial court with directions to impose a sentence on defendant other than death.

Supreme Court of Illinois

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook (Illinois) in favor of defendants, village, village officials, and trustees, and the orders granting defendants' motion for summary judgment and denying the taxpayers' motion for summary judgment pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 302(a), 73 Ill. 2d R. 302(A). Defendants filed a motion to dismiss the appeal.

The parties filed motions for summary judgment. The trial court dismissed the petition for writ of mandamus, granted defendants' motion, and denied the taxpayers' motion. People ex rel. Canton v. Crouch


No. 52151


Supreme Court of Illinois


79 Ill. 2d 356; 403 N.E.2d 242; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 308; 38 Ill. Dec. 154



March 28, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Fulton County, the Hon. Charles Wilhelm, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mayor challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Fulton County (Illinois), which entered summary judgment in favor of appellee city in a mandamus proceeding brought against mayor to compel him to execute two general obligation bonds authorized by a municipal ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Mayor refused to execute bonds based on some doubt as to the validity, interpretation, and constitutionality of the Real Property Tax Increment Allocation Redevelopment Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 11-74.4-1 through 11-74.4-11. Although the tax increment scheme was novel, the court found that it did not violate and constitutional provision. The mayor argued that the redevelopment of blighted private commercial areas within a municipality was not a public purpose. The court disagreed and found that the Act was enacted for promoting the public purpose of the state in reducing unemployment, relieving urban blight, and increasing the general tax base. The court determined that the portion of the Act permitting revenues collected by various taxing districts to be paid to the municipal treasurer to pay costs arising out of redevelopment was a valid public purpose and constitutional. The court also determined that the Act did not offend due process or equal protection and that it sufficiently defined the harm to be prevented and the general means available to a municipality to prevent the harm.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment in favor of city.

Rockford Drop Forge Co. v. Pollution Control Bd.


No. 52161


Supreme Court of Illinois


79 Ill. 2d 271; 402 N.E.2d 602; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 302; 37 Ill. Dec. 600



March 21, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on petition for review of an order of the Pollution Control Board.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant forging companies sought leave to appeal an order of the Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois), which upheld rules adopted by appellee Pollution Control Board of the State of Illinois (board) for noise emissions from stationary, or "property line," sources, after the forging companies filed a petition directly under the provisions of the Environmental Protection Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para. 1001 et seq. (1977).


OVERVIEW: The companies filed a petition directly in the appellate court, contending that the noise pollution provisions of the Environmental Protection Act (act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para. 1001 et seq. (1977), were unconstitutional because of vagueness and improper delegation. The companies also asserted that the regulations exceeded the power granted the board under the act, and that the regulations violated equal protection rights. The appellate court upheld the rules, refusing to consider the companies' constitutional objections on the basis that it lacked jurisdiction to do so. The companies appealed, the board cross-appealed, and the court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court. Section 24 of the act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para. 1024 (1977), was not improperly vague because what § 24 proscribed was conduct that violated any regulation or standard adopted by the board. The court could not say that the legislature contemplated that each regulation had to be tailored to some common law decision on tort liability; thus the board did not exceed its powers. It was not an equal protection violation for the board to address only one noise source category.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the appellate court, which upheld rules adopted by the board for noise emissions from stationary, or "property line," sources.

Totten v. State Board of Elections

Supreme Court of Illinois

January 28, 1980, Argued and Announced

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff ballot protesters challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which was in favor of defendants, state board and political party committee. Plaintiffs sought to enjoin the state board from refusing to certify the presidential preferences of candidates for delegate and alternate delegate to a nominating convention and to order it to permit such preferences to appear on primary election ballots.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed an action against defendants to enjoin the state board from refusing to certify the presidential preferences of candidates for delegate and alternate delegate to a nominating convention and to order it to permit such preferences to appear on ballots to be used in a primary election. The trial court entered a judgment in favor of defendants, and plaintiffs appealed. The court affirmed the judgment against plaintiffs. West Side Organization Health Services Corp. v. Thompson


No. 52288


Supreme Court of Illinois


79 Ill. 2d 503; 404 N.E.2d 208; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 324; 38 Ill. Dec. 784



March 21, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 29, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Joseph M. Wosik, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state officials sought review of a judgment entered by the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which had reversed the trial court's dismissal of plaintiff drug-rehabilitation providers' action to prohibit the state officials from interfering in the allotment or expenditure by the Dangerous Drug Commission (DDC) of the full amount that had been appropriated for the purchase of drug-abuse treatment services.


OVERVIEW: The general assembly passed a bill that allocated funds for the purchase of drug-abuse treatment services by the DDC during fiscal year 1977. The governor reduced that line item by $ 100,000. The general assembly subsequently overrode that veto. Thereafter, the governor directed that $ 100,000 of the funds appropriated for the DDC be withheld because of budgetary concerns. The drug-rehabilitation providers commenced an action, which sought to prohibit the state officials from interfering with the amount that had been allocated for the purchase of drug-abuse treatment services. The appellate court reversed the trial court's dismissal of that action. The state officials sought review of the appellate court's decision. The court reversed that decision and affirmed the trial court's judgment. Under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 127, para. 161 (1977), the power to incur obligations ceased on June 30 of the year when the act making that appropriation was enacted. However, the authority to pay continued until the end of the next fiscal quarter. Therefore, the litigation was rendered moot on September 30, 1977, because the disputed funds had lapsed on that date.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment and affirmed the trial court's judgment, which had dismissed the drug-rehabilitation providers' action against the state officials.

People v. Brownell


No. 51646


Supreme Court of Illinois


79 Ill. 2d 508; 404 N.E.2d 181; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 325; 38 Ill. Dec. 757



March 21, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 29, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Boone County, the Hon. David R. Babb, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; sentence vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Boone County, Illinois, which convicted him of murder, aggravated kidnapping, and rape, and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been arrested for attempted murder and rape, when detectives from a nearby county requested an interview with him in relation to a murder. After the interview, defendant requested counsel and consulted with him several times. He later asked to speak with the detectives, turning down offers to have his attorney present, and signed a rights waiver before giving a statement inculpating himself with the crime the detectives were investigating. At trial, defendant's motion to suppress the statement was denied, and he was convicted and sentenced to death. On appeal, defendant argued, inter alia, that the admission violated his right against self-incrimination and it was taken from him in disregard of his right to counsel. The court affirmed the conviction because the statement was made several hours after the initial interrogation, after defendant had conferred with his attorney several times, after he had been informed of his Miranda rights, and after he had expressly declined to remain silent or have counsel present. The court vacated the sentence of death and remanded for resentencing because an aggravating factor was erroneously included in the sentencing decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction because defendant had several opportunities to speak with his attorney, but he chose to make his inculpatory statement without counsel present and after waiving his rights. The court vacated the death sentence and remanded because the trial court erred in including an aggravating factor in its decision.

 

400 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Polich v. Chicago School Finance Authority


No. 52957


Supreme Court of Illinois


79 Ill. 2d 188; 402 N.E.2d 247; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 290; 37 Ill. Dec. 357



March 11, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original petition for declaratory judgment.



DISPOSITION: Judgment for defendants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner teachers filed an action relating to revenue in the court against respondents, Chicago School Finance Authority (the Authority) and board, seeking a declaratory judgment that the Authority and the other provisions of Ill. Pub. Act 81-1221(the Act) were invalid.


OVERVIEW: The Authority was created by the Act, which provided for the termination of the terms of all members of the school board and the appointment of a new board. The teachers, who were employed by the board, sought a declaratory judgment that the Authority and the other provisions of the Act were invalid. The court entered a judgment for the Authority and the board. The court determined that it was intended that the power to raise revenue through taxation was firmly vested in the General Assembly both through the inherent power of that body, and by the specific grant of the Constitution. The court held that the enactment of the legislation was not an impairment of contract proscribed by either the United States Constitution or the Constitution of Illinois. The court could not say that the Act constituted an unlawful delegation of legislative power. The court found that the enrolled bill rule was clearly applicable in the teachers' case, and the court held that the legislation was properly enacted. The court further held that the Act was constitutional and became effective upon approval on January 16, 1980.


OUTCOME: The court entered a judgment for the Authority and the board in the teachers' action relation to revenue, which sought a declaratory judgment that the Authority and the provisions of the Act were invalid.
